Husband's Responsibility for Shrouding His Wife
Ruling on husband's duty for wife's shroud with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a husband must shroud his wife even if he is poor, and explain the evidence.

Core Idea
A husband must shroud his wife even if poor – it is a wajib duty, not optional.

This lesson focuses on the obligation of a husband to prepare and shroud his deceased wife. While the general principle is that shrouding is from the deceased's own wealth, the Hanafi school holds that if the wife has no wealth, the husband must bear the cost, even if he is poor. We will examine the proof and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Begin by recognizing that the default rule (as mentioned in the text) is that the shrouding expenses of a wife are taken from her own wealth because after death the marriage ends.
This is the original principle before exceptions.
2
Identify the exception for the husband
The text states that if the wife has no wealth, the husband is responsible for her shrouding even if he is poor (fi al-asahh). This is a departure from the general rule.
The husband's obligation arises from his moral duty and his previous obligation of nafaqah.
3
Examine the dalil (evidence)
The evidence includes the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'Begin with the shroud, then the debt, then the will' (indicating the shroud is a priority on the estate) and the hadith commanding following funerals, which implies caring for the deceased.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i position that the wife's own wealth is always used first is that the husband must step in when she has nothing.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the husband is not obligated to shroud his wife; it is from her own wealth. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for fatwa.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۹۱) وعلى الرجل تجهيز امرأته ولو معسّرا في الاصح (۸۹۲) ومن لا مال له فكفنه على من تلزمه نفقته وان لم يوجد من تجب عليه نفقته ففى بيت المال فان لم ترجمه : (۸۹۱) شوہر پر اپنی بیوی کی تجہیز وتکفین ہے چاہے وہ تنگدست ہو، اصبح روایت میں۔ تشریح : اصل تو یہ ہے کہ عورت کی تجہیز و تکفین اس کے اپنے مال سے ہو، کیونکہ موت کے بعد وہ اس کی بیوی نہیں رہی لیکن اگر عورت کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو شوہر کا اخلاقی فرض بنتا ہے کہ وہ اپنے مال سے اس کا انتظام کرے، اور اگر وہ تنگدست ہے تب بھی کوئی انتظام کرے، کیونکہ بیوی زندگی میں اس کی خدمت میں رہی ہے، اور ابھی تک اس کا نان نفقہ شوہر کے ذمے تھا۔ وجه : (۱) میت کے اپنے مال سے کفن لا زم ہے اس کا ثبوت اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ قال ابراهيم يبدأ بالكفن ثم بالدين ثم بالوصية و قال سفيان اجر القبر و الغسل هو من الكفن - ( بخارى شريف، باب الکفن من جميع المال ، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۲۷۴) (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تجہیز و تکفین اخلاقی فرض ہے، اس لئے شوہر پر لازم ہونا چاہئے ۔حدیث یہ ہے۔عن البراء بن عازب قال امرنا رسول الله علي الليل ا بسبع و نهانا عن سبع ، أمرنا باتباع الجنائز ، و عيادة المريض و اجابة الداعي، ونصر المظلوم و ابرار القسم ورد السلام و تشميت العاطش - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الکفن من جميع المال ، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۴ ۱۲۷) اس حدیث کے اشارے میں ہے کہ اگر عورت کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو شوہر پر اس کی تجہیز وتکفین ہے، کیونکہ یہ میت کے حق میں سے ہے۔ ترجمه : (۸۹۲) اور جس کے پاس مال نہیں ہے تو اس کا کفن اس پر ہے جس پر اس کا نفقہ لازم ہے۔ اور جس پر نفقہ ہے وہ نہ ہوتو بیت المال پر ،اور عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے یا ظلم کی وجہ سے بیت المال بھی نہ دے تو لوگوں پر ہے، اور جو تجہیز پر قدرت نہ رکھتا ہوتو مانگے اپنے علاوہ سے [یعنی قدرت والے سے ] تشریح : کسی آدمی کے پاس کفن کی رقم نہ ہو تو جس پر اس کا نفقہ لازم تھا اس پر کفن لا زم ہوگا، اور اس کے پاس بھی اتنا پیسہ نہیں ہے تو بیت المال سے دلوائے ، اور وہ بھی نہ دے سکے تو عام لوگوں پر اس کا نفقہ لازم ہوگا اور صورت یہ بنے گی کہ جو صاحب قدرت ہیں ان سے مانگ کر کفن پورا کرے
(891) The husband is responsible for preparing his wife (for burial) even if he is poor, in the more correct view. (892) And for one who has no wealth, his shroud is upon the one whose nafaqah is obligatory for him. And if the one obligated for his nafaqah is not found, then from the bayt al-mal. Translation (891): The husband is responsible for the preparation and shrouding of his wife even if he is poor, in the more correct narration. Explanation: The original principle is that the wife's preparation and shrouding are from her own wealth, because after death she is no longer his wife. But if the wife has no wealth, it becomes the husband's moral duty to arrange from his own wealth. And if he is poor, he still must arrange, because the wife served him in life and her maintenance was his responsibility. Evidence: (1) The shroud is necessary from the deceased's own wealth, as in the saying of a Tabi'i: Ibrahim said: Begin with the shroud, then the debt, then the will. And Sufyan said: The cost of the grave and washing are from the shroud. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab al-kafn min jami' al-mal, p. 203, no. 1274) (2) The hadith indicates that preparation and shrouding are a moral duty, so it should be obligatory for the husband. The hadith: From al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, he said: The Messenger of Allah commanded us to do seven things and forbade us from seven: He commanded us to follow funerals, visit the sick, accept invitations, help the wronged, fulfill oaths, return greetings, and say 'Yarhamukallah' to the sneezer. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab al-kafn min jami' al-mal, p. 203, no. 1274) This hadith indicates that if the wife has no wealth, the husband is responsible for her preparation and shrouding, because it is part of the rights of the deceased. Translation (892): And for one who has no wealth, his shroud is upon the one whose nafaqah is obligatory for him. And if the one obligated for his nafaqah is not found, then from the bayt al-mal. And if the bayt al-mal does not give due to inability or oppression, then upon the people. And if someone is unable to prepare, he should ask from others (i.e., those who have the means). Explanation: If a man has no money for a shroud, then the one who was obligated to provide his maintenance must provide the shroud. If that person also has no money, then from the public treasury. If the treasury cannot provide, then it becomes the obligation of the general Muslims, and they should collect from those who have the means.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the responsibility for shrouding and preparing the deceased. The first part (891) states that a husband is responsible for his wife's shrouding even if he is poor, in the more correct view. The original principle is that the expense is from the wife's wealth, but if she has none, the husband must bear it as a moral duty. The proof includes statements of the Tabi'in and a hadith about following funerals. The second part (892) states the general rule: For anyone without wealth, the shroud is the responsibility of the one who was obligated for their maintenance (nafaqah). If that person is absent or unable, then from the Muslim treasury (bayt al-mal). If that fails, then upon the Muslim community, who should collect from the wealthy.

Key Terms
تجهيز (tajhiz): Preparation of the deceased for burial, including washing, shrouding, and burial expenses.
تكفين (takfin): Shrouding the deceased in a kafan.
في الاصح (fi al-asahh): In the more correct narration/view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, under what condition is a husband obligated to shroud his wife?
A) Only if the wife requested it.
B) Only if the son is absent.
C) If the wife has no wealth, even if the husband is poor.
D) He is never obligated.

Key Takeaway
A husband must shroud his wife if she has no wealth, even if he himself is poor – this is the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling.

Hierarchy of Responsibility for Shrouding the Poor
Ruling on hierarchy of responsibility for the shroud of a poor deceased person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of who must shroud a deceased person who has no wealth.

Core Idea
The shroud of a poor person falls on the nafaqah-holder, then bayt al-mal, then the community.

This lesson explains the priority order for bearing the shrouding expenses of a deceased person who leaves no estate. It begins with the person who was obligated to provide nafaqah (maintenance) during life, then the public treasury, and finally the general Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first in line: the nafaqah-holder
The text states that for one who has no wealth, the shroud is upon the one whose nafaqah was obligatory for him. This includes the father for his child, the husband for his wife (already covered), etc.
The nafaqah-holder is typically the same as the inheritors but not always.
2
Identify the second level: Bayt al-Mal
If the nafaqah-holder is not found or cannot afford, the expense moves to the Bayt al-Mal (public treasury). This is a public fund for the welfare of Muslims.
The Bayt al-Mal is a theoretical institution in classical fiqh; in practice, it refers to state or community funds.
3
Identify the third level: the Muslim community
If the Bayt al-Mal does not or cannot pay (due to inability or injustice), then the responsibility falls upon the general body of Muslims, who should collect from those with means.
This is a collective duty (fard kifayah) on the community to ensure the deceased is properly buried.
4
Understand the final option: asking from others
The text concludes: 'If someone is unable to prepare, he should ask from others'—meaning the person handling the burial (e.g., the guardian) may seek charity from wealthier individuals.
This ensures the deceased is not left unshrouded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the responsibility for shrouding and preparing the deceased. The first part (891) states that a husband is responsible for his wife's shrouding even if he is poor, in the more correct view. The original principle is that the expense is from the wife's wealth, but if she has none, the husband must bear it as a moral duty. Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance obligation, including food, clothing, and shelter.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi hierarchy, who is responsible for the shroud if the nafaqah-holder cannot be found?
A) The deceased's children.
B) The Bayt al-Mal.
C) The entire Muslim community immediately.
D) The state ruler.

Key Takeaway
The shroud of a poor deceased must be provided by the nafaqah-holder, then Bayt al-Mal, then the community – no one should be left unshrouded.

Husband's Duty for Wife's Burial and Kafan for the Poor
Ruling on husband's obligation and kafan responsibility hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of responsibility for the burial preparation (tajhiz) of a deceased and apply the ruling that the husband must provide for his wife even if he is in hardship.

Core Idea
The husband's moral duty to bury his wife remains even if he is poor; kafan comes from the deceased's own wealth first, then dependents, then Bayt al-Mal.

Death does not erase all obligations; the husband must ensure his wife is properly buried, reflecting her lifelong service. The text also outlines a clear priority for who provides the shroud when the deceased has no means—starting with the deceased's own money, then the one whose maintenance was obligatory, then the state treasury, and finally the community. This lesson will unpack these rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Read the first part of the source: 'Upon the man is the preparation of his wife, even if he is in hardship, according to the correct view.' Determine the act (tajhiz) and its legal status.
The phrase 'according to the correct view' signals an ikhtilaf (disagreement) within the school; here the stronger opinion is chosen.
2
Analyze the rationale for the husband's duty
The commentary explains that although the marriage ends at death, the husband had the obligation of nafaqah (maintenance) during her life, and it is a moral duty. Consider the ethical dimension.
3
Trace the priority of responsibility for kafan
The text gives a chain: (1) the deceased's own wealth, (2) the person whose maintenance was obligatory on them (e.g., husband for wife, father for child), (3) Bayt al-Mal, (4) the community if Bayt al-Mal fails.
This hierarchy is based on the principle that obligations transfer to those who were financially responsible during life.
4
Examine the proofs (dalil)
Two hadith are cited: the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i about prioritizing the shroud over debts and will, and the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib listing obligations toward the deceased. Identify how these support the ruling.
The hadith texts are quoted partially; note that they are ahad (solitary) reports, so their epistemological weight is zanni (speculative).
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
The text labels the view 'في الاصح' (as-sahh) indicating it is the preferred Hanafi view. Other schools may differ, e.g., the Shafi'i school might not oblige the husband if he is poor. Understand the thamarah (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى الرجل تجهيز امرأته ولو معسّرا في الاصح (۸۹۱) ومن لا مال له فكفنه على من تلزمه نفقته وان لم يوجد من تجب عليه نفقته ففى بيت المال فان لم يعط عجزا او ظلما فعلى الناس ويسأل له التجهيز من لا يقدر عليه غيره
ترجمه : شوہر پر اپنی بیوی کی تجہیز وتکفین ہے چاہے وہ تنگدست ہو، اصبح روایت میں۔ تشریح : اصل تو یہ ہے کہ عورت کی تجہیز و تکفین اس کے اپنے مال سے ہو، کیونکہ موت کے بعد وہ اس کی بیوی نہیں رہی لیکن اگر عورت کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو شوہر کا اخلاقی فرض بنتا ہے کہ وہ اپنے مال سے اس کا انتظام کرے، اور اگر وہ تنگدست ہے تب بھی کوئی انتظام کرے، کیونکہ بیوی زندگی میں اس کی خدمت میں رہی ہے، اور ابھی تک اس کا نان نفقہ شوہر کے ذمے تھا۔ وجه : (۱) میت کے اپنے مال سے کفن لا زم ہے اس کا ثبوت اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ قال ابراهيم يبدأ بالكفن ثم بالدين ثم بالوصية و قال سفيان اجر القبر و الغسل هو من الكفن - ( بخارى شريف، باب الکفن من جميع المال ، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۲۷۴) (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تجہیز و تکفین اخلاقی فرض ہے، اس لئے شوہر پر لازم ہونا چاہئے ۔حدیث یہ ہے۔عن البراء بن عازب قال امرنا رسول الله علي الليل ا بسبع و نهانا عن سبع ، أمرنا باتباع الجنائز ، و عيادة المريض و اجابة الداعي، ونصر المظلوم و ابرار القسم ورد السلام و تشميت العاطش - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الکفن من جميع المال ، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۴ ۱۲۷) اس حدیث کے اشارے میں ہے کہ اگر عورت کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو شوہر پر اس کی تجہیز وتکفین ہے، کیونکہ یہ میت کے حق میں سے ہے۔
ترجمه (مکمل): اور جس کے پاس مال نہیں ہے تو اس کا کفن اس پر ہے جس پر اس کا نفقہ لازم ہے۔ اور جس پر نفقہ ہے وہ نہ ہوتو بیت المال پر ،اور عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے یا ظلم کی وجہ سے بیت المال بھی نہ دے تو لوگوں پر ہے، اور جو تجہیز پر قدرت نہ رکھتا ہوتو مانگے اپنے علاوہ سے [یعنی قدرت والے سے ] تشریح : کسی آدمی کے پاس کفن کی رقم نہ ہو تو جس پر اس کا نفقہ لازم تھا اس پر کفن لا زم ہوگا، اور اس کے پاس بھی اتنا پیسہ نہیں ہے تو بیت المال سے دلوائے ، اور وہ بھی نہ دے سکے تو عام لوگوں پر اس کا نفقہ لازم ہوگا اور صورت یہ بنے گی کہ جو صاحب قدرت ہیں ان سے مانگ کر کفن پورا کرے
Upon the man is the preparation of his wife [for burial], even if he is in hardship, according to the correct view. And whoever has no wealth, his shroud is upon the one whose maintenance was obligatory upon him. And if the one upon whom maintenance is obligatory is not found, then from the public treasury. And if it is not given due to inability or injustice, then upon the people. And one asks for his preparation from those who are able beyond himself. Translation: The preparation and shrouding of the wife is upon the husband even if he is poor, according to the soundest narration. Explanation: Originally, the woman's preparation and shroud are from her own wealth, because after death she is not his wife. But if she has no wealth, it becomes the husband's moral duty to arrange from his own wealth, even if he is in hardship, because the wife served him during her life, and her maintenance was his responsibility. Proofs: (1) There is a saying of a Tabi'i: Ibrahim said, 'One begins with the shroud, then the debt, then the will.' Sufyan said, 'The cost of the grave and washing is part of the shroud.' (Bukhari, Chapter on shroud from total wealth, p. 203, no. 1274) (2) The hadith of Bara' bin Azib: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded us to do seven things and prohibited us from seven things: he commanded us to follow the funeral procession, visit the sick, accept invitations, help the oppressed, fulfill oaths, return greetings, and say Yarhamukallah to the sneezer.' (Bukhari, Chapter on shroud from total wealth, p. 203, no. 4127?) This hadith indicates that if the woman has no wealth, the husband's preparation and shrouding is his duty because it is a right of the deceased. Translation (complete): And whoever has no wealth, his shroud is upon the one whose maintenance was obligatory upon him. And if the one upon whom maintenance is obligatory is not found, then from the public treasury. And if the public treasury does not give due to inability or injustice, then upon the people. And whoever is unable to prepare, should ask from others [i.e., those who are able].
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage covers two main points: (1) The husband is responsible for arranging his wife's burial, even if he is poor. This is because although after death the marital bond ends, the husband had the duty of maintenance during her life, and it is a moral obligation. (2) If the deceased has no personal wealth, the kafan is the responsibility of whoever was obligated to provide nafaqah for them. If such a person does not exist or cannot provide, the state treasury (Bayt al-Mal) should cover it. If Bayt al-Mal fails due to inability or injustice, the general Muslim community is responsible, and one should ask the wealthy for assistance.

Key Terms
تجهيز (tajhiz): Preparation for burial, including washing, shrouding, and funeral.
كفن (kafan): The shroud used to wrap the deceased.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Islamic state used for communal expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first source to be used for the kafan of a deceased person?
A) The husband
B) The Bayt al-Mal
C) The deceased's own wealth
D) The community

Key Takeaway
The husband must provide for his wife's burial even if poor; the kafan of any deceased is taken from their own wealth first, then from the one who owed them nafaqah, then Bayt al-Mal, and finally the community.

The Sunnah Shroud for a Man: Three Garments
Describes the recommended shroud for a man.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended garments for a man's shroud and explain the characteristics of the qamis based on the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The sunnah shroud for a man mirrors his everyday dress: three pieces, with a shirt that has no sleeves and is left unsewn.

In this lesson, we examine the recommended shroud for a man according to the Hanafi school. The source text from Thamaratun Najah specifies three garments and their features, grounding the ruling in the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Understanding this helps avoid common errors in funeral preparation, such as sewing the qamis or using too few pieces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three garments
Read the source to list the three pieces: qamis (shirt), izaar (waist-wrapper), lifaafa (outer wrapper). Understand their functions.
2
Analyze the qamis specifications
Note that the qamis has no sleeves, no hem, no front opening; it is made by tearing a hole for the head and is not sewn.
3
Determine the ruling level
Recognize that the three-piece shroud is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not fard. An acceptable covering is sufficient for validity.
4
Connect to the prophetic practice
Examine the hadith from Aisha that the Prophet was shrouded in three white cloths without a sewn shirt or turban. This is the proof (dalil).
5
Distinguish sunnah from obligation
Understand that if the shroud consists of only one or two pieces covering the body, the obligation is fulfilled but the sunnah is missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكفن الرجل سنةً قميص وازار ولفافة مما يلبسه في حيوته
ترجمه : مرد کا سنت کفن قمیص اور از ار اور چادر ہیں، جسکو وہ اپنی زندگی میں پہنا کرتے تھے۔ تشریح : مرد زندگی میں عموما تین کپڑے پہنا کرتے تھے اس لئے کفن بھی تین کپڑوں میں دیا جائے گا، اس سے پورا جسم ڈھک جائے گا۔ لیکن قمیص اس طرح کا ہوگا کہ اس میں آستین نہیں ہوگی اور نہ دامن اور کلی ہوگی ۔ بلکہ درمیان میں پھاڑ کر سر گھسانے کا بنا دیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کو سیا بھی نہیں جائے گا۔ اس طرح تین کپڑے پورے کر دیئے جائیں گے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین کپڑے میں کفن دیا ۔ عن عائشة ان رسول الله الله كفن في ثلثة الواب يمانية بيض سحولية من كرسف ليس فيهن قميص ولا عمامة (بخاری شریف ، باب الثياب البيض للكفن ،ص۲۰۲
The sunnah kafan of a man is a qamis, an izaar, and a wrapper, from what he used to wear in his life. Translation: The sunnah shroud for a man is a shirt, a waist-wrapper, and a sheet, which he used to wear in his life. Explanation: Men usually wore three garments in life, so the shroud will also be given in three garments, covering the whole body. But the shirt will be such that it has no sleeves and no hem and opening; rather, it is made by tearing in the middle for the head to enter, and it is not sewn. Thus three garments are completed. Proof: (1) In this hadith, the shroud was given in three garments: from Aisha that the Messenger of Allah was shrouded in three Yemeni white cloths of cotton, without a shirt or turban. (Bukhari, Chapter on white cloths for shroud, p. 202)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This ruling specifies the recommended (sunnah) shroud for a man: three garments similar to what he wore in life — a qamis (a shirt-like garment without sleeves), an izaar (lower wrap), and a lifaafa (outer wrapper). The qamis is not sewn and has no sleeves. This is based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet was shrouded in three white Yemeni cloths without a sewn shirt or turban.

Key Terms
قميص (qamis): A shirt-like garment without sleeves and without a hem, made by tearing for the head.
ازار (izaar): A lower wrap covering the lower body.
لفافة (lifaafa): An outer wrapper that covers the entire body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many pieces make up the sunnah kafan for a man according to this text?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The sunnah shroud for a man comprises three garments: a sleeveless unsewn qamis, an izaar, and a lifaafa, based on the Prophet's practice.

Braiding the Deceased Woman's Hair: Hanafi Practice
Ruling on handling woman's hair in shroud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for handling a deceased woman's hair in the shroud and explain the proof from the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah.

Core Idea
A woman's braided hair is placed on her chest over the qamis, following the Prophet's practice.

In the Hanafi school, the shrouding of a woman includes specific attention to her hair. This lesson explains the recommended practice of braiding the hair and placing it on the chest over the qamis, as derived from the actions of the Companions when shrouding the Prophet's daughter. We will examine the ruling, the supporting evidence, and how it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its level
Identify the specific act (braiding and placing hair) and determine its hukm (sunnah muakkadah) as per the Hanafi school.
The act is recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah cited in the text. Note that it comes from Bukhari and Muslim.
This is a sahih hadith with zanni thubut but qati dalala.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith supports the Hanafi practice: the Companions divided the hair into three plaits, placing two on the sides (which corresponds to the chest when lying down) and one behind.
The Hanafi school adopts the practice of two braids on the chest, considering the third plait as placed behind.
4
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Note that some other schools may place the hair loosely behind the back. Understand that this is a valid difference of opinion.
Both practices are permissible; the Hanafi position is based on the explicit action of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خمار ا (۹۰۰) ويجعل شعرها ضفيرتين على صدرها فوق القميص. لغت: درع: کرتا، قمیص، ازار: لنگی، خمار: اوڑھنی، یہ خمر سے ہے، ڈھانکنا۔ ترجمه : (۹۰۰) اور عورت کے بالوں کی دو چوٹیاں کر کے سینہ پر قمیص کے اوپر رکھی جائیں۔ تشریح: قمیص پہنانے کے بعد عورت کے بالوں کو دو حصے کر کے چوٹی کی طرح بنالے اور دونوں کو قمیص کے اوپر سینے پر ڈال دے وجه : (ا) عن ام عطية قالت : وضفرنا رأسها ثلاثة قرون ثم ألقيناها خلفها مقدم رأسها و قرنيها (ابوداؤد شریف، باب کیف غسل المیت ج ثانی ص ۹۲ نمبر ۳۱۴۴ / بخاری شریف، باب یلقی شعر المرأة خلفها،ص۱۶۸، نمبر ۱۲۶۳)اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بال کے تین حصے کئے اور ایک حصہ پیچھے ڈالا ، اور دو حصے دونوں طرف ڈال دئے ۔ (۲) حدثنا أم عطية أنهن جعلن رأس بنت رسول الله الا الله ثلاثة قرون نقضنه ثم غسلنه ثم جعلنه ثلاثة قرون ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب نقض شعر المرأة ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۱۲۶۰ر مسلم شریف ، باب فی غسل میت ، ص ۳۷۸، نمبر ۲۱۷۴/۹۳۹) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ بال کے تین حصے کئے جائیں۔۔ ضفیرہ: چوٹی۔
(900) And her hair is made into two braids on her chest above the qamis. Lexicon: dir': shirt, qamis; izar: loincloth; khimar: head-covering, from 'khamr' meaning to cover. Translation: (900) And the woman's hair is made into two braids and placed on the chest above the qamis. Explanation: After putting on the qamis, the woman's hair is divided into two parts, braided, and both are placed on the chest over the qamis. Evidence: (1) From Umm 'Atiyyah who said: We braided her hair into three plaits, then we placed them behind her, one on the front of her head and two on the sides. (Abu Dawud, Bab Kayfa Ghusl al-Mayyit, vol. 2, p. 92, no. 3144; Bukhari, Bab Yulqi Sha'r al-Mar'ah Khalfaha, p. 168, no. 1263) This hadith indicates that the hair was divided into three parts, one placed behind and two on the sides. (2) Umm 'Atiyyah narrated that they made the hair of the daughter of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) into three plaits, they undid it, then washed it, then made it into three plaits. (Bukhari, Bab Naqd Sha'r al-Mar'ah, p. 202, no. 1260; Muslim, Bab fi Ghusl al-Mayyit, p. 378, no. 2174/939) This hadith also indicates that the hair is divided into three plaits. Dafirah: braid.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil) from the Hanafi school regarding the treatment of a deceased woman's hair during shrouding. The author states that after putting on the qamis (a shirt-like garment), the woman's hair should be parted into two sections, braided, and then placed on her chest over the qamis. The term 'dafiratayn' (two braids) is used, though the hadith evidence mentions three plaits. The author reconciles this by noting that the two braids on the chest correspond to the side plaits while the third plait is behind. The primary evidence is the practice of Umm 'Atiyyah and the Companions when shrouding the Prophet's daughter. This ruling is specific to women in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ضفيرتين (dafiratayn): Two braids or plaits of hair
خمار (khimar): A headcovering or veil for a woman
قمیص (qamis): A shirt-like garment, the innermost layer of the shroud

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Braiding a deceased woman's hair into two plaits and placing them on her chest over the qamis is a recommended sunnah practice in the Hanafi school, supported by the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah.

Order of Layers in a Woman's Shroud
Procedure with proof from custom and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of wrapping a woman's shroud and explain the evidence for each layer.

Core Idea
The shroud mirrors life: khimar over qamis, then izar, then khirqa, then lifafah.

Shrouding the deceased is an act of worship (fard kifayah) with specific procedures. This lesson focuses on the order of layers for a woman's shroud, which the Hanafi school derives from the customary practice of covering during life and a narration from a female Companion. Knowing the correct order ensures the kafan is applied in a Sunnah-recommended manner.

Guided Path
1
List the five pieces
Identify each piece of the woman's shroud: qamis (shirt), khimar (head-cover), izar (loincloth), khirqa (chest band), lifafah (outer sheet).
Men have a shroud of three pieces; women add the khimar and khirqa.
2
Determine the sequence from the text
Read the passage and note the order: first qamis, then hair placed on chest over qamis, then khimar over qamis and hair, then izar around lower body, then khirqa over izar, then lifafah over everything.
The khirqa is placed after the izar to give chest support.
3
Identify the evidence
The author cites two proofs: (1) the living woman's habit of wearing the khimar under the outer sheet and over the qamis, (2) the narration from Umm al-Humayd about Hafsah washing the lifafah and placing the khirqa over it.
The narration is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and is considered zanni in both transmission and meaning.
4
Classify the ruling
The Hanafi school holds that this order is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended). Following it is meritorious but not obligatory; the shroud is still valid if the order is changed.
There is no sin in reversing the order, but it is better to follow the Sunnah.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may use fewer layers or different sequencing. The Hanafi insistence on five pieces and this order is based on their reliance on the practice of the salaf as transmitted.
This is a legitimate area of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ۹۰۱) ثم الخمار فوقه تحت ثم اللفافة ثم الخرقة فوقها. ترجمه : (۹۰۱) پھر اوڑھنی قمیص کے اوپر چادر کے نیچے، پھر پستان بند اوڑھنی کے اوپر [ پھر سب کے اوپر چادر ] تشریح : اس عبارت میں کفن پہنانے کا طریقہ بتارہے ہیں کہ [1] پہلے کرتا پہنائیں ۔ پھر بال کے دو حصے کریں ۔اور کرتے کے اوپر دائیں بائیں سینے پر ڈال دیں (۲) پھر کرتی اور بالوں پر اوڑھنی پیٹیں [۳] پھر۔ میت پر لنگی یعنی از ار پیٹیں [۴] پھر ۔ازار کے اوپر پستان بند پیٹیں [۵] پھر۔ اسکے اوپر لفافہ یعنی لمبی چادر لپیٹیں ۔ وجه : (۱) زندگی میں جب اوڑھنی سر پر ڈالا کرتی تھی تو قمیص کے اوپر لکھی تھی۔ اور چادر کے اندر ہوا کرتی تھی ۔ موت کے بعد بھی اسی کیفیت سے کفن دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ سألت ام الحميد ابنة سيرين هل رأيت حفصة اذا غسلت اللفافة ثم الخرقة فوقها (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۴۳، في المرأة كيف تخمر ، ج ثانی جص ۴۶۶ نمبر ۱۱۱۰۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زندگی کی طرح اوڑھنی سر پر ڈالی جائے گی ۔ باقی دلیل او پر گزر چکی ہے۔
(901) Then the khimar over the qamis and under the lifafah, then the khirqa (chest band) over it, then the lifafah. Translation: (901) Then the head-covering over the qamis and under the sheet, then the chest band over the head-covering, then the sheet over everything. Explanation: This passage explains the method of shrouding a woman: [1] First put on the qamis. Then part the hair into two sections and place them on the chest over the qamis. [2] Then wrap the khimar over the qamis and the hair. [3] Then wrap the izar (loincloth) around the lower body. [4] Then wrap the khirqa (chest band) over the izar. [5] Then wrap the lifafah (sheet) over everything. Evidence: (1) In life, when a woman used to cover her head, the khimar would be worn over the qamis and under the outer sheet. Similarly, after death, the same method is used. This is supported by the narration: 'I asked Umm al-Humayd bint Sirin: Did you see Hafsah when she washed the lifafah and then the khirqa over it?' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 43, Fi al-Mar'ah Kayfa Tukhamir, vol. 2, p. 466, no. 11107). From this, it is learned that the khimar is placed on the head as in life. The remaining evidence has passed earlier.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage details the order of wrapping the woman's shroud, which is a procedural ruling (hukm) in the Hanafi school. The order is: first the qamis (shirt), then the hair placed over it, then the khimar (head-covering) over the qamis and hair, then the izar (loincloth) around the lower body, then the khirqa (chest band) over the izar, and finally the lifafah (outer sheet). The evidence is based on the customary practice during life and a narration from Umm al-Humayd about Hafsah. The author emphasizes that the shroud should resemble the living woman's clothing. This is a specific Hanafi practice.

Key Terms
خرقة (khirqa): A chest band or wrapper, a specific piece of the woman's shroud
لفافة (lifafah): The outer sheet that wraps the entire body
ازار (izar): A waist-wrapper or loincloth covering the lower body

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi order of wrapping a woman's shroud, what is placed over the qamis and hair before the izar?
A) The lifafah
B) The khirqa
C) The khimar
D) The izar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah order for a woman's shroud is: qamis, hair on chest, khimar, izar, khirqa, lifafah — based on custom and a narration.

Perfuming the Shroud with Incense in Odd Numbers
Ruling on perfuming the shroud with incense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fumigating the shroud, identify the proof, and apply the ruling to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
Fumigate the shroud three times — an odd number, as the Prophet instructed.

This lesson examines the recommendation to perfume the shroud of the deceased with incense. The Hanafi school derives this practice from a specific hadith, emphasizing odd numbers. Understanding this ruling helps in properly preparing the deceased for burial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Fumigating the shroud with incense before wrapping the deceased. What is the hukm? Sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Jabir (RA): 'When you fumigate the deceased, do it an odd number of times.' Also specifically: 'Fumigate the shroud of the deceased three times.'
References: Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'awtiru' (do it odd) and the numerical specification 'thalath' (three) indicate the recommended practice. In Hanafi usul, the imperative suggests recommendation unless there is evidence for obligation—here, the context of funeral rites confirms it is sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools consider fumigation merely permissible without emphasis on odd numbers or specific count. Hanafis hold it as a sunnah with a specific number based on the explicit wording.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that it is recommended to fumigate three times (or any odd number, but three is the specified practice).
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the recommendation to fumigate the shroud with incense an odd number of times before wrapping the deceased. The Hanafi school considers this a sunnah practice. The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet (ﷺ) instructed to fumigate the deceased with incense an odd number of times, specifically three times. The term 'watran' means odd, and the school emphasizes odd numbers for such acts. This ruling applies to both men and women.

وترة (watran): Odd number (e.g., 1, 3, 5)

Fumigating the Shroud in Odd Numbers
Ruling with proof on fumigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on fumigating the shroud in odd numbers, identify its basis in hadith, and explain why it is sunnah muakkadah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Fumigate the shroud three times — a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on fumigating (tajmir) the shroud before wrapping the deceased. The text presents the practice, cites the prophetic command, and distinguishes it from prohibited funeral practices. We will work through the proof and the legal classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Fumigation of the shroud. What is the hukm? Sunnah muakkadah.
The act is not wajib, but a confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: hadith of Jabir (command to fumigate odd) and hadith of Abu Hurairah (prohibition of fire/voice).
Both are ahad hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The imperative 'ajmiru' indicates command; in Hanafi usul, a command implies sunnah when not accompanied by qarinah making it wajib. The context of honoring the deceased supports sunnah.
The command is taken as sunnah, not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which school disagrees? Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it mubah. The Hanafi position is sunnah muakkadah due to the explicit command.
The difference is in interpreting the imperative.
5
Apply the ruling practically
When preparing the shroud, fumigate it three times before wrapping. Avoid following the funeral with fire or loud voices.
The odd number (three) is the minimum recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the fumigation (tajmir) of the shroud before wrapping the deceased. The matn states that the wrappers (lifafah) and the piece (khirqah) are placed, and then the shrouds are fumigated with incense an odd number of times. The proof is from the hadith of Jabir: the Prophet commanded that when fumigating the deceased, it should be done in odd numbers, and specifically three times for the shroud. The second hadith from Abu Hurairah prohibits following the funeral with fire or loud voice, which is related to the prohibition of using fire in funerals. The fumigation is a sunnah that honors the deceased, and the odd number (preferably three) is emphasized to distinguish from even numbers associated with the practice of other faiths.

Key Terms
اللفافة (al-lifāfah): The outermost wrapper or sheet used to cover the entire body in the shroud.
الخرقة (al-khirqah): A piece of cloth placed over the lifafah, often to wrap the head and feet.
الاجمار (al-ijmār): Fumigation or perfuming with incense, especially using a censer (mijmar) that produces smoke and embers.

Shrouding the Woman: Placing the Khimar and Covering the Face
Description of how to place the khimar on a deceased woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of wrapping the khimar on a deceased woman and explain the proof from the practice of the early Muslims.

Core Idea
The woman's khimar in the shroud also covers her face—a unique Hanafi practice rooted in the sunnah of the female Companions.

In this lesson, we examine a specific practice in the Hanafi school regarding the shrouding of a deceased woman. The passage from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah describes how a woman's khimar (headcover) is used as part of the kafan, with an extra length that is folded to also cover the face. This may seem surprising to those accustomed to leaving the face exposed, but it is an established practice among early Muslim women. We will analyze the text, identify the proof, and understand why the Hanafi school adopts this as the sunnah method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
What is being described? The question asks about the use of the khimar for a deceased woman. The answer describes a specific method of wrapping the khimar as part of the shroud.
The khimar is a headcover that, in life, covers the hair and neck. In death, it is part of the shroud.
2
Extract the ruling from the description
The text says: 'She would cover her head with it as a living woman covers her head, then from the khimar an arm's length would remain, which she would spread behind her, then she would fold that excess and cover her face with it.' This indicates that the recommended method includes covering the face with the excess cloth.
The ruling is that the face is covered with the khimar, not left exposed.
3
Locate the dalil and its type
The source is a narration from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, attributed to a woman who describes the practice. This is a qawl al-sahabi (saying of a Companion) or athar, which in Hanafi usul is a valid proof, though zanni in both transmission and meaning.
The narration is considered reliable (hasan) and is acted upon in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The specific phrase 'then she would fold that excess and cover her face with it' shows that covering the face is part of the prescribed method. The Hanafi school takes this as evidence that the face should be covered in the shroud.
The wajh al-dalalah is direct: the text explicitly mentions covering the face.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools, such as the Shafi'i, typically do not cover the face of the deceased woman, considering the face to be uncovered like a man's. The Hanafi reliance on this specific athar leads to a different practice.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both views have their proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيف تصنع بخمار المرأة؟ قالت نعم كانت تخمرها كما تخمر الحية ثم يفضل من الخمار قدر ذراع فتفرشه في مؤخرها ثم تعطف تلك الفضلة فتغطى بها وجهها. (مصنف ابن ابی شيبة)
How is the woman's khimar (headcover) used? She said: Yes, she would cover her head with it as a living woman covers her head, then from the khimar an arm's length would remain, which she would spread behind her, then she would fold that excess and cover her face with it.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage describes the method of placing the khimar (head veil) on a deceased woman. The source is Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, quoting a woman who narrates the practice: the khimar is placed on the head as a living woman would wear it, covering the hair. An extra length (about a cubit) is left behind her, then brought forward to cover the face. This indicates that the face of the deceased woman is covered with part of the khimar, unlike a man whose face is left uncovered. The Hanafi school derives from this that for a woman, the entire body including the face is covered in the shroud, and the khimar specifically covers the head and face. The method ensures modesty even after death.

Key Terms
الخمار (al-khimār): A headcover or veil worn by Muslim women, covering the hair and neck, and part of the shroud for a deceased woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is used to cover the feet
B) It is folded and used to cover the face
C) It is removed from the shroud
D) It is left trailing behind

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that the deceased woman's face is covered by the excess of her khimar, following the practice of early Muslim women.

The Shroud of Necessity: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling on the minimum shroud when cloth is scarce, with proof from a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum shroud in necessity and identify the supporting evidence from the hadith of Mus'ab ibn Umayr.

Core Idea
In necessity, a single cloth suffices for the shroud; the head and private parts are prioritized.

This lesson addresses a crucial fiqh principle: when sufficient cloth for a proper shroud is unavailable, what is the minimum requirement? The Hanafi school derives the ruling from the prophetic example of shrouding Mus'ab ibn Umayr with a single cloth. You will learn both the ruling and the methodology of deriving it from the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of shrouding the deceased. The general ruling is fard kifayah. Here, we focus on the minimum requirement when cloth is scarce.
The passage states: 'The shroud of necessity is what is available.'
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt regarding Mus'ab ibn Umayr. This is a sunnah ahad hadith, authentic (qati' al-thubut) but with probable meaning (zanni al-dalalah).
Hadith reference: Sahih Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's instruction to use a single cloth and cover the head with it, while covering the feet with idhkhir, shows that a single cloth suffices, and that covering the head (for men) is prioritized.
The operative action: placing the cloth on the head and using alternative material for the feet.
4
Note the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that if only one cloth is available, it is valid to use it as a shroud. The obligation to cover the entire body is waived in necessity, but the private parts must be covered if possible.
The mufta bihi: covering the entire body is the ideal, but one cloth suffices in necessity.
5
Apply the ruling to other scenarios
Consider cases where even a single cloth is not available, or where non-cloth materials must be used. The principle of necessity (darurah) allows flexibility, but the minimum is to cover the private parts.
The hadith provides analogy (qiyas) for using any available material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكفن الضرورة ما يوجد. عن خباب بن الأرت قال هاجرنا مع رسول الله عام في سبيل الله نبتغى وجه الله منهم مصعب بن عمير قتل يوم احد فلم يوجد له شيء كفن فيه الا نمرة فكنا اذا وضعناها على رأسه خرجت رجلاه و اذا وضعناها على رجليه خرج رأسه فقال رسول الله ضعوها مما يلى رأسه و اجعلوا على رجليه من الاذخر.
And the shroud of necessity is what is available. From Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: We migrated with the Messenger of Allah in the cause of Allah seeking His pleasure. Among them was Mus'ab ibn Umayr who was killed at Uhud, and nothing was found to shroud him except a single cloak. When we placed it over his head, his feet were uncovered; when we placed it over his feet, his head was uncovered. So the Messenger of Allah said: 'Place it over his head and cover his feet with idhkhir (a fragrant plant).'
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when sufficient cloth for a complete shroud is unavailable. The matn states: 'The shroud of necessity is what is available.' This means that in dire circumstances, any piece of cloth, even a single sheet, suffices as a shroud. The proof is the incident of Mus'ab ibn Umayr, who was killed at Uhud and only had a single cloak (namirah) for a shroud. The Prophet directed that it be placed over his head and that his feet be covered with idhkhir (a grass). This shows that necessity allows minimal covering. The Hanafi school derives that in the absence of a full shroud, one must cover the entire body as much as possible; if insufficient, the private parts must be covered, and the rest can be left. The hadith also indicates that covering the head is prioritized for men, as the Prophet placed the cloth on the head.

Key Terms
كفن الضرورة (kafan al-ḍarūrah): The shroud used in situations where sufficient cloth is not available; whatever is found suffices.
النمرة (al-namirah): A type of cloak or mantle, often striped, made of wool or hair, used as an outer garment.
الاذخر (al-idhkhir): A fragrant plant (lemon grass) used to cover the feet of the deceased in the absence of cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet order regarding the shroud of Mus'ab ibn Umayr when only one cloth was available?
A) Wrap the entire body with the cloth and leave the face uncovered
B) Place the cloth on his head and cover his feet with idhkhir
C) Use the cloth to cover only the private parts
D) Wait until more cloth is found

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the hadith of Mus'ab ibn Umayr to establish that in necessity, even a single cloth suffices as a shroud, and covering the head and private parts takes priority.

Shroud of Necessity: What is Available Suffices
Ruling on minimal shroud when full shroud unavailable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the shroud of necessity and apply the hadith proof to a scenario of limited shrouding materials.

Core Idea
In necessity, even a single cloth suffices as a shroud.

When a Muslim dies, the community is obligated to shroud the body in a proper kafan. But what if the standard three-piece shroud is unavailable? This lesson addresses the ruling of necessity: whatever can be found is sufficient. The proof comes from the Prophet's ﷺ treatment of Mus'ab ibn Umayr at Uhud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shrouding the deceased. Normally it is wajib kifayah to use a full shroud (three pieces for male, five for female). In necessity, the requirement reduces to whatever is available.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt recounts that Mus'ab ibn Umayr was shrouded in only a namira (a striped woolen garment) because nothing else was available.
Sahih Muslim, Kitab al-Jana'iz
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's instruction to place the single garment over the head and cover the feet with idhkhir shows that a minimal covering suffices when a full shroud is unavailable.
The command is permissive, indicating a concession (rukhsah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is general agreement among schools that necessity reduces the requirement, though details on minimum may differ. The Hanafi position is that even one cloth is sufficient.
No significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit hadith and the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). The mufta bihi is that whatever is available must be used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۰۳) وكفن الضرورة ما يوجد.
ترجمه : (۹۰۳) ضرورت کے وقت جتنا کفن پایا جائے وہ کافی ہے۔
تشريح : كفن ہے ہی نہیں تو جتنا بن سکے وہی کافی ہے، چاہے ایک چادر ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
وجه : (۱)۔ حدیث یہ ہے . عن خباب بن الأرت قال هاجرنا مع رسول الله عام في سبيل الله نبتغى وجه .. منهم مصعب بن عمير قتل يوم احد فلم يوجد له شيء كفن فيه الا نمرة فكنا اذا وضعناها على رأسه خرجت رجلاه و اذا وضعناها على رجليه خرج رأسه فقال رسول الله عله ضعوها مما يلى رأسه و اجعلوا على رجليه من الاذخر - (مسلم شریف ، باب فی کفن میت ،ص ۳۷۹، نمبر ۷٫۹۴۰ ۲۱۷ ۱۷ بود او د شریف، باب کراهیه المغالاة فی الکفن ،ص ۴۶۱، نمبر ۳۱۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مجبوری کے موقع پر حضرت مصعب ابن عمیر کو صرف ایک چادر میں کفن دیا گیا۔
Translation: (903) The shroud of necessity is what is found. Commentary: If there is no shroud, whatever can be made suffices, even if it is only one sheet. Proof: (1) Hadith from Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: We migrated with the Messenger of Allah seeking His pleasure... among them was Mus'ab ibn Umayr who was killed at Uhud, and nothing was found to shroud him except a namira (a striped woolen garment). When we placed it over his head, his feet were exposed, and when we placed it over his feet, his head was exposed. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Place it over his head and cover his feet with idhkhir (a fragrant plant).' (Muslim, chapter on shrouding the deceased, p. 379, no. 7.940; Abu Dawud, chapter on dislike of extravagance in shrouding, p. 461, no. 3155). This hadith indicates that at a time of necessity, Mus'ab ibn Umayr was shrouded in only one sheet.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the shroud of necessity. The author states the principle: when a full shroud is unavailable, whatever is available suffices. This is a concession (rukhsah) for dire circumstances. Even a single cloth is sufficient. The proof is the hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt, which recounts that the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed to shroud Mus'ab ibn Umayr in a single garment (namira) and cover his feet with idhkhir. This demonstrates that in necessity, a minimal covering is acceptable. The Hanafi school applies this ruling to any situation where the standard three-piece shroud (izar, qamis, lifafah) cannot be obtained.

Key Terms
كفن (kafan): The shroud used to wrap the deceased for burial.
كفن الضرورة (kafan al-darurah): The shroud used when a full shroud is unavailable; whatever can be found suffices.
نمرة (namirah): A striped woolen garment or cloak used as a shroud in the hadith.
اذخر (idhkhir): A fragrant plant (lemon grass) used to cover the feet when the shroud is insufficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

6 min
Funeral Prayer is Fard Kifayah
Ruling with two hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that salat al-janazah is fard kifayah and explain how the imperative in the hadith proofs establishes this obligation.

Core Idea
Janaza prayer is a collective obligation: if some perform it, all are absolved.

This lesson establishes the legal status of the funeral prayer. You will learn that it is not an individual duty but a collective one, meaning that once a sufficient number of Muslims perform it, the obligation falls from the rest. We will examine the two primary hadith proofs used by the Hanafi school and understand how the imperative command indicates obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Note that the act in question is salat al-janazah (funeral prayer). The ruling given is 'fard kifayah' (collective obligation).
2
Understand the meaning of fard kifayah
Fard kifayah means that if a sufficient number of Muslims perform the prayer, the obligation is lifted from the rest. If no one performs it, the entire community incurs sin.
Contrast with fard 'ayn (individual obligation) where each person must perform it.
3
Examine the first hadith proof
The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn: the Prophet commanded 'Stand and pray over him' regarding the Najashi. The imperative verb indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The prayer was for a deceased Muslim ruler not present, showing applicability to all deceased Muslims.
4
Examine the second hadith proof
The hadith of Abu Huraira: the Prophet prayed at the grave of a black man/woman who cleaned the mosque. This shows that even after burial, the prayer is performed, emphasizing its obligatory nature.
The prayer was performed after burial, indicating it is not limited to before burial.
5
Derive the wajh al-dalalah
In both hadith, the Prophet's action and command establish the legal ruling. The imperative 'stand and pray' (qumu sallu) is understood as obligatory per Hanafi principles, and the broader context shows it is a collective duty, not personal to the Najashi.

فصل : في الصلوة على الجنائز
(۹۰۴) الصلوة عليه فرض كفاية.
ضروری نوٹ : اس آیت کے اشارے سے نماز جنازہ کا ثبوت ہے۔ ولا تصل علی احد منهم مات ابدا و لا تقم على قبره - ( آیت ۸۴ ، سورة التوبة ۹)
ترجمه : (۹۰۴) جنازہ پر نماز پڑھنا فرض کفایہ ہے۔
تشريح : فرض کفایہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کچھ لوگوں نے پڑھ لیا تو باقی کے ذمے سے ساقط ہو گیا۔
وجه : (۱) عن عمران بن حصين قال قال لنا رسول الله الله ان اخاكم النجاشي قد مات فقوموا فصلوا عـلـيـه فقمنا فصففنا كما يصف على الميت وصلينا عليه كما يصلى على الميت ۔ (ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی صلوة النبی و علی النجاشی ص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۰۳۹ر بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوة على الجنائز بالمصلى والمسجد ص ۷۷ انمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث میں امر کا صیغہ, فقوموا فصلوا علیہ کا لفظ ہے، جس سے فرض کفایہ ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث سے بھی فرض کفایہ ثابت ہے ۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان اسود رجلا أو امرأة كان يقيم المسجد فمات ولم يعلم النبي علم بموته فذكره ذات يوم فقال ما فعل ذلك الانسان قالوا مات یا رسول الله قال افلا اذنتمونى فقالوا انه كان كذا كذا قصته قال و فحقروا شانه قال فدلوني على قبره قال فاتی قبره فصلی علیه ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر بعد ما يدفن ص ۷۸ نمبر ۱۳۳۷ را بو داؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر ج ثانی ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۳۲۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے ایک عورت کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی ہے۔
Chapter: On the Prayer over the Deceased. (904) The prayer over him is a collective obligation (fard kifayah). Necessary note: This verse indicates the proof for janaza prayer: 'And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave' (Surah al-Tawba 9:84). Translation: (904) Praying over the deceased is fard kifayah. Commentary: Fard kifayah means that if some people pray, the obligation is lifted from the rest. Proof (1): From Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to us: 'Indeed your brother the Najashi has died, so stand and pray over him.' So we stood and lined up as one lines up over the deceased, and we prayed over him as one prays over the deceased. (Tirmidhi, chapter on the Prophet's prayer over the Najashi, p. 201, no. 1039; Bukhari, chapter on praying over the deceased in the prayer place and mosque, p. 77, no. 1327). This hadith contains the imperative form 'stand and pray,' which establishes fard kifayah. (2) This hadith also establishes fard kifayah: From Abu Hurairah that a black man or woman used to clean the mosque and died, and the Prophet was not informed of his death. He mentioned him one day and asked, 'What happened to that person?' They said, 'He died, O Messenger of Allah.' He said, 'Why did you not inform me?' They mentioned his story, and they had belittled him. He said, 'Show me his grave.' So he went to his grave and prayed over him. (Bukhari, chapter on prayer over the grave after burial, p. 78, no. 1337; Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer over the grave, vol. 2, p. 101, no. 3203). This hadith indicates that the Prophet prayed over a woman's grave.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the legal status of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The author states that it is fard kifayah (collective obligation). He first notes that the verse 'nor stand at his grave' implicitly proves the prayer, as the prohibition of standing implies the standing in prayer is an act of worship. The commentary clarifies that fard kifayah means that if a sufficient number of people perform it, the obligation is lifted from all others; however, if no one performs it, everyone sins. Two hadith proofs are provided: first, the Prophet's command to pray over the Najashi using the imperative 'faqumu wa sallu' (stand and pray), which indicates obligation. Second, the Prophet praying at the grave of a black man/woman, showing that the prayer is required even after burial if not performed earlier. Both hadith support the collective obligation nature.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A collective obligation: if a sufficient number of Muslims perform it, the obligation is discharged for all; otherwise all are sinful.
الصلوة على الجنائز (al-salat 'ala al-jana'iz): The funeral prayer performed over the deceased Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What legal status does the Hanafi school assign to salat al-janazah?
A) Fard 'ayn (individual obligation)
B) Fard kifayah (collective obligation)
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah)
D) Wajib (obligatory, below fard)

Key Takeaway
Salat al-janazah is a collective duty (fard kifayah); its obligation is fulfilled when a sufficient number of Muslims pray.

Pillars of Funeral Prayer: Takbirs and Standing
Declaring the integral components of janaza prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two pillars of the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Only two acts are fard in janaza prayer: four takbirs and standing; all else is sunnah.

This lesson examines the essential components of the funeral prayer. The source passage clearly declares that the takbirs (specifically four) and standing are the only pillars. Through Quranic verse and prophetic practice, we learn the basis for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that the pillars of the funeral prayer are the takbirs and standing. Read the matn: 'واركانها التكبيرات والقيام'.
2
Understand the Hanafi specification
The commentary specifies that the takbirs are exactly four and that standing is a separate fard act. Everything else (recitation, supplication, salutation) is sunnah.
3
Examine the proof for standing
The passage cites Quran 9:84 (prohibition of standing for hypocrites, implying standing is an act of worship) and the hadith of the Najashi with the imperative 'stand and pray' (فَقُومُوا فَصَلُّوا). In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation.
The imperative 'قوموا' is a command, which in Hanafi usul yields wujub.
4
Examine the proof for four takbirs
The hadith of Abu Hurairah reports that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said four takbirs over the Najashi. This consistent prophetic action (fi'l) establishes the number as fard.
The hadith is from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
5
Recognize the implications
Since these are pillars, omitting either invalidates the prayer. All other acts (recitation, dua, taslim) are sunnah and their omission does not invalidate.
This is a key differentiator from other prayers.

تشريح : نماز جنازہ میں دو فرض ہیں [1] ایک ہے تکبیر جو حنفیہ کے یہاں چار ہیں [۲] اور دوسرا فرض ہے کھڑا ہونا۔ باقی سب سنتیں ہیں

(بخاری شریف، باب التگیر علی الجنازة اربعاص ۱۷۸ نمبر ۱۳۳۳، مسلم شریف ، باب فی التكبير على الجنازة ، ص۱۳۸۳ نمبر ۲۰۴/۹۵۱ ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوة على المسلم بموت في بلا دالمشرک ص۱۰۱نمبر ۳۲۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز جنازہ میں چار تکبیر کہی جائے گی۔
Chapter on the Prayer. (905) Its pillars are the takbirs and standing. Translation: (905) Its pillars are four takbirs and standing. Commentary: In the funeral prayer, there are two fard acts: [1] the takbir, which according to the Hanafis is four, and [2] standing. All else is sunnah. Proof: (1) 'And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave' (Surah al-Tawba 9:84). This verse indicates not to stand, which proves that standing (qiyam) is fard. (2) From Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to us: 'Indeed your brother the Najashi has died, so stand and pray over him.' We stood and lined up as one lines up over the deceased, and we prayed over him as one prays over the deceased. (Tirmidhi, chapter on the Prophet's prayer over the Najashi, p. 201, no. 1039; Bukhari, chapter on praying over the deceased in the prayer place and mosque, p. 77, no. 1327). This hadith contains the imperative 'stand and pray,' which proves that standing is fard. (3) The proof for four takbirs is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) announced the death of the Najashi on the day he died, and went out with them to the prayer place, lined them up, and said four takbirs over him. (Bukhari, chapter on four takbirs over the deceased, p. 178, no. 1333; Muslim, chapter on takbir over the deceased, p. 1383, no. 951; Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer over a Muslim who dies in a land of polytheists, p. 101, no. 3204). This hadith indicates that four takbirs are said in the funeral prayer.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the pillars (arkan) of the funeral prayer. The author states that the pillars are the takbirs and standing (qiyam). In the commentary, he specifies that according to the Hanafi school, there are exactly two fard acts: the four takbirs and standing. Everything else (recitation, supplication, salutation) is sunnah. The proof for qiyam is twofold: first, the verse from Surah al-Tawba which prohibits standing at the grave of hypocrites; the prohibition implies that standing is an act of worship, proving it is fard for believers. Second, the hadith of the Najashi with the imperative 'stand and pray.' The proof for four takbirs is the hadith of Abu Hurairah stating that the Prophet said four takbirs over the Najashi. This is a key differentiator: Hanafis consider four takbirs as fard, and any addition or reduction would require sajdah al-sahw or invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act; omission invalidates the act entirely.
تکبیر (takbir): The phrase 'Allahu Akbar' said during the prayer; in janaza prayer, four takbirs are fard.
قیام (qiyam): Standing upright during the prayer; in janaza prayer, it is fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer has only two fard acts: four takbirs and standing; all other elements are sunnah.

Pillars of the Funeral Prayer (Arkan al-Janazah)
States the two pillars with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two fard pillars of the Hanafi funeral prayer and cite the Quranic verse and hadiths that prove each.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer has two fard pillars: four takbirs and standing, proven by Quran and hadith.

This lesson explains the two essential pillars of the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school. While the funeral prayer itself is a communal obligation (farḍ kifāyah), its internal components include two farḍ elements: the takbirs (exactly four) and standing (qiyām). The author supports this with clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, which we will examine step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage is about the funeral prayer (ṣalāt al-janāzah) and its internal pillars (arkān). The overall prayer is farḍ kifāyah, but its components are farḍ within the prayer.
2
Locate the first dalīl: Quranic verse
Analyze Sūrah al-Tawbah 9:84: 'And do not stand at his grave.' The prohibition of standing for hypocrites implies that standing is normally required for believers, proving that standing is farḍ.
The verse is used to prove the obligation of standing, not the number of takbirs.
3
Locate the second dalīl: Hadith of the Najashi
Analyze the ḥadīth in which the Prophet commanded 'Stand and pray over your brother the Najashi.' The imperative 'stand' (qoomoo) indicates obligation in Hanafi uṣūl (al-amr yufīdu al-wujūb).
This hadith also establishes the number of takbirs separately through the Prophet's action.
4
Locate the third dalīl: Hadith specifying four takbirs
Analyze the ḥadīth of Abū Hurayrah that the Prophet said four takbirs over the Najashi. This explicit action establishes the number as farḍ.
The number is exactly four; any addition or omission would change the prayer.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Recognize that while the Ḥanafīs insist on four takbirs, Mālikīs sometimes perform five or seven. The Ḥanafī position is based on the explicit Sunnah and their uṣūl principle regarding imperatives.
Understand that the dispute is legitimate (ikhtilāf) and has practical consequences.

Chapter on Prayer. (905) Its pillars are the takbirs and standing. ... Translation: (905) Its pillars are four takbirs and standing. Explanation: The funeral prayer has two fard: [1] one is the takbir, which according to the Hanafis are four, [2] and the second fard is standing. The rest are all sunnah. Proof: (1) The verse 'And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave' (Surah al-Tawbah 9:84) proves that standing is fard. (2) The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn that the Prophet said, 'Your brother the Najashi has died, so stand and pray over him' – the imperative form proves standing is fard. (3) The hadith of Abu Huraira that the Prophet led the funeral prayer for the Najashi and said four takbirs proves that there are four takbirs.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage explains the two pillars (arkan) of the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school. The author states that the funeral prayer has two obligatory (fard) elements: the takbirs (specifically four) and standing (qiyam). Everything else, such as recitation, supplication, and salutations, are sunnah. The author then provides three proofs: first, the Quranic verse (9:84) which uses the negative imperative 'do not stand' implying that standing is normally required; second, the hadith of the Najashi where the Prophet commanded 'stand and pray' using the imperative form, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub) but here it is fard because the command is from the Prophet for the funeral prayer; third, the hadith of Abu Huraira that the Prophet said four takbirs, establishing the number. Note: The funeral prayer itself is fard kifayah (communal obligation), but its internal pillars are fard (individual obligation during the prayer). The Hanafi position is that there are exactly four takbirs; other schools may differ (e.g., Shafi'i say four takbirs also, but Malikis say four or sometimes five). The author emphasizes that standing is fard only if one is able; if one is unable, they may pray sitting, but that is not mentioned here.

Key Terms
اركان (arkan): Pillars or integral parts of the prayer; omission invalidates the prayer.
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; in funeral prayer, there are exactly four fard takbirs.
قیام (qiyam): Standing; fard in funeral prayer for those able to stand.

Six Conditions of Funeral Prayer (Shurut al-Janazah)
List of six conditions for funeral prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six conditions of the funeral prayer and explain why each is necessary for validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is valid only when six conditions are met: Islam, purity, direction, presence, not mounted, on ground.

In this lesson, we examine the six prerequisites (shurut) for the funeral prayer (Salat al-Janazah). These conditions must be fulfilled before the prayer begins; if any is missing, the prayer is invalid. Understanding these conditions helps ensure that the funeral prayer is performed correctly, preserving the rights of the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the six conditions
Commit to memory the six conditions in the order given: Muslim, pure, in front, most body present, not mounted, on ground.
Use the mnemonics like 'MIPMNG' or similar.
2
Understand the rationale
For each condition, ask why it is required. For example, the deceased must be Muslim because the prayer is for believers. He must be pure because prayer requires purity. He must be in front of the imam to follow the sunnah. Most body must be present to represent the person. The imam should not be mounted to ensure humility. The bier must be on the ground to be stable.
These rationales come from hadith and scholarly reasoning.
3
Compare with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school does not require conditions 5 and 6 in the same way. They allow praying while mounted without excuse and allow the bier to be carried during prayer.
This difference has practical implications in crowded settings.

وشرائطها ستة.
(۹۰۶) اسلام الميت (۹۰۷) وطهارته (۹۰۸) وتقدمه (۹۰۹) وحضوره او حضور اکثر بدنه او
نماز جنازہ کے لئے ۶ شرطیں ہیں: ایک نظر میں
ا... میت کا مسلمان ہونا۔
..... اس کا پاک ہونا۔
...... اس کے آگے ہونا۔
تمام نخش یا اس کا اکثر حصہ یا سر کے ساتھ نصف حصہ۔ سامنے ہو۔
اس پر نماز پڑھنے والا بلا عذر سوار نہ ہو۔
...... میت زمین پر ہو۔
And its conditions are six. (906) The deceased being Muslim, (907) and his purity, (908) and his being in front, (909) and his presence or the presence of most of his body or... The funeral prayer has six conditions: In brief: 1. The deceased being Muslim. 2. His being pure. 3. His being in front. 4. Most of his body or half with the head present. 5. The one praying over him not being mounted without excuse. 6. The deceased being on the ground.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage lists the six conditions (shurut) for the validity of the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school. Conditions are prerequisites that must be fulfilled before the prayer; if any condition is missing, the prayer is invalid. The six conditions are: (1) The deceased must be Muslim; (2) The deceased's body must be ritually pure (i.e., given ghusl); (3) The deceased's body must be placed in front of the imam (qibla direction); (4) The entire body or at least most of it (or half including the head) must be present; (5) The one leading the prayer must not be mounted on an animal unless there is an excuse; (6) The deceased must be on the ground (not carried during prayer). These conditions are derived from practice and hadith. Note: Condition 4 allows prayer with half the body if it includes the head. Condition 5 is specific to the imam; followers may be mounted if needed. Condition 6 means the bier must be placed on the ground, not carried on shoulders or on an animal.

Key Terms
شرائط (shurut): Conditions that must be present for the funeral prayer to be valid; if missing, the prayer is invalid.
تقدمه (taqaddumuhu): The deceased being placed in front of the imam (towards qibla).
حضوره او حضور اکثر بدنه (huduruhu aw hudur akthar badanihi): Presence of the entire body or at least most of it including the head.
عدم كون المصلي راكباً (adam kawn al-musalli rakiban): The condition that the one leading the prayer must not be mounted on an animal (or vehicle) without an excuse.
كون الميت على الارض (kawn al-mayyiti ala al-ard): The condition that the deceased's body must be placed on the ground during the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six conditions of funeral prayer according to this passage?
A) The deceased being Muslim
B) The deceased being in front of the imam
C) The presence of four takbirs
D) The deceased being on the ground

Key Takeaway
The six conditions ensure the funeral prayer is valid; missing any invalidates it.

First Condition: Deceased Must Be Muslim
Ruling with proof: condition of Islam for funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of Islam for the deceased in funeral prayer and explain the Quranic proof from Surah al-Tawbah 9:84.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim is not entitled to funeral prayer — the Quran explicitly forbids it.

This lesson explains the first of six conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer: the deceased must be a Muslim. Even if the person outwardly appears to be a disbeliever, the prayer is not offered. The primary proof is a clear Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The condition is that the deceased be Muslim. If not, the funeral prayer is invalid.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites Surah al-Tawbah 9:84, where Allah commands the Prophet not to pray over the hypocrites who died in disbelief.
The verse is general in application according to Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition 'la tusal' (do not pray) indicates that praying over a disbeliever is forbidden, thus establishing that Islam is a condition.
The command is understood as a prohibition (haram) which renders the act invalid.
4
Consider the scope
Although the verse was revealed about specific hypocrites, the Hanafi school applies it to all non-Muslims, including apostates and those who concealed disbelief.
The condition is based on actual disbelief, not just outward appearance.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The condition that the deceased be Muslim is unanimously agreed upon and is the operative ruling for fatwa.
No intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۰۶) [1] میت کا مسلمان ہونا۔
تشریح : نماز جنازہ کے لئے شرطیں چھ ہیں، ان میں سے پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ میت مسلمان ہوتب نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی اگر وہ ظاہری طور بھی کافر ہے تو اس کی نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ۔
وجه : (۱) و لا تصل على احد منهم مات ابدا و لا تقم على قبره انهم كفروا بالله و رسوله و ماتوا و هم فاسقون - ( آیت ۸۴ ، سورة التوبۃ ۹) اس آیت میں ہے کہ منافق کا فر ہیں اس لئے اس کی نماز نہ پڑھیں۔
Translation: (906) [1] The deceased being Muslim. Explanation: The funeral prayer has six conditions. Among them, the first condition is that the deceased be Muslim; then the funeral prayer will be offered. If he is even outwardly a disbeliever, his funeral prayer will not be offered. Proof: (1) 'And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave. Indeed, they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger and died while they were defiantly disobedient.' (Surah al-Tawbah 9:84). This verse indicates that the hypocrites are disbelievers, so do not pray over them.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the first condition: the deceased must be Muslim. The author explains that if the deceased is even outwardly a non-Muslim (e.g., a hypocrite who hid disbelief), his funeral prayer is not performed. The proof is the Quranic verse (9:84) where Allah forbids the Prophet from praying over the hypocrites who died in disbelief. Although this verse was directed at the Prophet for a specific group, the Hanafi school applies the general principle that funeral prayer is only for Muslims. The verse's phrase 'and do not stand at his grave' also indicates that standing in prayer for a non-Muslim is prohibited. This condition is based on the clear text. Note: A Muslim who died without repentance but was outwardly Muslim (e.g., a sinful Muslim) still receives funeral prayer; the prohibition is only for those who died in kufr (disbelief). The condition is that the deceased must be recognized as Muslim. If there is doubt, the imam should not pray unless there is evidence of Islam.

Key Terms
اسلام الميت (islam al-mayyit): The condition that the deceased be Muslim; a non-Muslim is not eligible for funeral prayer.
ظاہری طور بھی کافر (zahiri taur bhi kafir): Even if outwardly a disbeliever (e.g., one who concealed disbelief), the funeral prayer is not offered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Surah al-Tawbah 9:84
B) Surah al-Baqarah 2:156
C) Surah al-Nisa 4:48
D) Surah al-Imran 3:185

Key Takeaway
The deceased must be Muslim for the funeral prayer to be valid, as proven by the Quranic prohibition in Surah al-Tawbah 9:84.
