Condition of Purity for the Deceased in Funeral Prayer
Ruling with proof: condition of purity for funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the deceased be ritually pure (tahir) for the funeral prayer and derive this ruling from the hadith of Umm Atiyyah.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is invalid if the deceased is not washed – purity is a binding condition.

This lesson examines the second condition for the validity of the funeral prayer: the deceased must be in a state of ritual purity, which is achieved through ghusl. We will explore the hadith evidence that establishes this rule, the reasoning behind it, and its practical application. Understanding this condition ensures that the funeral prayer is performed correctly and is accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition stated in the passage
Read the passage and locate the explicit condition: the deceased must be pure (tahir). Note how the ruling is framed: if it becomes known that the deceased is impure (napaak), the funeral prayer is not offered.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The passage cites the hadith of Umm Atiyyah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded washing his daughter. Identify the exact wording: 'اغسلنها' (wash her).
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The imperative command 'aghsilnaha' (wash her) indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. This command to wash the deceased proves that purification is a necessary step before the funeral prayer.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the exception for martyrs
Although not mentioned in the passage, the Hanafi school exempts martyrs (shuhada) from washing. Their funeral prayer is valid without ghusl. This exception is based on other evidence.
The exception is agreed upon by all schools.
5
Conclude the ruling
The final ruling: the funeral prayer of an unwashed deceased is invalid if it is possible to wash the body. The condition of purity is established by the hadith and is essential for the validity of the prayer.
The mufta bihi position: washing the deceased is fard kifayah; without it, the janazah prayer is not valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۰۷) [۲] اس کا پاک ہونا۔
تشریح : اگر پتہ چل جائے کہ میت نا پاک ہے تو نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
صلى الله
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے . عن ام عطية قالت دخل علينا رسول الله له حين توفيت ابنته فقال اغسلنها ثلاثا او خمسا او اكثر من ذلك ان رأيتن ذلك بماء وسدر واجعلن في الآخرة كافورا او شيئا من كافور ( بخاری، نمبر ۱۲۵۳) و في حديث اخرى قال ابدأن بميامنها و مواضع الوضوء منها . ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل الميت د وضوءه بالماء والسد رص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۲۵۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب غسل لمیت ،ص ۱۳۷۸ نمبر ۲۱۶۸/۹۳۹) اس میں ہے کہ غسل دے
Translation: (907) [2] His being pure. Explanation: If it becomes known that the deceased is impure, then the funeral prayer will not be offered. Proof: (1) There is a hadith from Umm Atiyyah: 'The Messenger of Allah entered upon us when his daughter died and said: Wash her three times, or five, or more if you see fit, with water and sidr, and put camphor in the last wash.' And in another hadith he said: 'Start with the right side and the places of wudu.' This indicates that he should wash (the deceased).
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage explains the second condition: the deceased must be ritually pure (tahir), meaning that the body has been given a proper ghusl (ritual wash) before the funeral prayer. If it is known that the deceased was not washed (e.g., because of lack of water or neglect), the funeral prayer should not be performed until the body is purified. The proof comes from the hadith of Umm Atiyyah where the Prophet instructed his daughter's washing, showing that washing the deceased is obligatory. Additionally, the instruction to start with the right side and the places of wudu indicates that the washing is a purification that makes the deceased tahir. The Hanafi school holds that the ghusl of the deceased is fard kifayah, and the prayer is only valid if the body is pure. If the body is not washed due to an excuse (e.g., martyr), the condition may be waived, but that is not discussed here. The condition applies to the deceased's body being free from ritual impurity (janabah) and physical impurity (najis).

Key Terms
پاک (pak): Ritually pure; the deceased must be given a proper ghusl to be in a state of purity.
غسل (ghusl): The ritual washing of the deceased's body, obligatory before funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the second condition for the validity of the funeral prayer according to the passage?
A) The deceased must be Muslim.
B) The deceased must be pure (washed).
C) The deceased must be male.
D) The prayer must be performed in a mosque.

Key Takeaway
The deceased must be ritually pure (tahir) before the funeral prayer; the proof is the Prophet's command to wash his daughter.

Six Conditions for Janazah Prayer: Hanafi Proofs
Lists and proves six conditions for Janazah prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for Salat al-Janazah and identify the proof for each condition from Quran, Hadith, or Companion practice.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer requires six pre-conditions — missing any one invalidates it.

Salat al-Janazah is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) that is easy to perform but has specific prerequisites. This passage from Thamaratun Najah enumerates six conditions that must be met before the prayer is valid. Each condition is supported by textual evidence, reflecting the Hanafi commitment to grounding rulings in primary sources.

Guided Path
1
List the six shurut
Identify each condition from the passage: (1) deceased Muslim, (2) deceased pure, (3) deceased in front, (4) presence of most of body or half with head, (5) worshipper not riding without excuse, (6) deceased on ground.
These are shurut (external prerequisites), not arkan (integral parts).
2
Examine the proof for each
For each condition, note the specific proof cited: Quran 9:84 for Islam, hadith of washing for purity, practice of Companions for presence, etc.
The passage uses Quran, hadith, and athar as evidence.
3
Identify the Hanafi uniqueness
Condition 3 (presence of deceased) is distinctly Hanafi — other schools permit salat al-gha'ib generally. Understand the reasoning and the exception for Negus.
Cross-madhhab difference is significant.
4
Understand the ruling on riding
Condition 5 shows interplay of qiyas and obligation of standing. Without excuse, riding invalidates prayer because it omits the obligatory qiyam.
Analogy (qiyas) suggests permissibility, but the requirement of standing overrides.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a hypothetical funeral, check each condition. For example: deceased is non-Muslim? Do not pray. Deceased is impure? Must wash first, etc.
Practical application solidifies understanding.

Source Text

بات ہے۔ وجه : قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ سواری پر نماز جنازہ جائز ہے اسکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال رأيـت الـحـسـن يصلى على جنازة أبي رجاء العطاردي على حمار . مصنف ابن ابي شبيبة ، باب ے ے، فی الرجل والمرأة يصلى على الجنازة وهو راكب ، ج ثانی ص ۴۸۵، نمبر ۱۱۳۳۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گدھے پر سوار ہو کر جنازے کی نماز پڑھی۔ (۲) سواری پر نماز پڑھے گا تو قیام کو چھوڑنا پڑے گا جو فرض ہے اس لئے بغیر عذر کے سواری پر نماز نہ پڑھے۔ ترجمه : (۹۱۱)[۶] میت زمین پر ہو۔ پس اگر چوپائے پر ہو یالوگوں کے ہاتھ پر ہوتو مختار مذہب کے مطابق نماز جائز نہیں
Chapter on Prayer. Its conditions are six. (906) Islam of the deceased (907) its purity (908) its being in front (909) its presence or presence of most of its body or half of it with its head (910) that the one praying over it is not riding without an excuse (911) that the deceased is on the ground. For Janazah prayer there are 6 conditions: at a glance: 1. The deceased is Muslim. 2. It (the deceased) is pure. 3. It is in front. 4. The entire bier or most of it or half with the head is present. 5. The one praying over it is not riding without excuse. 6. The deceased is on the ground. Translation: (906) [1] The deceased being Muslim. Explanation: The conditions for Janazah prayer are six, among them the first condition is that the deceased is Muslim; then Janazah prayer will be performed. If he is apparently a disbeliever, his Janazah prayer will not be performed. Proof: (1) "And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave. Indeed they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger and died while they were defiantly disobedient." (Quran 9:84) This verse indicates that the hypocrite is a disbeliever, so do not pray over him. Translation: (907) [2] Its purity. Explanation: If it is known that the deceased is impure, then Janazah prayer will not be performed. Proof: (1) In a hadith: from Umm Atiyyah (may Allah be pleased with her) who said, "The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) entered upon us when his daughter died and said, 'Wash her three times, or five times, or more than that if you see fit, with water and sidr, and put camphor in the last wash.'" (Bukhari, no. 1253) And in another hadith he said, "Begin with her right side and the places of wudu." (Bukhari, chapter of washing the deceased, and his wudu with water and sidr, p. 201, no. 1254; Muslim, chapter of washing the deceased, p. 1378, no. 2168/939) This indicates that she should be washed. Translation: (908) [3] Its being in front. Explanation: The Hanafi position is that if the deceased is in front, Janazah prayer is performed; if not, the absent (gha'ib) prayer is not performed. And the absent prayer of the Negus was performed as an exception. Proof: (1) If absent prayer were permissible, then many Companions passed away and their prayer would have been performed until today, but it is not done, so we do not have absent prayer. (2) In this hadith: from Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) who said, "Jibril (peace be upon him) descended and said, 'O Muhammad, Mu'awiyah ibn Mu'awiyah al-Muzani has died. Do you wish to pray over him?' He said, 'Yes.' Then Jibril struck with his wing until no tree or mound remained except it was leveled, and his bier was raised until he saw him, and he prayed over him with two rows of angels behind him, each row seventy thousand angels." (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter of prayer over the absent deceased with intention, vol. 4, p. 84, no. 7033) This hadith shows that the bier was brought before his eyes and he prayed, indicating that the bier is in front. Translation: (909) [3] The entire bier is present, or most of the body is present, or half with the head is present. Explanation: Here the principle is stated that as much of the deceased's body must be present that gives the sense that the deceased is present; then only will Janazah prayer be performed over it. For example, if only a leg or a hand is present, prayer will not be performed, because it is not called a deceased. Now three cases are mentioned: [1] The entire bier is present, [2] Most of the bier is present, [3] Half is present but with the head; the head is considered the source, so the bier is considered present, hence prayer will be performed. Proof: If half with the head is present, prayer is performed, and for this there is a Companion's practice: from Khalid ibn Ma'dan that Abu 'Ubaydah prayed over heads. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated regarding washing the limbs... and prayer over it, vol. 4, p. 27, no. 6826) Translation: (910) [5] The one praying over it is not riding without an excuse. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that Janazah prayer, in one respect, is only supplication, so analogy requires that it can be performed while riding. In another respect, it is prayer because it has tahrimah (opening takbir) and standing, so it should not be performed while riding. However, if there is an excuse, it is different. Proof: Analogy requires that Janazah prayer while riding is permissible; its evidence is this practice: He said, "I saw al-Hasan praying over the Janazah of Abu Raja' al-'Utaridi while on a donkey." (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man and woman praying over the Janazah while riding, vol. 2, p. 485, no. 11336) This practice indicates that he prayed over the Janazah while riding a donkey. (2) If he prays while riding, he would have to leave standing, which is obligatory, so without excuse he should not pray while riding. Translation: (911) [6] The deceased is on the ground. So if it is on an animal or on people's hands, then according to the preferred school, prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof presentation of the six conditions (shurut) for the validity of Salat al-Janazah according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by listing the six conditions: (1) the deceased is Muslim, (2) the deceased is ritually pure (tahir), (3) the deceased is in front of the worshipper, (4) the entire body or most of it or half with the head is present, (5) the worshipper is not riding without an excuse, and (6) the deceased is on the ground. Each condition is then explained with a proof from the Quran, Hadith, or practice of the Companions. The first condition is proven by Quran 9:84, which prohibits praying over disbelievers. The second condition is proven by the hadith of washing the deceased, indicating that purification is necessary. The third condition regarding the presence of the deceased is a distinct Hanafi position; the author argues that absent (gha'ib) prayer is not generally permissible, citing the practice of the Companions and a hadith about Mu'awiyah ibn Mu'awiyah where the bier was brought before the Prophet (peace be upon him). The fourth condition specifies how much of the body must be present: the entire body, most of it, or half with the head. The proof is a practice of Abu 'Ubaydah praying over heads. The fifth condition about not riding is explained by a conflict between qiyas (analogy) that allows riding since Janazah prayer is partly supplication, and the requirement of standing which is an obligatory part of prayer. The author resolves that without excuse, riding invalidates the prayer, citing the practice of al-Hasan al-Basri who prayed while riding on a donkey but noting that standing is obligatory. The sixth condition requires the deceased to be on the ground; if on an animal or held, the prayer is invalid according to the relied-upon position. The passage emphasizes that these conditions are specific to the Hanafi school and are supported by textual evidence.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition that must be fulfilled before the prayer is valid; if any shart is missing, the prayer is invalid.
ميت (mayyit): The deceased person over whom Janazah prayer is performed.
غائبانہ نماز (gha'ibana namaz): Janazah prayer performed in the absence of the deceased's body; Hanafis generally do not permit it except in exceptional cases like the Negus.
راكب (rakib): One who is riding on an animal or vehicle while performing Janazah prayer; without excuse, it is not allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six conditions for Salat al-Janazah according to the Hanafi school?
A) The deceased is Muslim.
B) The deceased is ritually pure.
C) The deceased is of sound mind before death.
D) The deceased is on the ground.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires six specific pre-conditions for Janazah prayer, each supported by a clear proof from Quran, Sunnah, or Companion practice, and missing any one invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Conditions for Janazah Prayer
States three conditions with proofs and chosen view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer in the Hanafi school and identify the proof (athar) for the condition regarding presence of the deceased.

Core Idea
Three conditions must be met for janazah prayer—deceased present, worshipper not riding, deceased on ground—unless an excuse exists.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a collective obligation, but its validity depends on specific conditions. This passage from the Hanafi matn presents three essential conditions, with proofs from Companion practice and the chosen view (mukhtar). Understanding these conditions ensures the prayer is performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the passage and list the three conditions mentioned: 1) presence of the deceased's body, 2) the one praying not riding without excuse, 3) the deceased on the ground.
The passage repeats condition 1 and 3; they are distinct conditions.
2
Understand the threshold for presence
For condition 1, note that the entire body, most of the body, or half with the head suffices. A single limb is insufficient. The head is considered the basis.
The evidence for half with head comes from Abu Ubayda's practice.
3
Analyze the riding condition
Condition 2 prohibits riding without excuse because janazah prayer includes standing which is obligatory. Analogy (qiyas) from supplication would permit riding, but the prayer aspect overrides.
The proof from Hasan al-Basri riding a donkey shows exception with excuse.
4
Examine the ground condition
Condition 3 requires the deceased to be on the ground or something like it. If on an animal or carried on hands, the prayer is invalid according to the chosen view unless an excuse exists.
The term 'mukhtar' indicates this is the relied-upon position.
5
Recognize the role of excuses
Each condition can be waived in case of a valid excuse (udhr). The text explicitly allows exceptions.
What constitutes an excuse is determined by later fiqh works.

Source Text

فصل في الصلوة (۹۰۹) وكون الميت على الارض فان كان على دابة او على ايدى الناس لم تجز الصلوة على المختار الا من عذر . (۹۱۰) وكون المصلى عليها غير راكب بلا عذر . (۹۱۱) وكون الميت على الارض فان كان على دابة او على ايدى الناس لم تجز الصلوة على المختار الا من عذر . ترجمه : (۹۰۹) [۳] پوری نعش حاضر ہو، یا بدن کا اکثر حصہ حاضر ہو، یاسر کے ساتھ آدھا حصہ حاضر ہو۔ تشریح : یہاں یہ اصول بتا رہے ہیں کہ میت کی اتنی لاش موجود ہو جس سے محسوس ہوتا ہو کہ میت موجود ہے تب ہی اس پر نماز جنازہ ہوگی ،مثلا ایک ٹانگ ہے یا ایک ہاتھ موجود ہے تو اس پر نماز نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ اس کو میت نہیں کہتے ۔ اب اس کی تین صورتیں بتا رہے ہیں [1] پوری نفش موجود ہو [۲] یانش کا اکثر حصہ موجود ہو ۔ [۳] آدھا حصہ موجود ہو لیکن اس کے ساتھ سر بھی ہو تو سر کو اصل مانا جاتا ہے اس لئے گویا کہ نفش موجود ہے اس لئے اب اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی۔ وجه : آدھے کے ساتھ سر ہو تو نماز پڑھی جائے گی اس کے لئے یہ عمل صحابی ہے۔ عن خالد بن معدان ان ابا عبيدة صلى على رؤوس ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب ما ورد فی غسل الاعضاء... والصلاۃ علیہ ، ج رابع ص ۲۷، نمبر ۶۸۲۶) ترجمه : (۹۱۰) [۵] اس پر نماز پڑھنے والا بلا عذر سوار نہ ہو۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ نماز جنازہ ایک اعتبار سے صرف دعاء ہے اس لئے قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ سواری کی حالت میں بھی پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔ اور ایک اعتبار سے نماز ہے کیونکہ اس میں تحریمہ ہے، قیام ہے اس لئے سواری پر نہیں ہونی چاہیئے ہاں عذر ہو تو اور بات ہے۔ وجه : قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ سواری پر نماز جنازہ جائز ہے اسکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال رأيـت الـحـسـن يصلى على جنازة أبي رجاء العطاردي على حمار . مصنف ابن ابي شبيبة ، باب ے ے، فی الرجل والمرأة يصلى على الجنازة وهو راكب ، ج ثانی ص ۴۸۵، نمبر ۱۱۳۳۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گدھے پر سوار ہو کر جنازے کی نماز پڑھی۔ (۲) سواری پر نماز پڑھے گا تو قیام کو چھوڑنا پڑے گا جو فرض ہے اس لئے بغیر عذر کے سواری پر نماز نہ پڑھے۔ ترجمه : (۹۱۱)[۶] میت زمین پر ہو۔ پس اگر چوپائے پر ہو یالوگوں کے ہاتھ پر ہوتو مختار مذہب کے مطابق نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی ،مگر عذر سے۔ تشریح : میت زمین پر ہو یا ایسی چیز پر ہو جو زمین کی طرح ہے تو نماز جائز ہے، چنانچہ اگر سواری پر ہو یا لوگوں کے ہاتھوں پر ہو تو مختار مذہب کے مطابق نماز جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہاں سواری پر رکھنے میں یا لوگوں کے ہاتھوں پر رکھنے میں عذر ہو تو جائز ہے۔
Chapter on prayer. (909) And the deceased being on the ground; if on an animal or on people's hands, the prayer is not permissible according to the chosen view except due to an excuse. (910) And the one praying not being a rider without an excuse. (911) And the deceased being on the ground; if on an animal or on people's hands, the prayer is not permissible according to the chosen view except due to an excuse. Translation: (909) [3] The entire bier is present, or most of the body is present, or half with the head. Explanation: Here the principle is that enough of the corpse must be present to indicate the deceased is present; for example, if only a leg or hand is present, prayer is not performed because it is not called a deceased. The three cases: [1] whole bier present, [2] most of the body present, [3] half present with the head; the head is considered the basis so the prayer is performed. Proof: for half with head, the practice of a Companion: from Khalid ibn Mi'dan that Abu Ubaydah prayed over heads. (Sunan Bayhaqi...) Translation: (910) [5] The one praying over it should not be riding without an excuse. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that the funeral prayer is in one sense merely a supplication so analogy permits riding, but in another sense it is a prayer with takbir and standing so riding is not allowed without an excuse. Proof: Analogy permits with the effect that al-Hasan prayed on a donkey. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) Also, riding would omit standing which is obligatory, so without excuse he should not pray riding. Translation: (911) [6] The deceased be on the ground. So if on an animal or on people's hands, according to the chosen view the prayer is not valid except due to an excuse. Explanation: The deceased must be on the ground or something like it; if on an animal or in people's hands, it is not valid according to the chosen view unless there is an excuse.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proofs explaining three conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer in the Hanafi school. First condition (909): The deceased's body must be sufficiently present. At least most of the body, or half with the head, must be present. A single limb is not enough. The author cites the practice of Abu Ubayda praying over heads as evidence. Second condition (910): The imam and congregation should not be riding without an excuse. While funeral prayer is like a supplication, it also includes acts of prayer like takbir and standing, so riding is not allowed unless there is a valid reason. The author mentions that al-Hasan al-Basri prayed on a donkey, indicating permissible with an excuse. Third condition (911): The deceased must be placed on the ground, not on an animal or carried on hands, except for an excuse. The chosen (mukhtar) view in the madhhab is that it is not valid otherwise. These conditions ensure the prayer is performed with proper respect and focus.

Key Terms
حذاء (hudha'): Opposite, facing (used for imam's position relative to deceased).
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred view in the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because any part represents the deceased.
B) No, because the body must be mostly present or half with head.
C) Yes, if there is an excuse.
D) Only if the leg is more than half the body.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is only valid when the body is sufficiently present (most or half with head), the worshipper is not riding, and the deceased is on the ground, unless an excuse exists.

The Imam's Position in the Janazah Prayer: Standing Opposite the Chest
Lists four sunnahs of funeral prayer and explains the first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnahs of the janazah prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling that the imam stands opposite the chest for both male and female deceased.

Core Idea
The imam stands at the chest of the deceased to testify to the light of faith within.

This passage enumerates the four sunnah acts of the funeral prayer and elaborates on the first: the imam's placement. Understanding this position is a practical lesson in following the Prophet's practice and the Hanafi method of reconciling multiple proof texts.

Guided Path
1
List the four sunnahs
Identify the four sunnahs mentioned in the passage: imam's position, thana, salawat, and dua for the deceased.
These are sunnah mu'akkadah; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Focus on the first sunnah
Isolate the ruling: the imam stands opposite the chest (sadr) of the deceased, whether male or female.
The word 'hudha' means opposite, directly facing.
3
Examine the first proof
Analyze the athar of 'Ata: 'When a man prays over the deceased, he stands at the chest.' This is explicit support.
This is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Examine the second proof
Analyze the hadith of Samurah: the Prophet stood 'in her middle' for a woman who died in childbirth.
Reported by Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
5
Reconcile the proofs
Understand the Hanafi reconciliation: 'middle' refers to the chest area, as the chest contains the light of faith and is the central part of the body.
This shows the principle of jam' al-adillah (harmonizing evidence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسننها اربعه (۹۱۲) قيام الامام بـحـذاء صدر الميت ذكرا كان أو أنثى (۹۱۳) والثناء بعد التكبيرة الاولى ..... دوسری تکبیر کے بعد رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر دورد پڑھنا. ..... تیسری تکبیر کے بعد میت کے لئے دعا کرنا. ترجمه : (۹۱۲) [۱] میت خواہ مرد ہو یا عورت ہوا مام اس کے سینے کے برابر کھڑا ہو۔ تشریح : نماز جنازہ میں چار سنتیں ہیں، ان میں سے ایک سنت یہ ہے کہ امام مرد کے اور عورت کے سینے کے برابر میں کھڑا ہو۔۔ حذاء: کا معنی ہے سامنے۔ وجه (۱) سینہ کے پاس کھڑے ہونے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے ۔ عن عطاء قال اذا صلى الرجل على الجنازة قام عند الصدر (مصنف بن ابی شیبة ۱۰۲، فى المرأة ابن يقام منها فى الصلوة والرجل على الجنازة اين تقام منهج ثالث ص ۶ نمبر ۱ ۱۵۵ار مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب اين يقوم الامام من الجنازة ج ثالث ص ۳۳۰ نمبر ۶۳۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کے سینہ کے پاس کھڑا ہونا چاہئے (۲) اس لئے بھی کہ سینہ میں نور ایمان ہے تو وہاں کھڑے ہو کر گویا کہ نور ایمان کی گواہی دینا ہے۔ اور اسکی شفارس کر رہا ہے۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت کے درمیان کھڑا ہو۔ حدثنا سمرة بن جندب قال صليت وراء النبي لة على امرأة ماتت في نفاسها فقام عليها وسطها (بخاری شریف، باب این یقوم من المرأة والرجل صے سے انمبر ۱۳۱ر مسلم شریف ، باب این یقوم الامام من البيت للصلاة علیه، ص ۱۳۸۸ نمبر ۲۲۳۵/۹۶۴ را ابو داود شریف ، باب این یقوم الامام)
And its sunnahs are four. (912) The imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, be it male or female. (913) And the thana (praise) after the first takbir. ... After the second takbir, sending blessings upon the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ). ... After the third takbir, making supplication for the deceased. Translation: (912) [1] Whether the deceased is male or female, the imam stands opposite his/her chest. Explanation: The funeral prayer has four sunnahs; one of them is that the imam stands opposite the chest of the male and female. 'Hudha' means opposite. Proof: (1) The evidence for standing near the chest is the athar from 'Ata: when a man prays over the deceased, he stands at the chest. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) (2) Also because the chest contains the light of faith, so standing there testifies to that light and intercedes for it. (3) There is a hadith that he stood in the middle of a woman: Samurah ibn Jundub prayed behind the Prophet (ﷺ) over a woman who died in childbirth, and he stood opposite her middle. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof enumerating the four sunnah acts of the janazah prayer and elaborating on the first one. The four sunnahs are: (1) the imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, (2) reciting thana (praise) after the first takbir, (3) sending salawat upon the Prophet after the second takbir, and (4) making dua for the deceased after the third takbir. The author focuses on the first sunnah, providing two proofs: the athar of 'Ata that the imam stands at the chest, and the hadith of Samurah where the Prophet (ﷺ) stood in the middle of a female deceased. The Hanafi school reconciles these by considering the chest as the primary location for males and females, with the 'middle' referring to the chest area. The commentary also gives a spiritual reason: the chest houses the light of faith, and standing there is like witnessing and interceding for that light.

Key Terms
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts that the Prophet (ﷺ) regularly performed; omission does not invalidate.
صدر (sadr): Chest; the physical location where the imam stands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the imam stand when leading the funeral prayer for a female deceased?
A) At her head.
B) At her feet.
C) Opposite her chest.
D) In the middle of her body.

Key Takeaway
The imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female, as the sunnah position in the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer

Sunan of Janazah Prayer and Location Ruling
Ruling on location and list of four sunan with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan of the janazah prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the condition regarding the location of the deceased.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer has four confirmed sunan; the deceased must be on ground unless excused.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh textbook first establishes a key condition for the janazah prayer: it must be performed with the deceased on the ground or a surface like the ground. Then it enumerates the four recommended acts (sunan) within the prayer, each supported by textual evidence from hadith and the practice of early Muslims. Understanding these details ensures the prayer is performed in accordance with the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on location
The passage begins by stating that if the deceased is on an animal or carried on people's hands, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen (mukhtar) position, unless there is a valid excuse. This is the mufta bihi ruling.
The phrase 'ala al-mukhtar' signals that this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.
2
List the four sunan
The text explicitly says 'wa sunanuha arba'ah' and then lists: (1) imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased, (2) reciting thana' after the first takbir, (3) sending durood upon the Prophet after the second takbir, and (4) making du'a for the deceased after the third takbir.
These sunan are mu'akkadah (confirmed) but not obligatory; missing them reduces perfection.
3
Examine the evidence for the imam's position
The commentary cites an athar from 'Ata' that the imam should stand at the chest, and a hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet stood at the middle of a woman's body (to screen her). The Hanafi preference for chest is based on these narrations and the idea that the chest contains the light of faith.
4
Examine the evidence for the sequence of recitations
The hadith of the Prophet praying over the Najashi with four takbirs provides the basis for the number. Athar from al-Sha'bi and the practice of Abu Hurairah specify the order: thana', durood, du'a, then taslim after the fourth takbir.
The fourth takbir is not part of the sunan; it is followed by the taslim (salam).
5
Understand the flexibility in the du'a
The text says no specific du'a is required; the transmitted (ma'thur) du'a is best. It quotes the well-known du'a from 'Awf ibn Malik as an example.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that the du'a for the deceased is recommended but not restricted to one wording.

Chapter on Prayer. The ground: if it is on an animal or on the hands of people, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen position except due to an excuse. Its sunan are four: (912) The imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, male or female. (913) And the praise after the first takbir, and the prayer upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the second, and the supplication for the deceased after the third. (914) And nothing specific is prescribed for it, and if he supplicates with the transmitted supplication, it is better and more effective, including what ‘Awf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his lodging, expand his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail...'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi fiqh textbook. It first states a ruling: the janazah prayer must be performed with the deceased on the ground or a surface like the ground (e.g., a bier on the ground) to be valid; if on an animal or carried on people's hands, it is not valid unless there is a valid excuse (like fear or necessity). This is the relied-upon position (mukhtar). Then it enumerates the four sunan (recommended acts) of the janazah prayer according to the Hanafi school: (1) the imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female, (2) reciting the thana' (glorification of Allah) after the first takbir, (3) sending blessings (durood) upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the second takbir, and (4) making supplication for the deceased after the third takbir. The fourth sunan is less strictly defined; any supplication suffices, but the transmitted (ma'thur) supplication is best—the author quotes the well-known du'a from 'Awf ibn Malik. The passage then provides proofs (wajh) for these sunan, citing athar (sayings of the Companions/Tabi'in) and hadith. For the imam's position, it cites the practice of 'Ata' and a hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub. For the sequence of takbirs and recitations, it cites the hadith of the Prophet's prayer over the Najashi (Negus) with four takbirs, the saying of al-Sha'bi, and the practice of Abu Hurairah. The author follows the Hanafi madhhab throughout.

Key Terms
الصلوة على الميت (al-salat 'ala al-mayyit): The funeral prayer performed for a deceased Muslim, consisting of four takbirs, standing, with specific recitations and supplications.
السنة (al-sunnah): In this context, the recommended acts (sunan) within the janazah prayer, not obligatory but rewardable.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or relied-upon position of the Hanafi madhhab for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The janazah prayer has four confirmed sunan and requires the deceased to be on the ground or similar unless excused.

Salah — Prayer

Actions After Each Takbir in Salat al-Janazah
Explains the sunnah actions after each of the four takbirs in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions after each of the four takbirs in Salat al-Janazah and identify the evidence from the Sunnah that supports them.

Core Idea
Four takbirs in janazah prayer: after first thana, after second darood, after third dua, after fourth salam.

This lesson explains the specific actions prescribed after each takbir in the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school. The Prophet's practice and the statements of early authorities establish that each takbir is followed by a distinct act. We will examine the textual proofs and the recommended supplications, ensuring our prayer aligns with the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the four takbirs
Begin by understanding that the Hanafi school considers the four takbirs in Salat al-Janazah as wajib. The specific actions after each are sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
List the actions after each takbir
Memorize the sequence: after first takbir: thana (praise of Allah); after second: darood (salutations upon the Prophet); after third: dua (supplication for the deceased); after fourth: salam (greeting of peace).
3
Examine the primary dalil
Read the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet made four takbirs over an-Najashi. This is the core evidence for the number of takbirs.
Hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari.
4
Analyze the supporting athar
Consider the statement of ash-Sha'bi and the narration of Abu Hurairah that explicitly specify the actions after each takbir. Recognize that these athar provide the details of the sequence.
From Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Understand the Hanafi position on the fourth takbir
According to zahir al-riwayah, after the fourth takbir one should not recite any supplication or Surah al-Fatihah, but only make the salam. This is because the dua has already been performed after the third takbir.

من أحييته منا فأحيه على الايمان و من توفيته منا فتوفه على الاسلام الايمان ، اللهم ! لا تحرمنا أجره و لا تضلنا بعدہ ۔ ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الدعاء للمیت ،ص ۴۶۸، نمبر ۳۲۰ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما يقول في الصلوة على الميت ،ص ۱۹۸، نمبر ۱۰۲۴) اس حدیث میں وہ دعاء کی عبارت ہے جو نماز جنازہ کی تیسری تکبیر کے بعد پڑھتے ہیں۔ ۔ اس کے علاوہ بھی دعاء پڑھے گا تو دعا ادا ہو جائے گی۔ ترجمه : (۹۱۵) اور چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد ظاہر روایت میں بغیر دعا کے سلام پھیر دے۔ تشریح: میت کے لئے دعا تیسری تکبیر کے بعد ہو چکی ہے اس لئے چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد دعا نہیں کرے گا، اور نہ سورہ فاتحہ پڑھے گا۔ وجه : (۱) عن الشعبي قال : التكبيرة الاولى على الميت ثناء على الله ، و الثانية صلاة على النبى الله الله ، الثالثة دعاء للميت ، و الرابعة تسليم ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القراءة والدعاء فی الصلوۃ علی لمیت ، ج ثالث ،ص۳۱۶، نمبر ۶۴۶۲ /مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب ۸۴، ما بدأ به بالتكبير الاولى في الصلاة عليه والثانية والثالثة والرابعة ، ج ثانی ص ۴۹۰، نمبر ۱۱۳۷۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ چوتھی کے بعد سلام پھیرے۔
Chapter on prayer: And the salutation upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, after the second [takbir], and supplication for the deceased after the third [takbir]. Nothing specific is prescribed for him, and if he supplicates with what is transmitted, that is better and more effective. Among it is what 'Auf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his resting place, widen his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail, purify him from sins as a white garment is purified from filth, and give him a house better than his house, a family better than his family, a spouse better than his spouse, admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the torment of the grave and the torment of the Fire.' And he makes salutations after the fourth rak'ah. Explanation: In funeral prayer, four takbirs are said. After the first, recite thana; after the second, send blessings on the Prophet; after the third, recite the funeral supplication; and after the fourth takbir, make salutations. Evidence: (1) From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah announced the death of an-Najashi on the day he died, and went out with them to the prayer place, arranged them in rows, and made four takbirs over him. This hadith indicates that four takbirs are said in funeral prayer. (2) From ash-Sha'bi: 'The first takbir over the deceased is praise of Allah, the second is prayer upon the Prophet, the third is supplication for the deceased, and the fourth is salutations.' This athar shows that after the first takbir is thana, after the second is darood, after the third is dua for the deceased, and after the fourth is salam. (3) Someone asked Abu Hurairah how to pray over the deceased, and he said: 'By Allah, I will inform you: Follow it with its people; when they place it [the deceased], you say takbir, praise Allah, send blessings on His Prophet, then say: O Allah, Your servant and the son of Your servant...' This athar shows thana after the first takbir, darood after the second, and dua for the deceased after the third. Translation (914): And nothing specific is prescribed for him; if he supplicates with transmitted supplications, that is better and more effective. For example, what 'Auf ibn Malik learned from the Messenger of Allah: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his resting place, widen his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail, purify him from sins as a white garment is purified from filth, and give him a house better than his house, a family better than his family, a spouse better than his spouse, admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the torment of the grave and the torment of the Fire.' According to the Hanafis, generally for adults this supplication is recited after the third takbir. From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah prayed over a deceased and said: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our young and our old, our males and our females, our present and our absent. O Allah, those of us whom You keep alive, keep them alive upon faith, and those of us whom You take, take them upon Islam/faith. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not lead us astray after him.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). This supplication is also recited after the third takbir. If one recites another supplication, it will be valid. Translation (915): And after the fourth takbir, according to zahir ar-riwayah, he makes salams without supplication. Explanation: The supplication for the deceased has already been done after the third takbir, so after the fourth he should not supplicate nor recite Surah al-Fatihah. Evidence: (1) From ash-Sha'bi: The first takbir over the deceased is praise of Allah, the second is prayer upon the Prophet, the third is supplication for the deceased, and the fourth is salutation. This athar indicates that after the fourth is salam.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the actions performed after each of the four takbirs in Salat al-Janazah. It begins by stating the ruling: after the first takbir, one recites thana (praise of Allah); after the second, salam upon the Prophet (darood); after the third, dua for the deceased; and after the fourth, the salam greeting. The author then provides the evidence for the four takbirs from the hadith of Abu Hurairah regarding the Prophet's prayer over an-Najashi (the Negus), which is the primary proof for the number of takbirs. Next, he cites the statement of the tabi'i ash-Sha'bi, which specifies the actions after each takbir. He also mentions another narration from Abu Hurairah describing the procedure. Regarding the dua, the passage explains that no specific form is prescribed; any supplication is acceptable, but using transmitted (ma'thur) supplications is best. It gives the famous dua narrated by 'Auf ibn Malik and the one from Abu Hurairah. The Hanafi position is that for adults, the dua of 'Auf is commonly recited. The passage concludes that according to zahir ar-riwayah (the well-known transmission), after the fourth takbir one should not recite any supplication or Fatihah, but directly say salam. The evidence is again from ash-Sha'bi's statement that the fourth takbir is for taslim. All rulings are based on the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' in the funeral prayer; four takbirs are sunnah mu'akkadah.
ثناء (thana): Praise of Allah, typically 'Subhanakallahumma...', recited after the first takbir.
دعاء ماثور (dua ma'thur): Supplication transmitted from the Prophet, preferred for use after the third takbir.
درود (darood): Blessings upon the Prophet (e.g., 'Allahumma salli ala Muhammad') recited after the second takbir.
تسليم (taslim): The greeting of peace (salam) that concludes the prayer, performed after the fourth takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Surah al-Fatihah
B) Thana (praise of Allah)
C) Darood (salutations upon the Prophet)
D) Supplication for the deceased

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes specific sunnah actions after each of the four takbirs in funeral prayer, with the fourth takbir being solely for salam.

No Supplication After the Fourth Takbir in Janazah Prayer
Ruling to not make dua after fourth takbir in janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the fourth takbir in janazah prayer and explain the evidence from the athar of al-Sha'bi.

Core Idea
The fourth takbir is for salam only, not for dua — the supplication ends after the third.

In the Janazah prayer, the four takbirat each have a distinct purpose. This lesson clarifies what should be done after the fourth takbir: according to the Hanafi school, the time for supplication is after the third takbir, and after the fourth, one simply says the salam. This ruling is supported by the practice of the early generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? After the fourth takbir, the ruling is to give salam and refrain from any supplication or recitation.
The ruling is a sunnah muakkadah, meaning it is a highly recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof comes from an athar (report) of al-Sha'bi (may Allah have mercy on him), recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
The athar is a saying of a tabi'i, which in Hanafi usul is considered a valid source (qawl sahabi) when there is no contrary evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar explicitly assigns each takbir a purpose: first takbir is praise of Allah, second is salawat, third is dua for the deceased, and fourth is salam. The fourth takbir is thus designated for salam only, not for additional dua.
This explicit assignment shows that the fourth takbir is the closing, and any additional supplication would be contrary to its intended purpose.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'is) allow or recommend supplication after the fourth takbir. However, the Hanafi school relies on the athar and the principle that the supplication for the deceased is completed after the third takbir.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether one may raise hands for dua after the fourth takbir.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the Zahir al-Riwayah position, which is the most authoritative transmitted opinion. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and others confirm that the mufta bihi is to give salam without supplication.
The ruling is not overridden by istihsan, and the dalal of the athar is considered sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۱۵) اور چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد ظاہر روایت میں بغیر دعا کے سلام پھیر دے۔ تشریح: میت کے لئے دعا تیسری تکبیر کے بعد ہو چکی ہے اس لئے چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد دعا نہیں کرے گا، اور نہ سورہ فاتحہ پڑھے گا ۔  و  صلى الله وجه : (۱) عن الشعبي قال : التكبيرة الاولى على الميت ثناء على الله ، و الثانية صلاة على النبى الله الله ، الثالثة دعاء للميت ، و الرابعة تسليم ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القراءة والدعاء فی الصلوۃ علی لمیت ، ج ثالث ،ص۳۱۶، نمبر ۶۴۶۲ /مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب ۸۴، ما بدأ به بالتكبير الاولى في الصلاة عليه والثانية والثالثة والرابعة ، ج ثانی ص ۴۹۰، نمبر ۱۱۳۷۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ چوتھی کے بعد سلام پھیرے۔ من غير دعاء في ظاهر الرواية
Translation: (915) And after the fourth takbir, according to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), he should give salam without supplication. Explanation: The supplication for the deceased has already been made after the third takbir, so after the fourth takbir he should not make supplication, nor recite Surah al-Fatihah. And the Prophet ﷺ said: (1) From al-Sha'bi: The first takbir over the deceased is praise of Allah, the second is salutation upon the Prophet ﷺ, the third is supplication for the deceased, and the fourth is salutation. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on recitation and supplication in janazah prayer, vol. 3, p. 316, no. 6462 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter 84, what is begun with the first takbir... vol. 2, p. 490, no. 11375) In this effect, he gives salam after the fourth. Without supplication in the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof about the procedure after the fourth takbir in janazah prayer. The author states the relied-upon position from Zahir al-Riwayah: after the fourth takbir, one should immediately give salam without any supplication. The explanation clarifies that the supplication for the deceased has already been completed after the third takbir; therefore, adding more supplication or reciting Surah al-Fatihah after the fourth takbir is not appropriate. The proof is the athar of al-Sha'bi, which outlines the purpose of each takbir: the first is praise of Allah, the second is salawat on the Prophet, the third is supplication for the deceased, and the fourth is closing with salam. This indicates that the fourth takbir is solely for the purpose of leaving the prayer, not for additional requests. The phrase 'without supplication in the apparent narration' confirms that this is the rule in the well-known transmitted texts of the school.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' in the funeral prayer; each takbir marks a distinct part of the prayer.
ظاہر الروایة (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known transmitted rulings of Imam Muhammad from Imam Abu Hanifa and the two shaykhs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After the third takbir
B) After the fourth takbir without supplication
C) After the fourth takbir with supplication
D) After reciting Surah al-Fatihah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the fourth takbir of the Janazah prayer is exclusively for the salam, and no supplication should follow it.

Raising Hands in Janazah: Only the First Takbir
Rule statement restricting hand-raising to first takbir in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands in the funeral prayer and distinguish it from the Shafi'i practice.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer for the deceased, hands are raised only at the first takbir.

This lesson addresses a specific element of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah): the raising of hands (raf' al-yadayn). While in regular prayers hands are raised at multiple points, the janazah prayer has its own distinct practice. The Hanafi school follows a particular sunnah in this regard, and it is important to know the correct practice to avoid acting against the established sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses raising hands in salat al-janazah. The ruling is that it is sunnah to raise hands only at the first takbir.
2
Locate the basis
Understand that the first takbir is takbirat al-ihram, which commences the prayer.
3
Note the restriction
The text explicitly prohibits raising hands in any other takbir.
4
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school raises hands in every takbir; this is a practical difference.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a Hanafi will raise hands only at the beginning of the janazah prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٩١٦ ) ولا يرفع يديه في غير التكبيرة الاولى ترجمه : (۹۱۶) اور تکبیر اولی کے سوا کسی دوسری تکبیر میں ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے۔ تشریح : پہلی تکبیر میں ہاتھ اٹھائے کیونکہ یہ تکبیر تحریمہ ہے، اس کے علاوہ تکبیر میں ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے۔
(916) And he should not raise his hands in other than the first takbir. Translation: (916) And he should not raise his hands in any other takbir except the first. Explanation: He should raise his hands in the first takbir because it is the takbirat al-ihram; he should not raise his hands in other takbirs.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This is a clear ruling statement about the practice of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) in the funeral prayer. The author states that hands are raised only in the first takbir, which is the takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir). In all subsequent takbirs (second, third, fourth), the hands remain at the sides. The explanation notes that the first takbir is the one that commences the prayer, hence the raising of hands is associated with it. This is the established Hanafi practice based on the sunnah.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbīrat al-taḥrīmah): The first takbir that initiates the prayer and prohibits actions that were previously permissible.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): The act of raising the hands up to the ears or shoulders during prayer takbirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which takbir of janazah prayer does the Hanafi school require raising the hands?
A) All four takbirs
B) The first and third takbirs
C) Only the first takbir
D) Only the fourth takbir

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi funeral prayer, hands are raised only at the first takbir, which is the takbirat al-ihram.

Imam Says Five Takbirs: To Follow or Wait?
Ruling on whether to follow imam who says five takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when an imam says five takbirs in janazah prayer and identify the proofs that support the preferred position (mukhtar).

Core Idea
The follower should not follow the imam in the fifth takbir but wait for salam.

In janazah prayer, the standard number of takbirs is four. What happens if the imam says five? Does the follower have to follow along, or is there a different rule? This passage from the Hanafi text presents the preferred (mukhtar) position: the follower should not follow the imam in the extra takbir, but wait for his salam. The ruling is rooted in the four-takbir sunnah and the consensus of the Companions, while acknowledging that a fifth takbir is also reported and does not invalidate the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first line of the Arabic passage: what is the instruction regarding the imam's fifth takbir?
The phrase 'لم يُتبع' means 'he is not to be followed' – a clear directive.
2
Locate the evidence for four takbirs
Find the hadith of Abu Huraira and the practice of Umar. These establish the four-takbir norm.
The Prophet's funeral prayer for al-Najashi and the consensus of the Companions on four takbirs are key proofs.
3
Understand the evidence for five takbirs
Find the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam. How does this affect the ruling?
This report shows that the Prophet sometimes said five takbirs; hence the prayer is valid even with five.
4
Analyse the preference (mukhtar)
Why does the school choose the follower to wait rather than follow? Consider the strength of the evidence and the concept of 'mutaba'ah' (following the imam).
The four-takbir practice is more consistent and agreed upon; the fifth is an exception that does not require the follower's imitation.

(917) And if the imam says five takbirs, he should not be followed, but he should wait for his salam according to the chosen view. Translation: (917) And if the imam says five takbirs, he should not be followed, and according to the chosen school, he should wait for his salam. Explanation: According to most imams, there are only four takbirs in janazah, but there is also evidence in hadith for a fifth takbir; therefore, due to hadith, if someone says a fifth takbir, the prayer is not invalidated, and following him also has no harm. However, the chosen school is that one should not follow the imam in the fifth takbir, but wait for his salam and give salam with him. Evidence: (1) Takbirs are only four, for this there is the hadith of Abu Huraira that the Prophet ﷺ announced the death of al-Najashi and led the prayer with four takbirs. (2) Also the hadith of Abu Wa'il that Umar gathered the people and consulted about the number of takbirs; some said five, some seven, some four, and he united them on four. (3) There is evidence for a fifth takbir in the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that he used to say four but once said five and attributed it to the Prophet ﷺ.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses an issue where the imam deviates from the standard four takbirs and says five. The author presents the Hanafi position with the proofs. The ruling: the follower should not follow the imam in adding a fifth takbir; instead, he should wait silently until the imam gives salam, then give salam with him. The explanation clarifies that although four takbirs are the established practice (based on the Prophet's action in the funeral of al-Najashi and the consensus of the Companions led by Umar), a fifth takbir is also reported from some Companions like Zayd ibn Arqam who narrated that the Prophet sometimes said five. Because of this divergent report, if the imam says five, the prayer remains valid. However, the follower is not required to follow in the extra takbir; the preferred position is to wait and join the imam in salam. This illustrates a nuanced approach: maintaining the standard while accommodating a rare sunnah that would otherwise make the prayer valid.

Key Terms
مختار (mukhtār): The preferred or chosen ruling within the Hanafi school after considering all evidences.
اتباع (ittibāʿ): Following the imam in prayer actions.
تكبير (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Follow the imam and say five takbirs.
B) Not follow and leave the congregation.
C) Wait for the imam's salam and then give salam.
D) Recite the prayer again after the imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mukhtar view holds that when an imam says five takbirs, the follower should not follow the extra takbir but wait for salam, because the four-takbir practice is the established sunnah.

Supplication for a Child or Insane Deceased
Ruling on supplication for child/insane deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct supplication for a child or insane person in janazah and explain why istighfar is omitted.

Core Idea
For a sinless deceased, do not ask forgiveness; ask Allah to make them a stored treasure and intercessor.

This passage gives the specific ruling for the supplication in janazah when the deceased is a child or an insane person. The key distinction is that these individuals are not accountable for sins, so the dua focuses on benefiting the living through their intercession and stored reward, rather than seeking forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the supplication for a child or insane person during janazah. The ruling prescribes a specific dua and prohibits asking for forgiveness.
The act is part of janazah prayer (salah al-janazah).
2
Understand the rationale
Recognize why istighfar is not said: children and insane persons are free from sin because they lack accountability. Seeking forgiveness implies sin, which contradicts their status.
This is based on the principle that accountability (taklif) requires sanity and puberty.
3
Memorize the prescribed dua
Learn the Arabic phrases: 'Allahumma aj'alhu lana faratan, wa aj'alhu lana ajran wa dhukhran, wa aj'alhu lana shafi'an wa mushaffa'an'.
The dua asks Allah to make the deceased a precursor, a reward, a stored treasure, and an intercessor.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
When leading or participating in janazah for a child or insane person, recite this dua instead of the usual istighfar. Ensure the congregation is aware of this distinction.
This is a sunnah practice; omitting istighfar is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Translation: (918) And one should not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a child, because they are already forgiven. Rather, one should say: 'O Allah, make him a precursor for us, and make him a reward and a stored treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.'
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling regarding what to say in supplication for a deceased who is a child or an insane person. The author states that one should not ask for forgiveness for them because they are not accountable for sins; they are already forgiven by virtue of being free from sin. Instead, the appropriate dua is to ask Allah to make them a 'farat' (precursor who goes ahead to prepare the way), a reward (ajr), a stored treasure (dhukhur), and an intercessor (shafi') whose intercession is accepted (mushaffa'). This dua is reported from the Prophet ﷺ and is specific to those who die without having reached the age of responsibility or without mental capacity.

Key Terms
فرط (faraṭ): A precursor who goes ahead to prepare a place for the family in Paradise.
ذخر (dhukhur): A stored treasure or reward reserved for the family in the Hereafter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For children and insane persons, the janazah supplication asks Allah to make them a precursor and stored treasure, not forgiveness.

Raising Hands and Following the Imam in Funeral Takbirs
Rulings on hand-raising and following imam in funeral takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands in funeral prayer and explain the correct response when the imam performs five takbirs.

Core Idea
In Hanafi funeral prayer, hands are raised only at the first takbir; if the imam says five, the follower waits for his salam.

This lesson examines two specific rulings related to the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The first concerns when to raise hands during the takbirs. The second addresses a situation where the imam departs from the standard four takbirs. Understanding these rulings helps maintain proper congregational practice within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage gives two rulings: (1) hands are raised only at the first takbir; (2) if the imam says five takbirs, the follower does not follow but waits for the salam.
The first ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah; the second is the chosen (mukhtar) position.
2
Locate the evidence
The passage cites the hadith of Abu Huraira about four takbirs over al-Najashi and the companion practice reported by Umar. These establish the default of four takbirs.
The existence of a fifth takbir in some reports does not override the consensus.
3
Trace the derivation
From the hadith and companion consensus, the Hanafi ruling derives that four takbirs are the sunnah. The first takbir is takbir tahrimah, so hands are raised only there, analogically to the opening takbir in other prayers.
The fifth takbir is considered an exception that does not invalidate but also does not obligate following.
4
Note the intra-school variant
Imam Muhammad holds that hands should be raised at every takbir in janazah, similar to other prayers. However, the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, are given preference.
The text says 'fial-mukhtar' for the second ruling, indicating the relied-upon view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is: hands raised only at first takbir; if imam does five takbirs, wait for his salam and then conclude.
This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on prioritizing the established sunnah and companion consensus.

Without supplication in the apparent narration (916). And he does not raise his hands in other than the first takbir (917). And if the imam says five takbirs, he should not be followed, but rather wait for his salam according to the chosen position.

Translation (916): And he does not raise his hands in any takbir except the first.
Explanation: He raises his hands in the first takbir because it is takbir tahrimah; apart from that, he does not raise hands.
Translation (917): And if the imam says five takbirs, he should not be followed, and according to the chosen school, his salam should be waited for.
Explanation: According to most imams, there are only four takbirs in the funeral prayer, but there is also evidence for a fifth takbir in hadith. Therefore, if someone says a fifth takbir due to hadith, the prayer is not invalidated, and following him is also not problematic. However, the chosen school is that one should not follow the imam in the fifth takbir but rather wait for his salam, and when he says salam, one should say salam with him.
Reasoning: (1) There are four takbirs; for this, there is hadith: From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) announced the death of al-Najashi on the day he died, took them to the prayer ground, lined them up, and said four takbirs over him. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates four takbirs. (2) Also this: From Abu Wa'il: Umar gathered the people and consulted them about takbir over the funeral. Some said the Messenger of Allah said five, some said seven, some said four. He collected them on four takbirs as the longest prayer. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This companion practice shows that the companions reached consensus on four takbirs. (3) There is evidence for the fifth takbir in this hadith, so the prayer is not invalidated: Zaid ibn Arqam used to say four takbirs over our funerals, and he said five over a funeral, so I asked him, and he said the Messenger of Allah used to say them. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi).
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings on the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The first ruling (916) states that the worshipper raises his hands only at the first takbir, which is the takbir tahrimah (opening takbir), and does not raise them at subsequent takbirs. This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah. The second ruling (917) addresses a scenario where the imam performs five takbirs instead of the standard four. The text clarifies that the followers should not follow the imam in the fifth takbir; instead, they should wait for his salam and then conclude their prayer with him. The commentary explains that most imams hold that funeral prayer consists of four takbirs, and this is supported by the hadith of Abu Huraira and the consensus of the Companions as reported by Umar. However, there is also evidence for five takbirs from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Zaid ibn Arqam. Consequently, if an imam performs five takbirs, the prayer remains valid, but the chosen position (mukhtar) is that the follower does not join in the fifth takbir but rather waits. This illustrates the Hanafi approach: while there is evidence for a fifth takbir, the established practice and consensus (ijma) of the Companions on four takbirs is given precedence, making four the standard and five an exception that does not invalidate but also does not require following.

Key Terms
تكبيرة (takbirah): One utterance of Allahu Akbar in prayer; in funeral prayer, there are usually four.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred position within the Hanafi school.
تكبير تحريمة (takbir tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and makes previously permissible actions forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi funeral prayer, hands are raised only at the first takbir, and if the imam performs five takbirs, the follower waits for the salam.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Supplication for a Child and an Insane Person in Funeral Prayer
Ruling with proof from athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the supplication for a child and an insane person in funeral prayer and identify the evidence from the practice of Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
For children and the insane in funeral prayer, ask Allah to make them a precursor, not forgiveness.

In Hanafi fiqh, the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) includes a supplication that varies based on the deceased's age and accountability. For adults, we seek forgiveness; for children and the insane, who are sinless, we instead ask Allah to make them a precursor (farat) and reward for us. This lesson examines the specific supplication and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage gives a ruling about what to say (and what not to say) in funeral prayer for a child or insane person. The act is the recitation of the supplication after takbir. The ruling is that one must not seek forgiveness (istighfar) but should say a specific du'a.
This distinguishes the funeral prayer for children from that for adults.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites two evidence: (1) the practice of Hasan al-Basri transmitted by Abd al-Razzaq; (2) a similar narration in Bukhari. These are atbar (effects) from a tabi'i, which are accepted as hujja in Hanafi fiqh.
Hasan al-Basri was a prominent tabi'i and his practice is considered authoritative.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The evidence shows that Hasan al-Basri would recite al-Fatiha and then say the specific du'a (Allahumma ij'alhu lana farata...). This indicates that the sunnah for a child is to ask for these benefits rather than forgiveness.
The phrase 'for they are already forgiven' implies that seeking forgiveness is inappropriate.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools allow general supplication for children. Hanafis are specific: only the prescribed du'a should be said, and istighfar should be avoided.
This is an example of khilaf based on different approaches to textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : ( ۹۱۸) اور دیوانہ اور بچے کے لئے مغفرت نہ کی جائے ، کیونکہ یہ تو بخشے ہوئے ہیں بلکہ یوں کہے: اللهم اجعله لنا فرطا، واجعله لنا اجرا و ذخرا واجعله لنا شافعا و مشفعا “۔
وجه : اس اثر میں اس کا کچھ حصہ ہے. (۱) عن الحسن أنه كان اذا صلى على الطفل قال اللهم اجعله لنا فرطا، اللهم اجعله لنا اجرا - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الدعاء على الطفل ، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۴۶، نمبر ۶۶۱۵) اس اثر میں بچے پر دعا پڑھنے کا ثبوت ہے۔ (۲) بخاری شریف میں اثر اس طرح ہے . وقال الحسن : يقرأ على الطفل بفاتحة الكتاب و يقول اللهم اجعله لنا سلفا و فرطا و اجرا. (بخاری شریف، باب قرآة فاتحته الكتاب على الجنازة ، ص ۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۳۳۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بچے پر دعا کس طرح پڑھے۔
And he should not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a child, and he should say: O Allah, make him a precursor for us, and make him a reward and treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.

Translation (918): And forgiveness should not be sought for an insane person or a child, because they are forgiven; rather, he should say: O Allah, make him a precursor for us, and make him a reward and treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.
Reasoning: Part of this is in this effect: (1) From al-Hasan that when he prayed over a child, he said: O Allah, make him a precursor for us, O Allah, make him a reward for us. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This effect proves the supplication over a child. (2) In Bukhari, there is an effect like this: And al-Hasan said: Recite al-Fatiha over a child and say: O Allah, make him a predecessor and precursor and reward for us. (Bukhari) This effect shows how to supplicate over a child.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling (918) concerning supplication in the funeral prayer for a child (sabi) or an insane person (majnun). The ruling states that one should not ask for forgiveness (istighfar) for them, because they are already forgiven due to their inability to commit sin (they are not legally responsible). Instead, the person leading the prayer should say a specific supplication asking Allah to make the deceased a precursor (farat), reward (ajr), treasure (dhukhur), intercessor (shafi‘), and one whose intercession is accepted (mushaffa‘). The commentary provides evidence from the practice of Hasan al-Basri (a tabi‘i), who would recite Fatiha and this supplication when praying over a child. This is an important distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the supplication in funeral prayer varies based on the deceased's age and accountability.

Key Terms
فرط (farat): One who goes ahead; in this context, a precursor who prepares the way for others in the afterlife.
مشفّع (mushaffa'): One whose intercession is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why should one not seek forgiveness (istighfar) for a child in the funeral prayer according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because the child has no sins that need forgiveness.
B) Because the child is not a Muslim.
C) Because the funeral prayer for a child is not valid.
D) Because the parents should seek forgiveness instead.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi funeral prayer, for children and the insane, use the specific supplication asking Allah to make them a precursor and reward, and avoid seeking forgiveness.

Who Has Most Right to Lead Funeral Prayer
Ruling and proofs on funeral prayer leadership hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer and explain the dalil for the sultan's precedence over the wali.

Core Idea
The sultan, not the wali, is foremost to lead janazah — authority takes precedence over kinship in funeral rites.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah clarifies a common question: who should lead the funeral prayer when multiple claimants exist? The Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy based on authority and the sunnah of the Prophet and Companions. The ruling is recommended (mustahabb) but the order must be respected to honour the ruler's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy
List the five categories in descending order: sultan, deputy, qadi, imam of locality, wali.
2
Understand the rationale
Why does the sultan take precedence? Because leading janazah is a position of honour and authority; disregarding it is disrespectful.
3
Examine the first dalil
The hadith of the Prophet leading prayer over al-Najashi demonstrates that the leader of the Muslims leads the funeral prayer.
Hadith from Tirmidhi and Bukhari.
4
Examine the second dalil
The story of al-Husayn deferring to Sa'id ibn al-'As shows that the ruler's precedence is from the sunnah.
Narration from Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Shafi'is give priority to the wali over the sultan. The practical difference arises when both are present.
Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : امامت کا زیادہ حقدار کون ہے
ترجمه : (۹۱۹) نماز جنازہ کے لئے زیادہ حقدار بادشاہ ہے، پھر اس کا نائب، پھر قاضی، پھر مسجد محلہ کا امام، پھر ولی۔
تشریح : بادشاہ موجود ہو پھر بھی دوسرا آدمی نماز پڑھائے تو اس میں بادشاہ کی تو ہین ہے۔ اس لئے بادشاہ کو نماز پڑھانے کا زیادہ حق ہے۔ وہ نہ ہو تو قاضی، اور وہ بھی نہ ہو تو گاؤں کا امام، کیونکہ کہ زندگی میں اس کو اپنی نماز کا امام مانا ہے تو موت کے بعد بھی اپنی نماز کے لئے اسی پر راضی ہو گا۔ اور وہ بھی نہ ہو تو اس کا ولی نماز جنازہ پڑھانے کا زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ اور ولی میں بھی وراثت میں ولی عصبہ کی ترتیب ہوگی ۔ البتہ ولی اگر کسی اور کو نماز پڑھانے کی اجازت دے تو دے سکتا ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن عمران بن حصين قال قال لنا رسول الله له ان اخاكم النجاشي قد مات فقوموا فصلوا عـلـيـه فقمنا فصففنا كما يصف على الميت و صلينا عليه كما يصلى على الميت ۔ (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی صلى الله صلوة النبي لو علی النجاشی ص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۰۳۹ار بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوة على الجنائز بالمصلى والمسجد ص ۷۷ انمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث سے ایک بات تو یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ حضور سب کے امیر تھے اس لئے آپ نے نجاشی پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی۔(۲) والی اور امیر نماز جنازہ کا زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ سمعت ابا حازم يقول انى لشاهد يوم مات الحسن بن على فرأيت الحسين ابن على يقول لسعيد بن العاص ويطعن في عنقه تقدم فلولا انها سنة ما قدمت و كان بينهم شيء ( سن للمبتی ، باب من قال الوالی احق بالصلوة علی المیت من الولی ج رابع ص ۲۶، نمبر۶۸۹۴ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من أحق
Section: Who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer.
Translation (919): The most entitled to lead the funeral prayer is the sultan, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the locality, then the wali (guardian).
Explanation: If the sultan is present but someone else leads, that shows disrespect to the sultan. Therefore, the sultan has more right. If he is not present, then the qadi, and if he is also absent, then the imam of the village, because in life the deceased accepted him as imam for prayer, so after death he would also agree with him. If he is also absent, then his wali (guardian) has more right. Among walis, the order of inheritance among asabah (agnatic heirs) will apply. However, if the wali gives permission to someone else, he may lead.
Evidence: (1) From Imran ibn Husain that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed your brother al-Najashi has died, so stand and pray over him.' So we stood and lined up as one lines up over the deceased, and prayed over him as one prays over the deceased. (Tirmidhi, Bukhari) From this hadith, it is understood that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was the leader of all, so he led the prayer over al-Najashi. (2) That the governor and ruler are more entitled to lead funeral prayer is proven by this statement of a Companion: I heard Abu Hazim say: I was present on the day al-Hasan ibn Ali died, and I saw al-Husayn ibn Ali saying to Sa'id ibn al-'As, poking him in the neck: 'Come forward; were it not for the sunnah, I would not bring you forward.' And there was something between them. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage discusses the hierarchy of who has the greatest right to lead the funeral prayer (imamat al-janazah). The ruling (919) states that the sultan (ruler) is most entitled. If the sultan is not available, then his deputy (na'ib) takes precedence. If not, then the qadi (judge), then the imam of the locality (the one who led the deceased in daily prayers), and finally the wali (guardian). The explanation provides the reasoning: leading the funeral prayer is a position of honor and authority, and respecting the ruler's authority is important. Additionally, the imam of the locality is preferred because the deceased trusted him in life. The text also notes that among awliya (guardians), the order of inheritance among asabah applies, meaning the closest male relative in the asabah line takes precedence. However, the wali may delegate the role to another. The evidence includes two hadith: one about the Prophet leading the prayer over al-Najashi, demonstrating that the leader of the Muslims leads the funeral prayer even for an absent person; the second is a narration from al-Husayn ibn Ali deferring to Sa'id ibn al-'As due to his position as governor, indicating that the ruler has priority.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The legal guardian of the deceased, usually a close male relative like father or son.
سلطان (sultan): The ruler or head of state; the highest temporal authority.
قاضي (qadi): Judge appointed by the ruler to adjudicate cases.
نائب (na'ib): Deputy or representative of the sultan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer?
A) The wali (guardian) of the deceased.
B) The imam of the local mosque.
C) The sultan (ruler).
D) The qadi (judge).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the sultan (ruler) is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer, followed by deputy, qadi, imam of locality, and then the wali.
