Hierarchy of Leading the Funeral Prayer
Ruling on the order of precedence for leading the funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for leading the funeral prayer and identify the proofs that establish the ruler's precedence over the guardian.

Core Idea
The ruler leads the funeral prayer before the guardian — authority takes precedence over kinship.

This passage from Thamarat an-Najah presents the ruling on who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The matn gives a clear hierarchy, and the commentary provides proofs from the Prophet and the Companions. Understanding this hierarchy is important for correctly assigning the imam in funeral prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the hierarchy
List the five persons in order of entitlement as given in the matn: sultan, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the quarter, then the wali (guardian).
The wali is the last, not the first.
2
Understand the logic behind the order
The ruler takes precedence to avoid disrespect to his authority. The imam of the quarter takes precedence over the wali because the deceased accepted him as his prayer imam in life.
The wali's right is subordinate to public religious authority.
3
Examine the proof from the Prophet's action
The Prophet led the funeral prayer for an-Najashi, showing that the leader of the Muslims (the imam/ruler) has the right to lead funeral prayers.
This hadith establishes the general principle of the ruler's entitlement.
4
Examine the proof from the Companions' practice
Al-Husayn stepped back for Sa'id ibn al-'As (the governor), proving the governor's precedence. 'Ali sent for the quarter imam, showing the imam's right. 'Umar stated that the guardian has right only after the imam.
These athar from Abu Hazim, 'Ali, and 'Umar support the hierarchy.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school gives precedence to the wali over the ruler when the ruler is not present, while Hanafis maintain the ruler's precedence even then.
The difference causes a practical variation in who leads the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۱۹) السلطان احقُّ بصلوته ثم نائبه ثم القاضى ثم امام الحى ثم الولى
ترجمه : (۹۱۹) نماز جنازہ کے لئے زیادہ حقدار بادشاہ ہے، پھر اس کا نائب، پھر قاضی، پھر مسجد محلہ کا امام، پھر ولی۔ تشریح : بادشاہ موجود ہو پھر بھی دوسرا آدمی نماز پڑھائے تو اس میں بادشاہ کی تو ہین ہے۔ اس لئے بادشاہ کو نماز پڑھانے کا زیادہ حق ہے۔ وہ نہ ہو تو قاضی، اور وہ بھی نہ ہو تو گاؤں کا امام، کیونکہ کہ زندگی میں اس کو اپنی نماز کا امام مانا ہے تو موت کے بعد بھی اپنی نماز کے لئے اسی پر راضی ہو گا۔ اور وہ بھی نہ ہو تو اس کا ولی نماز جنازہ پڑھانے کا زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ اور ولی میں بھی وراثت میں ولی عصبہ کی ترتیب ہوگی ۔ البتہ ولی اگر کسی اور کو نماز پڑھانے کی اجازت دے تو دے سکتا ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن عمران بن حصين قال قال لنا رسول الله له ان اخاكم النجاشي قد مات فقوموا فصلوا عـلـيـه فقمنا فصففنا كما يصف على الميت و صلينا عليه كما يصلى على الميت ۔ (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی صلى الله صلوة النبي لو علی النجاشی ص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۰۳۹ار بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوة على الجنائز بالمصلى والمسجد ص ۷۷ انمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث سے ایک بات تو یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ حضور سب کے امیر تھے اس لئے آپ نے نجاشی پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی۔(۲) والی اور امیر نماز جنازہ کا زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ سمعت ابا حازم يقول انى لشاهد يوم مات الحسن بن على فرأيت الحسين ابن على يقول لسعيد بن العاص ويطعن في عنقه تقدم فلولا انها سنة ما قدمت و كان بينهم شيء (سن للمبتی ، باب من قال الوالی احق بالصلوة علی المیت من الولی ج رابع ص ۲۶، نمبر۶۸۹۴ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من أحق التقدم ان يأذن لغيره (۹۲۱) فان صلى غيره اعادها ان شاء ولا يعيد معه من صلى مع غيره بالصلوۃ علی المیت، ج ثالث ، ص۳۰۲، نمبر ۱۳۹۶ ) اس اثر میں حضرت حسینؓ حضرت حسنؓ کے ولی تھے۔ لیکن سعید بن عاص کو نماز جنازہ کے لئے آگے بڑھایا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس وقت والی اور امیر تھے ۔ اور حضرت حسین نے فرمایا یہ سنت ہے اس لئے والی اور امیر نماز پڑھانے کا ولی سے زیادہ حقدار ہیں۔ (۳)۔ محلے کا امام زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کی یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عـن عـلـى قال الامام احق من صلى جنازة ، ذهبت مع ابراهيم الى جنازة وهو وليها فارسل الى امام الحى فصلى عليها (مصنف ابن الى هیه ۷۳ ، ما قالوا فی تقدم الامام على الجنازة ، ج ثانی، ص ۲۸۳، نمبر ۱۱۳۰۶/۱۱۳۰۵ار مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب من أحق بالصلوة على ا لمیت ، ج ثالث ، ص۳۰۲ نمبر ۶۳۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسجد کا امام نماز کا حقدار ہے۔ (۴) امام کے بعد ولی نماز جنازہ کا زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عمر انه قال الولى احق بالصلوة عليها (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من احق بالصلوة على لمیت، ج ثالث ،ص۳۰۲ نمبر ۶۴۰۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ولی زیادہ حقدار ہے۔
(919) The sultan has more right to his prayer, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the quarter, then the guardian. Translation: (919) The one most entitled to lead the funeral prayer is the king, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the quarter mosque, then the guardian. Explanation: If the king is present and another person leads the prayer, it dishonors the king. So the king has more right to lead. If he is not present, then the qadi, and if he is not present, then the village imam, because in life he accepted him as his imam in prayer, so after death he would be pleased with him for his prayer. And if he is not present, then the guardian has more right to lead the funeral prayer. And among guardians, the order is according to the 'asaba inheritance order. However, the guardian may give permission to another to lead. Proof: (1) From 'Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Your brother an-Najashi has died, so stand and pray over him.' So we stood and lined up as one lines up over the deceased, and we prayed over him as one prays over the deceased. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi salat al-Nabi 'ala al-Najashi, p. 201, no. 1039; Bukhari, Bab al-salat 'ala al-jana'iz bi'l-musalla wa'l-masjid, p. 77, no. 1327) From this hadith it is learned that the Prophet was the leader of all, so he prayed over an-Najashi. (2) The governor and amir have more right to the funeral prayer; the proof is this saying of a Companion: I heard Abu Hazim say, I was present when al-Hasan ibn 'Ali died, and I saw al-Husayn ibn 'Ali saying to Sa'id ibn al-'As, while poking his neck, 'Step forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have stepped forward,' and there was something between them. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man qala al-wali ahaqqu bi'l-salat 'ala al-mayyit min al-wali, j. 4, p. 26, no. 6894; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab man ahaqqu bi'l-salat 'ala al-mayyit, j. 3, p. 302, no. 1396) In this effect, al-Husayn was the guardian of al-Hasan, but he put Sa'id ibn al-'As forward because he was the governor and amir at that time. And al-Husayn said, 'This is the sunna,' so the governor and amir have more right than the guardian. (3) The imam of the quarter has more right; the proof is this saying of a Companion: From 'Ali: The imam has more right to lead the funeral prayer. I went with Ibrahim to a funeral and he was its guardian, so he sent to the imam of the quarter and he prayed over it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab ma qalu fi taqaddum al-imam 'ala al-janaza, j. 2, p. 283, no. 11306/11305; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab man ahaqqu bi'l-salat 'ala al-mayyit, j. 3, p. 302, no. 6395) From this effect, it is learned that the imam of the mosque is entitled to the prayer. (4) After the imam, the guardian has more right to the funeral prayer; the proof is this saying of a Companion: From 'Umar: The guardian has more right to pray over it. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab man ahaqqu bi'l-salat 'ala al-mayyit, j. 3, p. 302, no. 6400) In this effect, it is that the guardian has more right.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on the hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The author states the ruling in the matn: the sultan (ruler), then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the local mosque, then the wali (guardian). The commentator explains that if a person of lower rank leads the prayer in the presence of one higher, it shows disrespect to the higher authority. The reasoning for the precedence of the local imam over the wali is that the deceased accepted him as his imam in life, so he would be pleased with him after death. Among guardians, the order follows the 'asaba inheritance order. The proofs cited are four: (1) The Prophet led the prayer for an-Najashi, showing that the leader (imam) of the Muslims has the right. (2) The incident of al-Husayn stepping back for Sa'id ibn al-'As, proving the governor's precedence. (3) 'Ali's action of sending to the quarter imam to lead, showing the imam's right. (4) 'Umar's statement that the guardian has the right after the imam. All proofs are from the actions and sayings of the Prophet and Companions, and they establish the Hanafi position that the ruler takes precedence over the guardian.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sulṭān): The ruling authority, the sultan or ruler who has political authority.
الولي (al-walī): The guardian of the deceased, typically a male relative from the 'asaba.
نائب (nā'ib): The deputy of the sultan, often the governor or viceroy.
القاضي (al-qāḍī): The judge, a religious legal authority.
امام الحى (imām al-ḥayy): The imam of the local quarter or village mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is the most entitled to lead the funeral prayer?
A) The wali (guardian)
B) The sultan (ruler)
C) The imam of the mosque
D) The qadi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy for leading the funeral prayer prioritizes public authority (sultan, deputy, qadi, imam of quarter) over private guardianship (wali).

Delegation of Leading the Funeral Prayer
Ruling with proof on delegation of funeral prayer leadership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the entitled person may delegate leading the funeral prayer and explain the evidence from the act of al-Husayn ibn 'Ali.

Core Idea
Delegation of funeral prayer leadership is permissible because the entitled person's permission prevents disrespect.

This ruling addresses a practical scenario: who leads the funeral prayer when the most entitled person is present but wishes to delegate? The Hanafi school, drawing on the precedent of al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, affirms that the entitled person may give permission to another. Let's examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the entitled person giving permission to another to lead the funeral prayer. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah).
The source says 'jā'iz' (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the action of al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, who as the guardian of his brother al-Hasan, gave permission to Sa'id ibn al-'As, the governor, to lead the funeral prayer.
The hadith is reported by Bayhaqi and Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Al-Husayn was the most entitled (wali) to lead, but he verbally instructed Sa'id to step forward. This shows that delegation is allowed; if it were not, al-Husayn would have led himself to uphold the sunna.
Al-Husayn's phrase 'were it not for the sunna, I would not have stepped forward' indicates that the sunna is to let the entitled person lead, but he chose to delegate.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some schools may restrict delegation more strictly, e.g., requiring the entitled person to lead unless excused. The Hanafis allow it as long as there is no disrespect.
The source mentions no explicit opposition, but the commentary notes it is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that delegation is permissible based on the precedent. The tarjih authority is straightforward in the commentary.
No explicit tarjih is given, but the ruling is presented as the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التقدم ان يأذن لغيره
ترجمه : (۹۲۰) اور جس کو آگے بڑھنے کا حق ہے وہ دوسرے کو اجازت دے سکتا ہے۔ تشریح : جو آدمی میت کی نماز کا زیادہ حقدار ہے وہ کسی دوسرے کو امامت کرنے کی اجازت دے جسکو آگے بڑھنے کا حق نہیں ہے تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں زیادہ حقدار والے کی توہین نہیں ہے، اور اس کی اجازت سے کام ہورہا ہے۔
وجه : سمعت ابا حازم يقول اني لشاهد يوم مات الحسن بن على فرأيت الحسين ابن على يقول لسعيد بن العاص ويطعن في عنقه تقدم فلولا انها سنة ما قدمت وكان بينهم شيء ) بیہقی ، باب من قال الوالی احق بالصلوة على الميت من الولی ج رابع ص ۴۶، نمبر ۶۸۹۴ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من أحق بالصلوۃ علی المیت ، ج ثالث ، ص۳۰۲ نمبر ۶۳۹۶) اس عمل صحابی میں حضرت حسین نے حضرت سعید بن العاص کو آگے بڑھایا۔
[The one entitled to lead may give permission to another]. Translation: (920) And the one who has the right to step forward may give permission to another. Explanation: The person who is most entitled to the funeral prayer may give permission to another who does not have the right to lead, and this is permissible. Because there is no disrespect to the one more entitled, and the action is done with his permission. Proof: I heard Abu Hazim say, I was present when al-Hasan ibn 'Ali died, and I saw al-Husayn ibn 'Ali saying to Sa'id ibn al-'As, while poking his neck, 'Step forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have stepped forward,' and there was something between them. (Bayhaqi, al-Sunan al-Kubra, Bab man qala al-wali ahaqqu bi'l-salat 'ala al-mayyit min al-wali, j. 4, p. 46, no. 6894; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab man ahaqqu bi'l-salat 'ala al-mayyit, j. 3, p. 302, no. 6396) In this action of the Companion, al-Husayn put Sa'id ibn al-'As forward.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that the one most entitled to lead the funeral prayer may delegate the role to another. The commentator explains that if a person who does not have the right leads with the permission of the one who does, it is permissible because the entitled person's honor is not violated; the action is done by his authorization. The proof is the incident of al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, who as the guardian of his brother al-Hasan, gave permission to Sa'id ibn al-'As, the governor, to lead. This shows that delegation is permissible and does not contravene the hierarchy.

Key Terms
التقدم (al-taqaddum): Stepping forward to lead the funeral prayer as the imam.
اذن (idhn): Permission or authorization given by the entitled person to another to lead.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The action of al-Husayn ibn 'Ali giving permission to Sa'id ibn al-'As
C) A consensus of the companions
D) A qiyas on regular prayer

Key Takeaway
Delegation of funeral prayer leadership is permissible in Hanafi fiqh when the entitled person gives permission without disrespect.

Repeating the Funeral Prayer When Led by a Non-Entitled Imam
Ruling with proof on repetition of funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating the funeral prayer and apply it when the entitled person was absent.

Core Idea
The entitled imam may repeat the funeral prayer, but those who already prayed should not, because it is fard kifayah.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a funeral prayer has been led by someone who was not the rightful imam (e.g., the local imam instead of the sultan). The text clarifies who may repeat and who must not. The ruling hinges on the nature of the funeral prayer as a communal obligation (fard kifayah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Distinguish between the entitled person (e.g., the sultan) and those who already prayed with the non-entitled imam.
The entitled person has not yet performed the prayer; others have.
2
State the ruling for each
The entitled person may repeat if he wishes; those who already prayed should not repeat.
Repetition is permissible but not obligatory for the entitled person.
3
Understand the reason
The funeral prayer is fard kifayah — once it is performed, the obligation is lifted for all. Therefore, repeating it is not required for those who already participated.
The entitled person's repetition is a separate act, not fulfilling the original obligation again.
4
Examine the proof
The hadith of the black man shows that the Prophet (ﷺ) led the funeral prayer at the grave after others had already prayed, indicating that the entitled imam may repeat.
The hadith is a sound (hasan) narration; it is used as evidence for the permissibility of repetition.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may not permit repetition after the funeral prayer has been performed, but the Hanafi school allows it for the one entitled to lead.
The disagreement stems from different interpretations of the hadith and the nature of the obligation.

Source Text

(۹۲۱) فان صلى غيره اعادها ان شاء ولا يعيد معه من صلى مع غيره
ترجمه : (۹۲۱) اور اگر دوسرا نماز پڑھ لے تو حقدار چاہے تو نماز دہراوے اور دوسرے ان کے ساتھ جنہوں نے نماز پڑھ لی ہے وہ نہ دہرا دیں۔
تشریح : مثلا سلطان کو نماز پڑھانے کا حق تھا لیکن مسجد کے امام نے نماز پڑھادی تو سلطان چاہے تو نماز جنازہ دوبارہ پڑھے، کیونکہ حقدار نے نہیں پڑھی ہے، اور جن لوگوں نے ابھی تک نہیں پڑھی ہے وہ بھی سلطان کے ساتھ ہو کر پڑھ سکتا ہے لیکن جن لوگوں نے امام کے ساتھ ایک مرتبہ پڑھ لی تو اب دوبارہ سلطان کے ساتھ نہ پڑھے، کیونکہ نماز جنازہ ایک ہی مرتبہ فرض ہے۔
وجه : عن ابي هريرة ان اسود رجلا أو امرأة كان يقيم المسجد فمات ولم يعلم النبي الا الله بموته فذكره ذات يوم فقال ما فعل ذلك الانسان قالوا مات يا رسول الله قال افلا اذنتمونى فقالوا انه كان كذا كذا قصته قال وفحقروا شانه قال فدلوني على قبره قال
(921) If another prays over him, [the entitled one] may repeat it if he wishes, and those who prayed with him should not repeat. Translation: (921) And if another leads the prayer, the entitled person may repeat the prayer if he wishes, but those who have already prayed with that other should not repeat. Explanation: For example, the sultan had the right to lead the prayer, but the imam of the mosque led it; then the sultan may repeat the funeral prayer if he wishes, because the entitled person did not pray. And those who have not yet prayed may also pray with the sultan, but those who have already prayed once with the imam should not repeat, because the funeral prayer is only obligatory once. Proof: From Abu Huraira: A black man or woman used to clean the mosque, then died, and the Prophet did not know... [hadith continues]
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning repetition of the funeral prayer when a non-entitled person has led it. The matn states that the entitled person may repeat the prayer if he wishes, but those who already prayed with the first imam should not repeat. The commentator explains the reasoning: the entitlement was not fulfilled, so the entitled person may repeat to earn the reward, but since the funeral prayer is a single obligation (fard kifayah), those who have already performed it are not required to repeat. The proof is the hadith of the black man who cleaned the mosque; when the Prophet discovered he had died and was buried without the Prophet's knowledge, he went to his grave and led the prayer over him. This shows that the one entitled (in this case, the Prophet as imam) may repeat the prayer even if others had already prayed.

Key Terms
اعادها (a'ādahā): To repeat the funeral prayer; the entitled person may perform it again.
من صلى مع غيره (man ṣallā ma'a ghayrihī): Those who already prayed with another (the non-entitled) imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The entitled imam may repeat the funeral prayer, but those who already prayed must not, because the obligation is communal and once fulfilled.

The Entitled Person May Authorize Another to Lead Janazah Prayer
Ruling on delegation of Janazah leadership with evidence from Companions' practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delegation of Janazah leadership and apply the order of precedence.

Core Idea
The rightful leader of Janazah may delegate; the ruler or imam takes precedence over the guardian.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on who has the right to lead the Janazah prayer. The core ruling is that the one most entitled may authorize another to lead in his place. The order of precedence is established by the sunnah: the ruler or his deputy, then the local imam, then the guardian (wali) of the deceased. The evidence comes from the action of Imam Husayn (may Allah be pleased with him) at the funeral of his brother Imam Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on authorization
State the Hanafi ruling: The one entitled to lead Janazah may authorize another person to lead. This is permissible and valid.
The authorization is based on the entitled person's permission, not on the delegate's own right.
2
Understand the order of precedence
List the order: ruler/deputy, local imam, guardian (wali). The ruler takes precedence over the guardian, as shown by Husayn's action.
This order is specific to Janazah; for regular prayers, the order may differ.
3
Examine the evidence from Husayn (ra)
Analyze the hadith: Husayn, though the wali, let Sa'id ibn al-'As (the governor) lead, saying 'Were it not that this is a sunnah, I would not have put you forward.' This proves the ruler's precedence and the permissibility of delegation.
The hadith is a sahih athar (traceable to a Companion).
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some Shafi'is hold that the deceased's appointment of a specific person takes precedence over the imam's right. The Hanafi school rejects this, prioritizing the sunnah order.
This difference affects real-world funeral arrangements.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۹۲۰) اور جس کو آگے بڑھنے کا حق ہے وہ دوسرے کو اجازت دے سکتا ہے۔ تشریح : جو آدمی میت کی نماز کا زیادہ حقدار ہے وہ کسی دوسرے کو امامت کرنے کی اجازت دے جسکو آگے بڑھنے کا حق نہیں ہے تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں زیادہ حقدار والے کی توہین نہیں ہے، اور اس کی اجازت سے کام ہورہا ہے۔

Section: Precedence: He may authorize another. If another prays, he may repeat if he wishes, but those who prayed with the other do not repeat with him over the Janazah prayer. ... In this narration, Husayn was the guardian of Hasan, but he let Sa'id ibn al-'As lead because he was the governor. He said this is the sunnah, so the ruler is more entitled than the guardian. (3) The local imam is more entitled, as per the saying of 'Ali: 'The imam is more entitled to lead the Janazah.' ... (4) After the imam, the guardian is more entitled, as per 'Umar's saying: 'The guardian is more entitled.' Translation (920): The one entitled to precedence may authorize another. Commentary: The person most entitled to the Janazah prayer may authorize another who has no right to precedence; it is permissible because no disrespect is shown and it is done with permission. Evidence: Abu Hazim said: I witnessed when Hasan ibn 'Ali died, Husayn ibn 'Ali said to Sa'id ibn al-'As, pulling his collar: 'Go forward; were it not that this is a sunnah, I would not have put you forward.'
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling from the Hanafi school on the Janazah prayer. It states that the person who has the right to lead the Janazah (the one most entitled, such as the ruler or the local imam) may authorize another person to lead in his place. This is permissible because it does not disrespect the rightful person and the prayer is performed with his permission. The evidence is the action of Imam Husayn (may Allah be pleased with him) at the funeral of Imam Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him). Husayn was the guardian (wali) of Hasan, but he let Sa'id ibn al-'As, who was the governor, lead the prayer. Husayn said, 'Were it not that this is a sunnah, I would not have put you forward,' indicating that the governor or ruler takes precedence over the guardian. This ruling applies to the Janazah prayer and establishes that the one with authority (the imam or ruler) is the most entitled to lead, and he can delegate that right to another. The commentary also mentions other related rulings: that the local imam is more entitled than a relative, and after the imam, the guardian (wali) is entitled. These are supported by sayings of the companions 'Ali and 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them).

Key Terms
التقدم (al-taqaddum): The right to lead the Janazah prayer, i.e., to be the imam.
ولي (wali): The guardian of the deceased, usually a close male relative (father, son, brother) who is responsible for the funeral arrangements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 'Were it not that this is a sunnah, I would not have put you forward.'
C) 'You are more learned in prayer.'
D) 'The governor must lead.'

Key Takeaway
The one entitled to lead Janazah may delegate, and the order of precedence is: ruler/deputy, then local imam, then guardian.

If Another Leads, the Rightful Person May Repeat but Not Those Who Prayed
Ruling on repetition of Janazah prayer when a non-entitled person leads

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating the Janazah prayer and apply it to scenarios involving entitled and non-entitled imams.

Core Idea
The entitled person may repeat Janazah; those who already prayed must not.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Janazah prayer: when someone other than the most entitled person leads the prayer. The Hanafi school rules that the entitled person may repeat the prayer if he wishes, but those who already prayed with the first imam should not repeat. This ruling is based on the Prophet's own action (peace be upon him) when he prayed at a grave after the prayer had already been performed. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary repetition of a fard kifayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is repeating the Janazah prayer. For the entitled person, repetition is permissible (sunnah muakkadah); for those who already prayed, it is not permissible.
The Janazah prayer is fard kifayah; once performed, it is fulfilled.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying at the grave after the burial, as narrated by Abu Huraira.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet was the most entitled person (ruler of the community) and he had not participated in the first prayer. By repeating the prayer, he demonstrated that the entitled person may repeat.
The action of the Prophet is a Sunnah that indicates permissibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that the entitled person should not repeat if he arrives after the prayer, but the relied-upon position is that he may repeat.
The stronger evidence supports repetition.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that the entitled person may repeat, based on the clear hadith and the principle that the entitled person's right is not nullified.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۲۱) اور اگر دوسرا نماز پڑھ لے تو حقدار چاہے تو نماز دہراوے اور دوسرے ان کے ساتھ جنہوں نے نماز پڑھ لی ہے وہ نہ دہرا دیں۔
تشریح : مثلا سلطان کو نماز پڑھانے کا حق تھا لیکن مسجد کے امام نے نماز پڑھادی تو سلطان چاہے تو نماز جنازہ دوبارہ پڑھے، کیونکہ حقدار نے نہیں پڑھی ہے، اور جن لوگوں نے ابھی تک نہیں پڑھی ہے وہ بھی سلطان کے ساتھ ہو کر پڑھ سکتا ہے لیکن جن لوگوں نے امام کے ساتھ ایک مرتبہ پڑھ لی تو اب دوبارہ سلطان کے ساتھ نہ پڑھے، کیونکہ نماز جنازہ ایک ہی مرتبہ فرض ہے۔
وجه : حضور سلطان تھے، اور انہوں نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تو آپ نے نماز پڑھی۔ عن ابي هريرة ان اسود رجلا أو امرأة كان يقيم المسجد فمات ولم يعلم النبي بموته فذكره ذات يوم فقال ما فعل ذلك الانسان قالوا مات يا رسول الله قال افلا اذنتمونى فقالوا انه كان كذا كذا قصته قال وفحقروا شانه قال فدلوني على قبره قال فانی قبره فصلی علیه ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر بعد ما يدفن ، ص ۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۳۳۷ را بود او د شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر ، ص ۴۶۸، نمبر۳۲۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے دوبارہ نماز پڑھی ہے۔
Translation (921): And if another prays, then the entitled person may repeat if he wishes, but those who prayed with the other do not repeat with him. Commentary: For example, the sultan had the right to lead, but the local imam led the prayer. Then the sultan may repeat the Janazah prayer if he wishes, because the entitled person did not pray. Those who have not yet prayed may join the sultan. But those who already prayed once with the imam should not pray again with the sultan, because the Janazah prayer is fard only once. Evidence: The Prophet (peace be upon him) was the sultan and he did not pray, so he prayed. Abu Huraira reported that a black man or woman used to clean the mosque and died without the Prophet knowing. He asked about him, and they told him he died, he said 'Why did you not inform me?' They said he was such and such, and they belittled his matter. He said 'Show me his grave,' so he went to his grave and prayed over it. (Bukhari, chapter on prayer at the grave after burial, p.213 no.1337; Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer at the grave, p.468 no.3203) This hadith shows that the Prophet prayed again.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a person other than the most entitled leads the Janazah prayer. The Hanafi position is that the entitled person (e.g., the ruler or local imam) may repeat the prayer if he wishes, because he did not participate in the first prayer. However, those who already prayed with the first imam should not repeat the prayer with the entitled person, because the Janazah prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) that is fulfilled once. The evidence provided is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who, upon learning that a man who used to clean the mosque had died without being informed, went to his grave and prayed over it. This indicates that the Prophet repeated the Janazah prayer after it had been performed by others, because he was the most entitled (as the leader of the community). The commentary clarifies that the Sultan (ruler) has a similar right: he may repeat the prayer, but those who already prayed should not repeat. This ruling is based on the principle that the entitled person's right is not nullified by another's act; he may choose to lead a second prayer for those who haven't prayed, but those who already prayed must not repeat, as it would be like offering the same fard twice.

Key Terms
اعادها (a'adaha): He repeats it (the Janazah prayer) — i.e., performs it again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the local imam leads the Janazah prayer and later the ruler arrives, what should those who already prayed with the imam do?
A) They should repeat the prayer with the ruler.
B) They should not repeat the prayer.
C) They must repeat the prayer to fulfill the right of the ruler.
D) They may choose to repeat or not.

Key Takeaway
The entitled person may repeat the Janazah prayer, but those who already prayed may not, because the obligation is fulfilled once.

Prayer at the Grave Before Decomposition
Ruling on performing Janazah prayer at the grave after burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Janazah prayer at the grave after burial and identify the condition under which it is permitted.

Core Idea
Prayer at the grave is valid as long as the body has not decomposed, even without ghusl.

Sometimes a person is buried without the Janazah prayer being performed due to various reasons. The Hanafi school teaches that this prayer can still be offered at the grave, as long as the body is intact. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, the key condition of decomposition, and the evidence from the Sunnah that supports this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing the Janazah prayer at the grave after burial. The ruling is that it is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) to fulfill the obligation that was missed.
This is not a new obligation; it is a compensatory act.
2
Determine the condition for validity
The prayer is valid only if the body has not decomposed. Decomposition is determined by local climate and customs, not by a fixed time period.
The hadith mentions the Prophet praying after three days, but that is not a fixed limit.
3
Understand that ghusl is not required
The text explicitly states 'even if he was not given a bath' (لم يغسل), meaning ghusl is not a condition for prayer at the grave.
This differs from the regular Janazah prayer which typically requires ghusl.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying at the grave of a black woman who used to clean the mosque. This shows that prayer at the grave is permissible after burial.
The condition of non-decomposition is derived from the fact that the Prophet prayed within three days, before decomposition would typically begin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۲۳) اور اگر کوئی بلا نماز کے دفن کیا جائے تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی اگر چہ نسل نہ دیا گیا ہو جب تک نفش پھٹی نہ ہو۔
تشریح : اگر بغیر نماز کے دفن کر دیا گیا ہو تو ہر جگہ کے موسم کے اعتبار سے اندازہ لگایا جائے گا کہ نعش پھٹی ہے یا نہیں ، اگر ابھی تک پھٹی نہیں ہوگی تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی ، اور پھٹ گئی ہے تو نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
وجه : ۔(۱) قبر پر نماز جنازہ پڑھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان اسود رجلا او امرأة كان يقيم المسجد فمات ولم يعلم النبي . بموته فذكره ذات يوم فقال ما فعل ذلك الانسان قالوا مات يا رسول الله قال افلا اذنتمونى فقالوا انه كان كذا كذا قصته قال وفحقروا شانه قال فدلوني على قبره قال فاتی قبرہ فصلی علیه ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة علی القبر بعد ماید فن ، ص ۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۳۳۷ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر ، ص ۴۶۸، نمبر ۳۲۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے ایک عورت کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث سے اندازہ لگتا ہے کہ پھٹنے سے پہلے نماز پڑھے، کیونکہ تین دن میں نماز پڑھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس أن رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى على ميت بعد موته بثلاث _( سنن بیھقی ، باب الصلوة على القبر بعد ما يدفن الميت ، ج رابع ص ۷۵ نمبر ۷۰۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین دن کے بعد حضور
Translation (923): And if someone is buried without prayer, then prayer should be performed at his grave, even if he was not given a bath (ghusl), as long as the body has not decomposed. Commentary: If buried without prayer, then depending on the climate of the place, it will be estimated whether the body has decomposed or not. If it has not yet decomposed, prayer will be performed over it; if it has decomposed, it will not be performed. Evidence: (1) The evidence for praying at the grave is this hadith: Abu Huraira reported that a black man or woman used to clean the mosque and died without the Prophet knowing. He asked about him, they said he died, he said 'Why did you not inform me?' They said he was such and such, and they belittled his matter. He said 'Show me his grave,' so he went to his grave and prayed over it. (Bukhari, chapter on prayer at the grave after burial, p.213 no.1337; Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer at the grave, p.468 no.3203) This hadith shows that the Prophet prayed over a woman's grave. (2) This hadith indicates that prayer should be offered before decomposition, because he prayed within three days. From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet prayed over a deceased three days after his death. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer at the grave after burial, 4:75 no.7003) This hadith shows that the Prophet prayed after three days.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage deals with the case of a deceased person who was buried without the Janazah prayer being performed. The Hanafi ruling is that the prayer may be performed at the grave, even if the deceased was not given ghusl (ritual washing), provided the body has not decomposed. The determination of decomposition depends on the climate and local conditions; the prayer is valid only if the body is still intact. The evidence comes from the well-known hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who prayed at the grave of a black woman who used to clean the mosque, after she had been buried. The Prophet was not informed in time, so he went to her grave and prayed over it. This indicates that prayer at the grave is permissible after burial. Additionally, the text cites a narration from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed over a deceased three days after death, showing that the limit is not a fixed time but based on decomposition. The commentary explains that if decomposition has started, the prayer cannot be performed at the grave. This ruling applies regardless of whether the deceased was washed or not; the key condition is the intactness of the body. The purpose is to fulfill the obligation of the Janazah prayer even after burial, so long as it is practically possible.

Key Terms
يتفسخ (yatafassa): To decompose, rot, or disintegrate; the state of the body after death when it begins to decay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only within 24 hours of burial.
B) As long as the body has not decomposed, regardless of time.
C) Only if the deceased was given ghusl.
D) It is never permissible to pray at the grave.

Key Takeaway
The Janazah prayer can be performed at the grave as long as the body has not decomposed, even if ghusl was not performed, fulfilling the obligation after burial.

Priority in Leading Funeral Prayer
Ruling with proof on priority in leading funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on who is more entitled to lead the funeral prayer and explain how a conflicting Qawl Sahabi is handled through the school's qa'idah.

Core Idea
The imam's Shari'ah-granted authority overrides a deceased's bequest for a specific person to lead the funeral prayer.

When a Muslim passes away, a funeral prayer is performed. A common question is who should lead it: the local imam or someone the deceased specifically requested? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this priority, which balances respect for the deceased's wishes with the general authority granted by Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The ruling: the one with general wilayah (the imam) has priority over a special appointee.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is an athar from Sayyidah Maimunah (may Allah be pleased with her) that she appointed Sa'id bin Zaid to lead her funeral prayer.
This suggests the appointee is preferred.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The apparent meaning of the hadith supports the appointee's priority. However, the Hanafi school uses a qa'idah (principle) that Shari'ah-granted authority (wilayah) should take precedence.
This is a case of overriding a zanni proof with a stronger principle.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is ikhtilaf: some scholars follow the apparent meaning of the hadith. The Hanafis give priority to the imam.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is that the imam's right prevails, but if someone else leads, the prayer is valid. This is based on later Hanafi consensus (mutakhkhirin).
The position is wajib (confirmed) but not absolutely obligatory to enforce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
(۹۲۲) ومن له ولاية التقدّم فيها احقُّ ممن اوصى له الميت بالصلوة عليه على المفتى به.
ترجمه : (۹۲۲) جسکو نماز میں آگے بڑھنے کی ولایت تھی ، وہ زیادہ حقدار ہے اس سے جسکے لئے میت نے اس پر نماز پڑھانے کی وصیت کی۔ مفتی بہ قول کے مطابق۔ تشریح : مثلا محلے کے امام کونماز پڑھانے کا حق تھا لیکن میت نے کسی رشتہ دار کے لئے وصیت کی وہ نماز جنازہ پڑھائے ،تو مفتی بہ قول یہ ہے کہ امام کو نماز پڑھانے کا زیادہ حق ہے، جس کے لئے وصیت کی ہے اس کو زیادہ حق نہیں ہے، چنانچہ امام اپنا حق ساقط نہ کرنا چاہے تو کرسکتا ہے۔
وجه : عن محارب بن دثار قال ماتت ام المؤمنين اظنها ميمونة فأوصت ان يصلى عليها سعيد بن زيد ( سنن بیہقی ، باب من قال الوصی بالصلاۃ علیہ اولی ان کان قد اوصی بھا الیہ ، ج رابع ، ص ۴۶، نمبر ۶۸۹۸ ) اس عمل صحابیہ میں ہے کہ جس کے لئے وصیت کی ہے وہ زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ لیکن قاعدے کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ جسکو شریعت نے حق دیاوہ زیادہ حقدار ہو۔ تا ہم کوئی بھی نماز پڑھادے گا تو نماز ہوجائے گی۔
Chapter. (922) Whoever has the authority to lead in it (the prayer) is more entitled than one for whom the deceased made a bequest to pray over him, according to the mufta bihi opinion. Translation: (922) The one who had the authority to lead in prayer is more entitled than the one for whom the deceased made a bequest to lead the prayer over him. According to the relied-upon opinion. Explanation: For example, the local imam had the right to lead the prayer, but the deceased made a bequest for a relative to lead the janazah prayer. The relied-upon opinion is that the imam has greater right to lead; the one for whom bequest was made does not have greater right. Thus, if the imam does not wish to forfeit his right, he may do so. Proof: From Muharib bin Dithar: Umm al-Mu'minin (I think Maimunah) died and bequeathed that Sa'id bin Zaid should pray over her. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This action of a female Companion indicates that the one bequeathed is better. But the principle requires that the one to whom Shari'ah gave the right is more entitled. However, if anyone leads the prayer, it is valid.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on who has priority in leading the funeral prayer. The matn states that the person holding general authority to lead prayers (e.g., the local imam) is more entitled than someone specifically appointed by the deceased. The 'mufta bihi' (relied-upon) position is that the imam's right prevails. The explanation clarifies with an example: if the deceased appoints a relative, the imam may still insist on leading. The proof is an athar from Sayyidah Maimunah (may Allah be pleased with her) who appointed Sa'id bin Zaid. The author notes the apparent conflict with the general principle (qa'idah) that the one granted authority by Shari'ah is more entitled. However, the ruling ultimately upholds the imam's priority. The passage also indicates that if someone else leads, the prayer is valid, so the right is not obligatory to enforce.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): The authority or right to lead the funeral prayer, typically held by the local imam or ruler.
مفتی بہ (mufta bihi): The relied-upon opinion in the Hanafi school for issuing fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The appointed person
C) The closest male relative
D) The deceased's executor

Key Takeaway
The one with Shari'ah-granted authority (imam) is entitled to lead the funeral prayer over a bequest, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Funeral Prayer at the Grave Before Decomposition
Ruling with proof on janazah prayer at grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer at the grave, identify the condition of body integrity, and evaluate the hadith evidences.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer at the grave is allowed only before body decomposition; the Prophet's action is the primary proof.

When a deceased Muslim is buried without the funeral prayer, the Hanafi school permits praying at the grave as long as the body has not decomposed. This ruling is based on multiple hadith, including the Prophet's own practice. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, its condition, and the textual evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn states that prayer is performed over the grave even if the deceased was not washed, provided the body has not decomposed. Note that this is a separate sunnah prayer, not a substitute for the missed one.
The ruling is conditional; if decomposition has started, prayer is not valid.
2
Analyze the condition (tafassukh)
The passage explains that the assessment of decomposition depends on local climate. The hadith give a guideline of three days, but the actual condition is physical integrity of the body.
The term 'tafassukh' refers to splitting or decay of the corpse.
3
Examine the primary proof (dalil naqli)
The hadith from Abu Hurairah reports the Prophet praying at a grave after burial. This establishes permissibility. The Prophet also prayed three days after death, indicating a timeframe before decomposition.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for sunnah ruling.
4
Evaluate supporting evidence
The passage also cites the hadith from Ibn Abbas and the action of Ibn Umar to reinforce the three-day guideline. These together confirm the ruling.
The multiple narrations strengthen the reliability of the practice.

فانی قبره فصلی علیه ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر بعد ما يدفن ، ص ۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۳۳۷ را بود او د شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی القبر ، ص ۴۶۸، نمبر۳۲۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے دوبارہ نماز پڑھی ہے۔

صلى الله
نماز پڑھے، کیونکہ تین دن میں نماز پڑھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس أن رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى على ميت بعد موته بثلاث _( سنن بیھقی ، باب الصلوة على القبر بعد ما يدفن الميت ، ج رابع ص ۷۵ نمبر ۷۰۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین دن کے بعد حضور
(پیدائش سے پہلے) نمازہ پڑھی۔ (۳) اس عمل صحابی میں بھی ہے ۔ توفی عاصم بن عمر وابن عمر غائب فقدم بعد ذلک قال ايوب احسبه قال بثلاث قال فقال ارونی قبر اخی فاروه فصلی علیه . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۶۲، فیلمیت یصلی علیہ بعد دفن من فعله ، ج ثالث ، ص ۴۴، نمبر ۱۱۹۳۹ رستن سبیھقی ، باب الصلوة على القبر بعد ما يدفن الميت، ج رابع ، ص ۸۱ نمبر ۷۰۲۵ ) اس اثر میں تین دن کا اشارہ ہے۔
(923) And if (the deceased) is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave even if he was not washed, as long as his body has not decomposed. So he came to his grave and prayed over him. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Book of Prayer at the Grave After Burial, p. 213, no. 1337; Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of Prayer at the Grave, p. 468, no. 3203) In this hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed again. Translation: (923) And if someone is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave even if he was not given a bath, as long as his corpse has not split. Explanation: If buried without prayer, it is assessed based on the climate of the place whether the corpse has split or not. If it has not split yet, prayer is performed; if it has split, it is not performed. Proof: (1) Evidence for performing janazah prayer at the grave is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah that a black man or woman used to clean the mosque and died, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not know of his/her death. One day he mentioned him/her and said, 'What happened to that person?' They said, 'He died, O Messenger of Allah.' He said, 'Why did you not inform me?' They told his story and that they had considered him insignificant. He said, 'Show me his grave.' So he came to his grave and prayed over him. (Bukhari and Abu Dawud) (2) From this hadith it is understood that prayer is performed before decomposition because he prayed after three days. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed over a deceased three days after his death. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) (3) Also in this action of a Companion: 'Asim bin 'Umar died, and Ibn 'Umar was absent. He came later, and Ayyub said he thinks after three days. He said, 'Show me my brother's grave.' They showed him and he prayed over him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) This effect indicates three days.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on performing the funeral prayer at the grave when the body was buried without prayer. The matn states that janazah prayer is offered at the grave even if the deceased was not washed, as long as the body has not decomposed. The explanation clarifies that the condition is based on whether the corpse has split (taphashsha), which depends on the local climate; if the body is still intact, prayer is valid. The proofs include multiple hadith: the famous hadith of the black man (or woman) from Abu Hurairah, the hadith of Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet prayed after three days, and the action of Ibn 'Umar indicating three days. These establish the permissibility and timeframe. The Hanafi position is that prayer at the grave is permitted before decomposition, and the three-day reference is a guideline. The 'wa law lam yughsal' (even if not washed) indicates that the condition of ghusl is not required for this prayer; it is a separate prayer for one missed.

Key Terms
تفسخ (tafassukh): Decomposition or splitting of the corpse; if the body has decomposed, prayer at the grave is no longer valid.
نعش (na'sh): The corpse or bier; here referring to the body in the grave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary condition for performing janazah prayer at the grave after burial without prior prayer?
A) The deceased must have been washed
B) The body must not have decomposed

D) A close relative must request it

Key Takeaway
Janazah prayer at the grave is permitted (sunnah) only if the body has not decomposed, with evidence from the Prophet's action and Companions' practice.

Preferring Separate Funeral Prayers for Multiple Janazahs
Choosing individual prayer for each funeral when multiple are present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying for multiple funerals and apply the principle of afdal fa afdal to order them.

Core Idea
When multiple funerals gather, pray separately for each, starting with the most virtuous.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: when several funeral prayers (janazah) are to be performed at the same time. The Hanafi school provides a clear recommendation on whether to combine or separate them, and how to prioritize. The ruling is not obligatory but a preferred practice, reflecting the school's emphasis on giving due respect to each deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? (Performing multiple janazah prayers). What is the ruling? (It is awla – better – to pray separately for each.)
Awla is a non-binding recommendation, not an obligation.
2
Understand the recommendation level
In Hanafi terminology, 'awla' indicates a preferred or superior action, but not a duty. Distinguish it from 'wajib' or 'fard'.
This helps avoid confusion about the binding nature of the ruling.
3
Apply the prioritization principle
When praying separately, one should give precedence to the most virtuous (afdal fa afdal). Virtue may be based on righteousness, age, gender, or other factors.
The text provides an example: men, then children, then women, but the principle is general.
4
Work through the example
If funerals of a man, a child, and a woman are present, the recommended order is: man first, then child, then woman. Alternatively, prioritize the most senior in righteousness.
The example is illustrative, not exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

افضل فالافضل (afdal fa afdal): The most virtuous, then the next virtuous; a principle of ordering.

Arrangement of Multiple Funerals for Combined Prayer
Ruling with proof on funeral arrangement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended order of placing bodies in a combined funeral prayer and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Men nearest the imam, then boys, then khuntha, then women — virtue determines proximity.

When multiple janazahs are prayed over in one prayer, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific order based on virtue and gender. This ruling, derived from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ at Uhud, ensures that the most virtuous are closest to the imam. Understanding this arrangement is essential for correctly performing combined funeral prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is arranging multiple bodies for a single funeral prayer. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory. The order is: men next to the imam, then boys, then khuntha, then women.
The chest of each body must be in front of the imam, with the row facing qiblah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas about the martyrs of Uhud, where the Prophet ﷺ prayed over ten at a time and repeatedly placed Hamzah (the most virtuous) in front.
Hadith reference: Ibn Majah, Bab ma ja'a fi al-salat 'ala al-shuhada', no. 1513.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's repeated placement of Hamzah in front indicates that virtue (fadl) determines proximity to the imam. This is the basis for ordering by gender and age: men (generally more virtuous than children and women) come first, then boys, then khuntha, then women.
Khuntha (ambiguous gender) is placed between boys and women due to uncertainty.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school may place the bodies differently, but the Hanafi school follows this hadith. The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
No detailed opposing proof is given in this passage.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) based on explicit Sunnah practice. The order is recommended but not obligatory; if changed unintentionally, the prayer is still valid.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۲۵) اور اگر بہت سے جمع ہو جائیں اور اس پر ایک نماز پڑھنی ہو تو سب کی ایک لمبی صف قبلہ کی جانب اس طرح کی جائے کہ ہر ایک کا سینہ امام سے آگے رہے۔ اور اس میں اس طرح ترتیب کی رعایت کی جاوے کہ امام کے متصل مردر کھے جائیں، پھر بچے ، پھر خنثی ، پھر عورتیں رکھیں جائیں۔ تشریح : اگر مثلا دس جنازے ہوں اور سب پر ایک ہی نماز پڑھنی ہو تو اس کی صورت یہ ہو کہ جو افضل ہے اس کو امام کے سامنے رکھے اس کے بعد اس سے کم افضل کو ، اس کے بعد اس سے کم افضل کو ۔ اور اگر مرد اور عورت اور بچے ہیں تو مرد کو امام کے سامنے رکھے ، پھر بچے کو رکھے ، پھر عورت کو رکھے، تا کہ امام سے عورت دور ہو۔
وجه : عن ابن عباس قال اتى بهم رسول الله الله يوم احد فجعل يصلى على عشرة عشرة و حمزة هو كما هو يرفعون و هو كما هو موضوع ۔ (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الصلاة على الشهداء ود منهم ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۱۵۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت حمزہ افضل تھے انکو حضور نے بار بار اپنے سامنے رکھا۔
Translation: (925) And if many (funerals) gather and one prayer is to be performed over them, then all are made into one long row facing the qiblah such that the chest of each is in front of the imam. And in it, order is observed: men are placed next to the imam, then boys, then khuntha, then women. Explanation: For example, if there are ten funerals and one prayer is to be performed over all, the method is that the most virtuous is placed in front of the imam, then the next virtuous, then the less virtuous. And if there are men, women, and children, men are placed in front of the imam, then children, then women, so that women are far from the imam. Proof: From Ibn Abbas: They were brought to the Messenger of Allah on the day of Uhud, and he began to pray over ten at a time, and Hamzah was as he was, they lifted and he was placed. (Ibn Majah) This hadith indicates that Hamzah was the most virtuous, so the Prophet placed him repeatedly in front of himself.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the arrangement of multiple bodies when they are prayed over in a single prayer. The matn (in Urdu) states that the bodies are arranged in a long row facing qiblah, with the chest of each in front of the imam (i.e., head towards qiblah). The order is: men nearest the imam, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodites), then women. The explanation clarifies that the most virtuous should be directly in front of the imam. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas about the martyrs of Uhud, where Hamzah was repeatedly placed in front. This shows that the Hanafi school prioritizes virtue in placement. The positioning of chests in front of the imam is a specific Hanafi practice to ensure the imam is aligned with the chests, as the prayer is valid with this arrangement.

Key Terms
خنثی (khuntha): A person of ambiguous gender; in this context, placed between boys and women.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for combined funeral prayers arranges bodies by virtue: men, then boys, then khuntha, then women, based on the Prophet's practice at Uhud.

Arrangement of Multiple Bodies in a Single Grave
Ruling statement on burial arrangement for multiple bodies in one grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi arrangement for burying men, women, and children in a single grave and distinguish it from the prayer arrangement.

Core Idea
In a single grave, the order is opposite to prayer: men towards qiblah, then boys, then women.

When multiple bodies must be buried in one grave, the order is not arbitrary. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific arrangement that reverses the order of prayer rows. This lesson clarifies that method and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the ruling concerns the burial of multiple bodies (men, women, children) in a single grave.
Not applicable for single graves.
2
Note the opposite principle
The burial arrangement is the reverse (عکس) of the prayer arrangement. In prayer, men are in front, then children, then women. In burial, the order is flipped relative to the qiblah.
The text explicitly uses the word 'عکس' to indicate reversal.
3
List the order
Place the man closest to the qiblah, then the child (boy), then the woman. This is the prescribed sequence.
If there are multiple individuals of each category, the order within each category is not detailed here.
4
Confirm the evidence
The text states that the proof has already been mentioned (referring to a previous hadith). This ruling is based on prophetic practice.
The hadith likely narrates the Prophet's (ﷺ) instruction for burial arrangement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۲۶) اور اگر ایک ہی قبر میں دفن کرنا ہوتو اس کا الٹار کھے۔ تشریح : : اگر مرد اور عورت اور بچوں کے جنازے ہوں اور ایک ہی قبر میں سب کو دفن کرنا ہو تو قبلے کی جانب پہلے مردکور کھے ، پھر بچوں کو رکھے، پھر عورت کو رکھے ۔ یہ مطلب ہے, وضعوا علی عکس هذا، کا۔ اور کی حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت گزر چکا ہے۔

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the arrangement for multiple bodies in a single grave. The author says the order is the opposite of the prayer arrangement (عکس). In prayer, men were closest to the imam; in burial, men are placed first towards the qiblah, then boys, then women. The text mentions that the proof for this has already been given (referring to a previous hadith, likely about the Prophet's practice). The opposite arrangement is to ensure that women are placed farthest from the qiblah side, perhaps due to modesty. The author emphasizes that this is the correct method, and the hadith evidence supports it.

Key Terms
عکس (aks): Opposite or reverse; here meaning the burial order is the reverse of the prayer order.
قبلة (qiblah): The direction of the Kaaba towards which Muslims pray. Bodies are placed facing qiblah.

Placing Multiple Janazahs in One Row for Prayer
Ruling on arrangement of multiple funerals for a single prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for arranging multiple janazahs in a single funeral prayer and identify the prescribed order of precedence.

Core Idea
When multiple funerals are prayed together, they form one row with the most virtuous nearest the imam.

When many janazahs are present for a single funeral prayer, they are not prayed individually but arranged in a single long row. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific order based on virtue and gender, ensuring that the most deserving are closest to the imam. This passage explains both the physical placement and the sequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining multiple janazahs in one prayer. The ruling is that they should be placed in a long row (ṣaffan ṭawīlan) facing the qibla, with their chests aligned in front of the imam.
This is a recommended (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) arrangement, not obligatory.
2
Determine the order of placement
The text specifies: men next to the imam, then boys after them, then khuntha (intersex individuals), then women. Within each category, the more virtuous person is placed closer.
The goal is to keep women farthest from the imam.
3
Understand the basis for order
The order is derived from the principle of preferring the more virtuous, as established in earlier hadith. This principle is applied to both gender and individual virtue.
If only one gender is present, arrange by virtue.
4
Apply to mixed groups
When men, boys, and women are present, the men are placed first, then boys, then women. The khuntha are placed between boys and women because their status is ambiguous.
This ensures that the imam's prayer is directed primarily at the most deserving.
5
Note the muftā bihī position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is as described: men nearest the imam, then boys, then khuntha, then women. This is the standard Hanafi practice.
Other schools may differ, but Hanafi maintains this order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if they are gathered and one prayer is performed upon them, make them a long row towards the qibla such that the chest of each is in front of the imam, and observe order: place men next to the imam, then boys after them, then khuntha, then women. Translation: And if many are gathered and one prayer is to be performed on them, make a long row for them all facing the qibla such that each one's chest is ahead of the imam. And in that maintain order: place men adjacent to the imam, then boys, then khuntha, then women. Explanation: For example, if there are ten janazahs and one prayer is to be performed, the method is: place the most virtuous in front of the imam, then the next virtuous, and so on. And if there are men, women, and boys, place the man in front of the imam, then the boy, then the woman, so that the woman is far from the imam.

Commentary
This passage details the arrangement when multiple funerals are prayed upon in one prayer. They are placed in a long row parallel to the qibla, with their chests toward the imam. The order is: men closest, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodites), then women—so that women are farthest. Within each category, the more virtuous is placed nearer the imam. This follows the principle of preferring the more virtuous, as established in the previous hadith.

Key Terms

الخناثى (al-khunāthā): Hermaphrodites (intersex individuals) whose gender is unclear.

Latecomer Joining Funeral Prayer Between Takbirs
Ruling with proof: joining procedure for latecomers in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer joining funeral prayer between takbirs and apply the analogy between takbirs and rak'ahs to determine the procedure.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, join the imam's current takbir, then make up missed ones after taslim — analogizing takbirs to rak'ahs.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) consists of four takbirs, which the Hanafi school treats as analogous to the four rak'ahs of a regular prayer. This analogy governs how a latecomer (masbuq) should join when arriving between takbirs. The source passage lays out the ruling, its reasoning, and supporting evidence from the tabi'in. By mastering this ruling, you will understand both the specific procedure and the broader Hanafi method of analogical reasoning in ibadat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two joining scenarios
The text distinguishes two cases: if the latecomer arrives before the imam has said the second takbir, he joins immediately; if he arrives between two takbirs (after the second but before the third), he must wait for the next takbir from the imam.
The key is whether the imam has begun a new 'unit' (takbir) or is still in the previous one.
2
Apply the masbuq analogy to takbirs
The four takbirs are treated like four rak'ahs. The latecomer is a masbuq who joins the current 'rak'ah' (i.e., the current takbir) rather than starting a new one. He must wait for the imam's next takbir to enter, then after taslim make up the missed takbirs.
This analogy is explicitly stated in the text: 'چهار تکبیریں گویا کہ چهار رکعتیں ہیں'.
3
Analyze the evidence from the tabi'in
Two athar are cited: (1) al-Harith reports that one should not say takbir until the imam says the next one; (2) Ibrahim commands to make up missed takbirs before the janazah is lifted. These are zanni in transmission but clear in dalalah.
The Hanafi school relies on these as supporting proofs for the ruling.
4
Contrast regular prayer joining rules
In regular prayer, a masbuq joins the current rak'ah and makes up the rest after taslim. Here, the same logic applies: join the current takbir, then make up the missed ones. The condition is that the janazah must still be present for makeup.
The difference is that in funeral prayer, there is no ruku', sujud, etc., only takbirs and supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۲۷) ولا يقتدى بالامام من وجده بين تكبيرتين بل ينتظر تكبير الامام فيدخل معه ويوافقه في دعائه ثم يقضى ما فاته قبل رفع الجنازة ترجمه: (۹۲۷) اور اس امام کی اقتداء نہ کرے جس کو دو تکبیر کے درمیان پائے بلکہ امام کی اگلی تکبیر کا انتظار کرے اور اس کے ساتھ داخل ہو اور اس کی دعاء میں اتباع کرے، پھر جو فوت ہو گیا اس کی قضا کرے جنازہ اٹھنے سے پہلے۔ تشریح : یہاں دو صورتیں ہیں [1] اگر امام نے تکبیر تحریمہ کہہ چکا ہو، اور اگلی تکبیر بھی نہیں کہی ہو اور کوئی آدمی آیا تو فورا تکبیر کہہ کر نماز میں شریک ہو جائے ، اس وقت اگلی تکبیر کا انتظار نہ کرے۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے بعد دو تکبیروں کے درمیان آدمی آیا تو ، مثلا درود شریف پڑھ رہے تھے کہ آدمی آیا تو ابھی تکبیر کہ کر شامل نہ ہو، بلکہ اگلی تکبیر یعنی دعا کی تکبیر کا انتظار کرے، اور جب امام دعا کی تکبیر کہے تب یہ آدمی تکبیر کہہ کر نماز میں شامل ہو۔ اور جب امام دعا پڑھے تو یہ بھی دعا پڑھے اور امام کے سلام پھیر نے کے بعد اپنی باقی تکبیر اور نماز پوری کرے، بشرطیکہ جنازہ وہاں موجود ہو۔ وجه : (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جنازے کی چار تکبیریں گویا کہ چار رکعتیں ہیں، اور دو تکبیریں چھوٹ گئیں تو گویا کہ دور کعتیں چھوٹ گئیں، اور یہ آدمی مسبوق ہو گیا، اور مسبوق کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ وہ پہلی رکعت شروع نہیں کرتا بلکہ امام جس رکعت میں ہوتا ہے اس رکعت میں شامل ہوتا ہے ، اس مثال میں امام دوسری تکبیر ، یعنی دوسری رکعت میں ہے اسلئے تیسری رکعت شروع کرنے کا انتظار کرے تاکہ زید تیسری رکعت میں شامل ہو سکے ، اور پہلی اور دوسری تکبیر امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ادا کرے، کیونکہ مسبوق امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد باقی رکعتیں ادا کرتا ہے، ایسے ہی زید امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد باقی تکبیر ادا کرے گا۔ تکبیر افتتاح بھی ایک رکعت کے درجے میں ہے اسلئے تکبیر افتتاح بھی پہلے نہیں کرے گا بعد میں ادا کرے گا۔ (۲) اثر میں ہے . عن الحارث أنه كان يقول اذا انتهى الرجل الى الجنازة و قد سبق ببعض التكبير لم يكبر حتى يكبر الامام . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۹۶، في الرجل منتهی الی الا مام وقد كبر أيدخل معه أو ينظر حتی پسند ابا تکمیر ، ج ثانی ص ۴۹۹ نمبر ۸ ۱۱۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ آنے والا آدمی تکبیر نہیں کہے گا جب تک کہ امام اگلی تکبیر نہ کہے۔ (۳) اور جنازہ اٹھانے سے پہلے قضا کرے اس کی دلیل یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال اذا فاتتك تكبيرة او تكبيرتان على الجنازة فبادر فكبر ما فاتك قبل ان ترفع ( مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب، في الرجل يفوته التكبير على الجنازة يقضيه ام لا وماذكر فيه، ج ثانی ص ۲۹۸، نمبر ۱۱۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے
And one should not follow the imam whom he finds between two takbirs, but rather wait for the imam's next takbir, enter with him, follow him in his supplication, then make up what he missed before the janazah is lifted. Translation: And do not follow the imam if you find him between two takbirs; instead wait for the imam's next takbir and enter with him and follow his supplication, then make up what was missed before the janazah is lifted. Explanation: There are two situations: (1) If the imam has said the opening takbir and has not yet said the next takbir, and a person comes, he should immediately say a takbir and join; he should not wait. (2) If a person comes between two takbirs after the opening takbir, e.g., while reciting durood, he should not say a takbir and join, but wait for the next takbir, which is the supplication takbir. When the imam says that takbir, this person says a takbir and joins. Then when the imam makes supplication, he also supplicates, and after the imam's taslim, he completes his remaining takbirs and prayer, provided the janazah is still present. Evidence: (1) They say the four takbirs are like four rak'ahs, and two missed takbirs are like two rak'ahs missed, making this person a masbuq. The masbuq does not start a new rak'ah but joins where the imam is. In this example, the imam is in the second takbir (second rak'ah), so he should wait to join in the third takbir. He will make up the first and second takbirs after the imam finishes. The opening takbir is also like a rak'ah, so he will not say it now but later. (2) Athar from al-Harith: 'When a man arrives at the funeral prayer and has missed some takbirs, he should not say takbir until the imam says a takbir.' (Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 2:499) (3) The athar from Ibrahim: 'If you miss one or two takbirs in funeral prayer, hasten to say what you missed before the janazah is lifted.' (Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 2:298)
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This detailed ruling explains the procedure for a latecomer (masbuq) in funeral prayer. The key principle is that the four takbirs are analogous to four rak'ahs. If someone joins after the imam has already said the opening takbir and is between two takbirs, he should not immediately begin with his own takbir but must wait for the imam's next takbir to join. Then after the imam's taslim, he completes the missed takbirs. The analogy with regular prayer (where the masbuq joins in the current rak'ah) is clearly drawn. Two athar from tabi'in support this: al-Harith reports that one should wait for the imam's next takbir, and Ibrahim says to make up missed takbirs before the janazah is lifted. The condition throughout is that the janazah is still present for the makeup.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbīr taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that starts the prayer.
مسبوق (masbūq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already started.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he arrives at the funeral prayer and finds the imam between the second and third takbirs?
A) Immediately say a takbir and join.
B) Wait for the imam's next takbir, say it with him, then make up missed takbirs after taslim.
C) Leave and wait for another funeral.
D) Make up the missed takbirs first, then join.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer's takbirs are treated like rak'ahs, so a latecomer must join the current takbir and make up missed ones after taslim.

Joining Imām at Takbīr Taḥrīmah in Janazah Prayer
Ruling on joining imam if present at takbir tahrimah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joining the imam at the takbir tahrimah of janazah prayer and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Arrive at the first takbir? Join immediately — do not wait.

In janazah prayer, timing is crucial. If you arrive exactly as the imam says the opening takbir, should you wait for the next takbir or join right away? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling, supported by the practice of a Tabi'i, and explains the difference between preferred and permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is joining the janazah prayer when arriving at the time of the takbir tahrimah. The ruling: it is mustahabb (preferred) to join immediately by saying your own takbir without waiting.
Mustahabb is between mubah and sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement of al-Hasan al-Basri (a Tabi'i) in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'A man who arrives at the janazah while they are praying enters with one takbir.'
This is an athar (narration from a Tabi'i), used as supporting evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The evidence shows that joining with a single takbir is sufficient and acceptable; waiting for the next takbir is not required.
The takbir tahrimah is the essential opening, so joining at that moment is analogous to starting with the imam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The differences among scholars are about preference (istihbab), not validity. If someone joins later, the prayer is still valid.
The Hanafi school takes the position that immediate joining is recommended; delaying is makruh tanzihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is mustahabb to join immediately; the authority comes from the practice of the Salaf as transmitted in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
This ruling is specific to janazah prayer but similar principles apply to other prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۲۸) ولا يـنـتـظـر تكبيـر الامـام مـن حـضر تحريمه
ترجمه : (۹۲۸) اور جو تحریے کے وقت حاضر ہواوہ امام کی اگلی تکبیر کا انتظار نہ کرے۔
تشریح : یہ اوپر کی پہلی صورت ہے کہ امام تحریمہ کی تکبیر کہ چکا ہے اس وقت ایک آدمی حاضر ہوا تو یہ اگلی تکبیر کا انتظار نہیں کرے گا بلکہ تکبیر کہہ کر تحریمہ میں شریک ہو جائے گا ، کیونکہ ابھی نماز شروع ہی ہوئی ہے، گویا کہ ابھی پہلی رکعت میں ہے اس لئے تکبیر کہہ کر شامل ہو سکتا ہے۔
وجه : عن الحسن في الرجل ينتهى الى الجنازة و هم يصلون عليها قال : يدخل معهم بتكبيرة _(مصنف ابن ابی شیبیۃ ، باب ۹۶ ، فی الرجل ین تھی الی الامام وقد كبر أيدخل معه أو ينتظر حتى يتد بالتکبیر ، ج ثانی ،ص ۴۹۹ نمبر ۱۱۴۸۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ایک تکبیر افتتاح کہے اور امام کے ساتھ داخل ہو جائے ۔
نوٹ :۔ یہ سب اختلاف استحباب کا ہے اس لئے درمیان میں بھی داخل ہو جائے گا تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔
(928) And one who is present at the time of takbir tahrimah does not wait for the next takbir of the imam. Translation: (928) And he who is present at the time of takbir tahrimah does not wait for the imam's next takbir. Explanation: This is the first scenario mentioned above: if the imam has said the takbir tahrimah and a person arrives, he should not wait for the next takbir. Rather, he should say takbir and join in the takbir tahrimah, because the prayer has just begun; it is as if he is in the first rak'ah, so he can join by saying takbir. Evidence: From al-Hasan regarding a man who arrives at the janazah while they are praying: he said, 'He enters with them with one takbir.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab 96, Hadith 11489) This statement of a Tabi'i indicates that he says one takbir iftitah and enters with the imam. Note: All these differences are about preference, so if someone enters in the middle, the prayer will still be valid.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from a Tabi'i (al-Hasan al-Basri). The author states that if a person arrives at the time of the first takbir (takbir tahrimah) of the janazah prayer, he should not wait for the next takbir but should immediately say his own takbir and join the prayer. The reasoning is that the prayer has just begun, and the imam is effectively in the 'first rak'ah' analogously. The proof is the statement of al-Hasan al-Basri that such a person enters with one takbir. The note at the end clarifies that these rulings are matters of preference (istihbab), so if one joins in between, the prayer is still valid; the differences are about what is better.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (taḥrīmah): The first takbīr of the prayer that initiates the state of prayer.
استحباب (istiḥbāb): Recommendation; an act is considered better but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if he arrives at the janazah prayer just as the imam is saying the first takbir (takbir tahrimah)?
A) Wait for the second takbir before joining.
B) Say takbir immediately and join.
C) Say takbir but wait for the imam's next takbir to start.
D) Recite something before joining.

Key Takeaway
Arriving at the takbir tahrimah of janazah prayer, you should join immediately without waiting.

Missing the Janazah Prayer After the Fourth Takbīr
Ruling on joining janāzah prayer after the fourth takbīr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a latecomer who arrives after the fourth takbīr in janāzah prayer and explain why the prayer is considered missed.

Core Idea
After the fourth takbīr in janāzah, no act remains – the prayer is missed.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the janāzah prayer. The text clarifies that if a person arrives after the imām has performed the fourth takbīr but before the salām, the prayer is considered missed entirely. The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning: after the fourth takbīr, nothing is recited, and the imām immediately proceeds to salām. Thus, there is no part of the prayer left to join.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is attending the janāzah prayer. The ruling is that if one arrives after the fourth takbīr, the prayer is missed.
2
Understand the structure of the janāzah prayer
The janāzah prayer consists of four takbīrs and a concluding salām. No recitation occurs after the fourth takbīr.
3
Determine why joining is impossible
After the fourth takbīr, there is no remaining act (rukn) to perform. The only remaining action is the salām, which is not preceded by any takbīr or recitation that a latecomer could share.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a person arrives after the imām has said the fourth takbīr, he cannot join the congregation. He has missed the prayer entirely.
5
State the muftā bihī position
The text specifies that this is the correct (al-ṣaḥīḥ) narration, which is the relied-upon position for fatwā.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۲۹) ومن حضر بعد التكبيرة الرابعة قبل السلام فاتته الصلوة في الصحيح.
ترجمه : (۹۲۹) اور جو چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد سلام سے پہلے حاضر ہو جائے صحیح روایت میں اس کی نماز فوت ہوگئی۔
تشریح : چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد کوئی چیز پڑھنی نہیں ہے، بلکہ فور اسلام ہے اس لئے جو آدمی چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد آیا اسکی رکعت فوت ہوگئی ، اس لئے اب وہ شامل نہیں ہوسکتا، اس کی نماز جنازہ فوت ہوگئی۔
(929) And whoever arrives after the fourth takbir before the salam, his prayer is missed according to the correct narration. Translation: (929) And he who arrives after the fourth takbir before the salam, his prayer is missed in the correct narration. Explanation: After the fourth takbir, nothing is to be recited; rather, immediately the salam is given. Therefore, the person who comes after the fourth takbir has missed his rak'ah (i.e., the entire prayer). Hence, he cannot join; his janazah prayer is missed.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling. The author states that according to the correct (sahih) narration, if a person arrives after the fourth takbir but before the imam says the salam, then the prayer is missed for him. The Urdu commentary explains that after the fourth takbir, there is no further recitation; the imam immediately gives salam. Therefore, the latecomer cannot join because there is nothing left to join. The prayer is considered missed entirely.

Key Terms
الصحيح (al-ṣaḥīḥ): The correct or sound narration/opinion within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He can join by saying takbīr and then salām immediately.
B) He can join but must repeat the entire prayer later.
C) The prayer is missed; he cannot join.
D) He should wait for the next janāzah.

Key Takeaway
The janāzah prayer has no remaining act after the fourth takbīr; therefore, a latecomer cannot join and his prayer is missed.
