Dislike of Janazah Prayer in the Mosque
Ruling with proof on janazah prayer in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying janazah in the mosque and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Praying janazah in the mosque is disliked but valid.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling regarding the janazah prayer: whether it should be performed inside the mosque. The Hanafi school holds that while the prayer is valid if performed inside, it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) due to the risk of defilement and a hadith that warns against it. We will trace the proof and understand the three scenarios outlined by the scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is praying the janazah prayer in a congregational mosque. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) but valid if performed.
The text states 'Wa tukrah al-salat 'alayhi fi masjid al-jama'ah'.
2
Recognise the three scenarios
The commentary explains three forms: (a) body and people inside mosque – disliked; (b) body outside, people inside – disliked; (c) body and imam outside, most followers inside – permissible.
The third scenario is an exception where the dislike does not apply.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah (Ibn Majah 1517, Bayhaqi 7040) where the Prophet said: 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is nothing for him.'
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'there is nothing for him' indicates no reward, implying the act is not recommended and thus makruh. The absolute statement shows it is not prohibited but discouraged.
The absence of reward does not mean invalidity; the prayer is still valid.
5
Note the exception and validity
Despite the dislike, if one prays, the prayer is valid. The text explicitly says 'bahar haal parh liya to ho jayegi' (if one prays, it will be valid).
This distinguishes makruh tanzihi from haram or makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۳۰) وتكرة الصلوة عليه في مسجد الجماعة وهو فيه او خارجا في المختار.
ترجمه : (۹۳۰) اور مسجد جماعت میں نماز جنازہ مکروہ ہے، خواہ جنازہ مسجد میں ہو خواہ خارج ہو، اور خواہ بعض لوگ مسجد میں ہوں، مختار روایت میں ۔
تشریح : مسجد میں جنازہ پڑھنے کی [1] ایک شکل یہ ہے کہ جنازہ بھی مسجد میں ہو اور امام اور مقتدی بھی مسجد میں ہوں ۔[۲] دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ میت تو مسجد سے باہر ہو اور امام اور مقتدی مسجد میں ہ ہوں تب بھی نماز جائز نہیں ہے۔ [۳] تیسری شکل یہ ہے کہ میت، اور امام اور کچھ مقتدی مسجد سے باہر ہوں، اور اکثر مقتدی مسجد میں ہوں یہ صورت جائز ہونی چاہئے۔
وجه : (۱) میت مسجد میں رکھی جائے تو ممکن ہے کہ مسجد کے تلویث ہونے کا خطرہ ہو۔ اس لئے مسجد میں نماز جنازہ پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ پڑھ لیا تو ہو جائے گی (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله من صلى علي جنازة في المسجد فليس له شيء . (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الصلاة على الجنائز في المسجد ، ص ۲۱۶، نمبر ۱۵۱۷ارسن سبیھقی ، باب الصلوة على الجنازة في المسجد ج رابع ص ۸۶ نمبر ۷۰۴۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسجد میں نماز پڑھنے سے ثواب نہیں ملے گا (۳)
(930) And it is disliked to pray over him in the congregation mosque, whether he (the deceased) is inside or outside, in the chosen opinion. Translation: (930) And it is disliked to pray janazah in the congregation mosque, whether the janazah is inside the mosque or outside, and even if some people are in the mosque, according to the chosen narration. Explanation: There are three forms of praying janazah in the mosque: [1] The janazah is inside the mosque and the imam and followers are also inside. [2] The deceased is outside the mosque and the imam and followers are inside—this is also not permissible (i.e., disliked). [3] The deceased, the imam, and some followers are outside the mosque, while the majority of followers are inside—this case should be permissible. Reason: (1) If the deceased is placed in the mosque, there is a risk of defiling the mosque. Therefore, it is makruh to pray janazah in the mosque. However, if one prays, it will be valid. (2) There is a hadith: From Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is nothing for him.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, Hadith 1517; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Hadith 7040) This hadith indicates that one will not get reward for praying in the mosque.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from hadith. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray the janazah prayer in the congregational mosque, regardless of whether the body is inside or outside the mosque, according to the chosen (mukhtar) narration. The Urdu commentary elaborates three scenarios: (1) both body and people inside—disliked; (2) body outside but people inside—also disliked; (3) body and imam outside with most followers inside—this is considered permissible (i.e., not disliked). The reasoning is to avoid any risk of defiling the mosque. The hadith from Abu Hurairah indicates that whoever prays janazah in the mosque will not receive reward (but the prayer is valid). The author notes that if one does pray in the mosque, the prayer is still valid.

Key Terms
مكروه (makrūh): An act that is disliked; it is better to avoid it, but if performed, it is valid and not sinful.
مختار (mukhtār): The chosen or preferred narration/opinion within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying janazah in the mosque?
A) It is haram and invalid.
B) It is makruh but valid if done.
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is permissible without any dislike.

Key Takeaway
The janazah prayer in the mosque is disliked (makruh tanzihi) but valid if performed, based on the hadith warning against it.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Funeral Prayer in the Mosque: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on janazah in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on janazah prayer in a mosque, explain the key proofs from both sides, and apply the ruling to different types of prayer spaces.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds janazah prayer in a masjid jama'ah as makruh, yet permits it in non-congregational spaces.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the permissibility of performing the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) inside a mosque. You will learn the specific conditions that lead to the Hanafi ruling of karahah (dislike) and contrast it with the Shafi'i view of permissibility. The focus is on understanding the proofs from Hadith and the statements of the Companions and Successors, and how the Hanafi school reconciles conflicting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
State the precise fiqh question: Is it permissible to perform janazah prayer inside a masjid jama'ah (a mosque where the five daily prayers are held with congregation)?
2
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
The Hanafi ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to pray janazah in a masjid jama'ah. However, if the location is not a masjid jama'ah (e.g., a home musalla, 'Eidgah, or madrasah) or there is a necessity like rain, the karahah is removed.
The key distinction is whether the place is designated for the five daily congregational prayers.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
The Hanafis cite the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) praying janazah for Najashi in the musalla (outside the mosque) and the statement of Kathir ibn Abbas that he never prayed janazah in the mosque.
These indicate practice and endorsement of praying outside.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position and its proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it permissible based on the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed over Suhayl ibn Bayda inside the mosque and the report that Abu Bakr's janazah was prayed in the mosque.
These are direct actions of the Prophet and a prominent Companion.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafis respond that the hadith of Aisha shows people criticized bringing janazah into the mosque, indicating general disapproval. The reported incidents were exceptions. Hence the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view.
The tarjih is based on reconciling all evidence, prioritizing the practice of the majority of the Companions.

Source Text

وجه : ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے (۱) عن عائشة انها لما توفى سعد بن ابي وقاص ... فبلغهن ان الناس عابوا ذلك و قالوا ما كانت الجنائز يدخل بها المسجد فبلغ ذالك عائشة فقالت ما اسرع الناس الى ان يعيبوا مالا علم لهم به ، عابوا علينا ان يمر بجنازة في المسجد وما صلى رسول الله على سهيل بن بيضاء الا في جوف المسجد. باضابطہ مسجد نہیں ہے، بلکہ صرف گھر میں نماز کے لئے مصلی ہے اس میں نماز جنازہ جائز ہے۔ عید گاہ اور مدرسے میں نماز جنازہ جائز ہوگی، کیونکہ وہاں پنج وقتہ جماعت نہیں ہوتی۔
Section: Outside and some people in the mosque according to the chosen opinion. In Madinah Tayyibah there was a separate place for janazah prayer. The hadith for this is: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) prayed over Najashi on the day he died, and went out with them to the musalla, lined them up, and said four takbirs. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that they went to the 'Eidgah outside the mosque to pray janazah, indicating that praying janazah in the mosque is not good. (4) The saying of a Tabi'i: From Kathir ibn Abbas, he said: I know that I never prayed janazah in the mosque. (Ibn Abi Shaybah, Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that I know I never prayed janazah in the mosque, indicating it is not good. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, praying janazah in the mosque is permissible. In Tirmidhi it is stated: Al-Shafi'i said: Janazah prayer for the deceased is performed in the mosque, and he used this hadith as evidence. (Tirmidhi) This phrase says that according to Imam Shafi'i, praying janazah in the mosque is permissible. His evidence is this hadith: (1) From Aisha that when Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas died... it reached them that people criticized that and said: Janazahs were not brought into the mosque. That reached Aisha, and she said: How quickly people criticize what they have no knowledge of! They criticized us that a janazah passes through the mosque, and the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) prayed over Suhayl ibn Bayda except inside the mosque. (Muslim, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is known that janazah prayer can be performed in the mosque. (2) From Hisham ibn 'Urwah, he said: My father saw people leaving the mosque to pray over a janazah, so he said: What are these people doing? Janazah was prayed over Abu Bakr only in the mosque. (Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shaybah) This athar shows that the janazah prayer of Abu Bakr was performed in the mosque. Note: But from the tone of the hadith it is clear that the general Sahaba expressed dislike (karahah) for bringing the deceased into the mosque. And that is the school of the Hanafis. Especially if the deceased is outside the mosque, there should be no karahah, or if there is a constraint like rain, then the karahah is reduced. Lexicon: Masjid al-jama'ah: A mosque in which the five daily prayers are held with congregation, and it is a formal mosque. Another is the home mosque, which is not a formal mosque but just a place for prayer in the home; in it, janazah prayer is permissible. In the 'Eidgah and madrasah, janazah prayer will be permissible because the five daily prayers are not held there.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling of performing salat al-janazah (funeral prayer) inside a mosque. The author presents the Hanafi position first: it is makruh (disliked) to pray janazah in a mosque where the five daily congregational prayers are held (masjid jama'ah). The evidence includes the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) praying over al-Najashi in the musalla (prayer ground) outside the mosque, and the statement of Kathir ibn Abbas that he never prayed janazah in the mosque. The author then presents the Shafi'i position: it is permissible based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed over Suhayl ibn Bayda inside the mosque, and the report that Abu Bakr's janazah was prayed in the mosque. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Aisha actually shows general disapproval (people criticized bringing janazah into the mosque), and the reported incidents were exceptions or due to specific circumstances. The author concludes with the relied-upon Hanafi view: karahah remains, but if the mosque is not a masjid jama'ah (e.g., a home musalla, 'Eidgah, or madrasah) or there is a constraint like rain, the karahah is reduced, making it permissible without dislike. This reflects the Hanafi principle that janazah prayer should ideally be outside the congregational mosque.

Key Terms
مسجد الجماعة (masjid al-jama'ah): A mosque where the five daily prayers are performed with congregation.
کراہیت (karahah): Dislike, legal disapprobation not amounting to prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) In the Ka'bah only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school deems janazah prayer in a masjid jama'ah as makruh, but permits it without karahah in non-congregational prayer spaces or when necessity dictates.

Funeral Rulings for Infant with Signs of Life vs Stillborn
Ruling on janazah for infant with or without signs of life

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for janazah salat on an infant based on signs of life, and identify the key hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Salat al-janazah is only obligatory for an infant who showed signs of life at birth; a stillborn is given ghusl and burial but no prayer.

This lesson examines the specific fiqh ruling regarding the funeral prayer for infants. The Hanafi school distinguishes between an infant who cries or shows any sign of life—treated as a living person—and a stillborn, who is washed and buried out of respect but not prayed over. The primary evidence is a hadith from Jabir (ra) narrated by Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of infants
The matn separates infants who show signs of life (istahalla) from those who do not. Note the different rulings for each.
Signs of life include crying, breathing, or movement.
2
State the ruling for each category
For an infant with signs: name, ghusl, janazah prayer. For stillborn: ghusl, wrapping, burial, but no prayer.
Ghusl and burial are always done out of respect.
3
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'The infant is not prayed over, does not inherit, nor is inherited from until he cries (shows sign of life).'
This is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا يصلى عليه حتى يستهل' conditions the obligation of salat on istihlal. The particle 'hatta' indicates a necessary condition.
This shows why no prayer is said for stillborn.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a baby born with a heartbeat that stops after a few seconds, determine if janazah prayer is performed.
Any sign of life qualifies, so prayer is performed.

(۹۳۱) ومن استهلّ سُمِّيَ وغسل وصلّى عليه وان لم يستهل غسل في المختار أدرج في خرقة و دفن ولم يصل عليه
ترجمه : (۹۳۱) اور جس بچے نے آواز نکالی تو نام رکھا جائے گا اور غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی ، ۔ اور اگر نہ روئے تو مختار مذہب میں غسل دیا جائے اور ایک کپڑے میں لپیٹ دیا جائے اور دفن کر دیا جائے اور اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔ تشریح بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد کوئی ایسی علامت ظاہر ہو کہ وہ زندہ پیدا ہوا تھا، مثلا روئے، یا حرکت کرے، یا سانس چل رہی ہو، تو وہ زندہ آدمی ہے اس لئے اس کا نام بھی رکھا جائے گا تا کہ قیامت کے دن اس نام سے پکارا جائے ، اور اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز بھی پڑھی جائے گی اور اگر زندگی کی کوئی علامت نہیں ہے تو یہ مردہ پیدا ہوا ہے اور گوشت کا لتھڑا ہے اس لئے احترام کے طور پر غسل دیا جائے گا اور تھوڑ اسا کفن بھی دیا جائے گا اور دفن بھی کیا جائے گا، البتہ چونکہ زندہ نہیں تھا اس لئے نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے . عن جابر عن النبي ال الله قال : الطفل لا يصلى عليه و لا يرث و لا يورث حتى يستهل . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ترک الصلوة على الطفل حتی یستھل ،ص ۲۴۹، نمبر ۱۰۳۲ رابن ماجته ، باب ما جاء فی الصلاة على الطفل ، ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۱۵۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روئے تو نماز پڑھی جائے ورنہ تو نہیں۔ لغت : استهل : هلال سے مشتق ہے، نیا چاند نکلنا، یہاں مراد ہے بچے کا رونا، زندگی کی کوئی علامت ۔ ادرج : درج سے مشتق ہے، پیٹنا۔ خرقہ : کپڑے کا ٹکڑا ۔
(931) And whoever (infant) cries (shows sign of life), he is named, given ghusl, and prayed over. If he does not cry, according to the chosen opinion, he is given ghusl, wrapped in a cloth, buried, and not prayed over. Translation: (931) And the child who cried out, he will be named, given ghusl, and prayed over. And if he did not cry, in the chosen school, he is given ghusl, wrapped in a piece of cloth, buried, and no prayer is performed for him. Explanation: If after birth any sign appears that he was born alive, e.g., cried, or moved, or breathed, then he is a living person, so he will be named so that he is called by that name on the Day of Resurrection, given ghusl, and prayed over. If there is no sign of life, then he was born dead and is a piece of flesh; as a mark of respect, he is given ghusl, given a brief shroud, and buried. However, since he was not alive, no prayer is performed. Evidence: (1) Hadith: From Jabir from the Prophet (ﷺ) said: The infant is not prayed over, does not inherit, nor is inherited from until he cries (shows sign of life). (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) This hadith states that if he cries, prayer is performed; if not, then no. Lexicon: 'Istahal' is derived from 'hilal' (new moon), meaning to appear; here it means the child's cry, any sign of life. 'Udrija' from 'daraja', to wrap. 'Khirqah': a piece of cloth.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling (hukm) regarding the funeral prayer for an infant who shows signs of life versus a stillborn. The matn states the rule concisely: if the infant cries (or shows any sign of life), it is treated as a living person—named, given ghusl, and prayed over. If no sign of life, ghusl is given, wrapped in a cloth, buried, but no prayer. The commentary explains that any sign of life (crying, movement, breathing) suffices. The evidence is a hadith from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah that explicitly states: 'The infant is not prayed over, does not inherit, nor is inherited from until he cries (i.e., shows sign of life).' This hadith is the primary proof. Note that the infant is still washed and buried out of respect even if stillborn, but the salat al-janazah is withheld because it is a prayer for a living Muslim who has died; a stillborn never lived, so it is not obligated. The lexical notes clarify the meaning of 'istihlal' as any sign of life, not just crying, contrary to some misunderstandings.

Key Terms
استهل (istahalla): Sign of life at birth, such as crying, moving, or breathing.
أدرج (udrija): Wrapped (in a cloth) for burial.
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth used as a simple shroud for the stillborn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, what condition must be met for salat al-janazah to be performed on an infant?
A) The infant must have been born alive with any sign of life.
B) The infant must have been older than six months.
C) The infant must have been named by the parents.
D) The infant must have been circumcised.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-janazah on an infant depends on whether it showed signs of life at birth; a stillborn is washed and buried but no prayer is performed.

The Captive Child's Janazah: Following the Disbelieving Parent
Ruling on janazah for a child captive with one parent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on janazah prayer for a child captive accompanied by a disbelieving parent and explain the dalil (athar of Hammad) that supports it.

Core Idea
A child captive follows the parent's religion; with a disbelieving parent, no janazah is offered.

This lesson addresses the legal status of a child taken captive in war when one disbelieving parent is present. The Hanafi school applies the principle of taba'iyyah (dependency) to determine the child's religion, and by extension, the permissibility of janazah prayer. We will examine the textual evidence from the athar of Hammad in the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling level
What is the act being ruled upon? It is salah al-janazah (funeral prayer) for a specific child. The ruling is that it is haram (prohibited) to perform it.
The prohibition is because the child is considered a disbeliever by following the parent.
2
State the underlying principle
The child's religion follows the parent with whom he is captured (taba'iyyah). If that parent is a disbeliever, the child is deemed a disbeliever.
This principle is derived from the athar and general Hanafi usul.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is an athar from Hammad (a tabi'i) recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
The athar explicitly states: 'When a child is between his parents and both are polytheists, no prayer is performed over him.'
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا يصلى عليه' directly proves the prohibition. The condition 'بين أبويه و هما مشركان' shows that the child's status depends on the parents' religion.
The ruling is derived from the explicit wording; no qiyas needed.
5
Note the exception
If the child is captured alone (without a parent), he is considered Muslim and janazah is performed. This is confirmed by the same athar: 'If he is not between his parents, he is Muslim.'
The exception reinforces the rule by contrast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۳۲) كصبي سُبِى مع احد ابويه
ترجمه : (۹۳۲) جیسے کوئی بچہ اپنے ماں باپ میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ قید کیا جائے تو اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔ تشریح : قاعدہ یہ ہے [1] کہ بچہ ماں باپ کے تابع ہوتا ہے اور اسی پر اسکے دین کا فیصلہ ہوتا ہے۔ اب والدین میں سے ایک کے ساتھ قید ہوا ہے، اور وہ کافر ہے اس لئے اس کے تابع ہو کر بچہ کا فر شمار کیا جائے ، اور کافر پر نماز جنازہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس بچے پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ۔
وجه : (ا) عـن حـمـاد قال : اذا كان الصبى من السبى أو غيرهم بين أبويه ، و هما مشركان فانه لا يصلى عليه ، و ان لم يكن بين أبويه فانه مسلم اذا مات و هو صبى يصلى عليه ، قال : و قال حماد : اذا ملكت الصبي فهو مسلم . (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الصلاۃ علی الصحی ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۵۴، نمبر (۶۶۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ماں باپ کا فر ہوں اور قید ہو کر آئے ہوں تو بچے کو اسکے تابع کر کے نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ، اور اسی میں ہے کہ تنا بچہ قید ہو ہوتو اسلام دار ہونے
(932) Like a child who is captured with one of his parents. Translation: (932) Like a child who is taken captive with one of his parents, then no prayer is performed over him. Explanation: The rule is that a child follows his parents, and his religion is decided accordingly. Now he has been captured with one of his parents, and that parent is a disbeliever, so the child is considered a disbeliever by following him. Since no janazah prayer is performed over a disbeliever, no janazah prayer will be performed over this child. Evidence: (1) From Hammad, he said: When a child is from the captives or others between his parents, and both are polytheists, then no prayer is performed over him. If he is not between his parents, then he is a Muslim if he dies as a child, and prayer is performed over him. He said, and Hammad said: When you own the child (as a captive), he is a Muslim. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that if parents are disbelievers and come as captives, the child follows them and no prayer is performed. And in it, it is said: a lone child captive is considered Muslim.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the status of a child captured in war (sabi) when only one parent is present. The matn states: 'Like a child captured with one of his parents' – indicating that the child is treated according to the religion of that parent. The explanation elaborates the principle: a child is dependent on his parents for determining his religion. If captured with one parent who is a disbeliever, the child is considered a disbeliever, and thus the janazah prayer is not performed. The evidence is an athar (statement) from Hammad (a tabi'i) recorded in the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq, which explicitly states that if the child is between two polytheist parents, no prayer is performed; but if alone (without a parent), the child is considered Muslim. The text also notes that if a child captive is owned (i.e., taken as a slave), he is considered Muslim. This highlights the Hanafi principle that a child without a disbelieving parent is presumed Muslim, but when accompanied by a disbelieving parent, the child's ruling follows that parent because of dependency.

Key Terms
سبی (sabi): A child taken captive in war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing janazah prayer for a child taken captive while with one disbelieving parent?
A) Prayer is performed as the child is innocent
B) Prayer is not performed because the child follows the parent's disbelief
C) Prayer is optional
D) Prayer is performed only if the child is orphaned

Key Takeaway
A child's religion follows his parent in captivity; therefore, janazah is not performed over a child captured with a disbelieving parent.

Ruling on the Newborn: Cry or No Cry
States the ruling for a live-born vs stillborn child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for funeral rites of a live-born vs stillborn child and apply the criterion of istihlal.

Core Idea
A newborn's cry separates a complete funeral from a respectful burial without prayer.

The moment of birth brings immediate questions: if the child shows no sign of life, how should we treat the body? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi distinction based on the presence or absence of istihlal (crying or other life signs). The ruling is grounded in a prophetic hadith and balances communal obligation with respect for the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the matn and note the contrast: 'istahalla' (cried out) vs 'lam yastahill' (did not cry). These define the two categories.
The key term 'istahalla' encompasses any sign of life: crying, movement, breathing.
2
Determine the hukm for each
For the live-born: naming, ghusl, and funeral prayer (fard kifayah). For the stillborn: ghusl (wajib), wrapping, burial, but no prayer.
The stillborn is given ghusl out of respect (ikram), not as a full fard.
3
Analyze the proof
The hadith from Jabir explicitly states: no prayer and no inheritance until the child cries (istahalla). This is the primary dalil for the distinction.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but the ruling is accepted due to other supporting evidence and practice.
4
Understand the rationale
A live-born is a full human being with rights; a stillborn is treated with dignity but lacks the status of a living person for funeral prayer.
The Hanafi school emphasizes respect for the stillborn by requiring washing and shrouding.
5
Apply the criterion
Any sign of life (crying, movement, breathing) after delivery qualifies as istihlal. If there is doubt, the child is considered live-born.
This is a rule of caution: the default is to treat as alive if any sign appears.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
(۹۳۱) ومن استهلّ سُمِّيَ وغسل وصلّى عليه وان لم يستهل غسل في المختار أدرج في خرقة و دفن ولم يصل عليه

ترجمه : (۹۳۱) اور جس بچے نے آواز نکالی تو نام رکھا جائے گا اور غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی ، ۔ اور اگر نہ روئے تو مختار مذہب میں غسل دیا جائے اور ایک کپڑے میں لپیٹ دیا جائے اور دفن کر دیا جائے اور اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔

تشریح بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد کوئی ایسی علامت ظاہر ہو کہ وہ زندہ پیدا ہوا تھا، مثلا روئے، یا حرکت کرے، یا سانس چل رہی ہو، تو وہ زندہ آدمی ہے اس لئے اس کا نام بھی رکھا جائے گا تا کہ قیامت کے دن اس نام سے پکارا جائے ، اور اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز بھی پڑھی جائے گی اور اگر زندگی کی کوئی علامت نہیں ہے تو یہ مردہ پیدا ہوا ہے اور گوشت کا لتھڑا ہے اس لئے احترام کے طور پر غسل دیا جائے گا اور تھوڑ اسا کفن بھی دیا جائے گا اور دفن بھی کیا جائے گا، البتہ چونکہ زندہ نہیں تھا اس لئے نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے . عن جابر عن النبي ال الله قال : الطفل لا يصلى عليه و لا يرث و لا يورث حتى يستهل . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ترک الصلوة على الطفل حتی یستھل ،ص ۲۴۹، نمبر ۱۰۳۲ رابن ماجته ، باب ما جاء فی الصلاة على الطفل ، ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۱۵۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روئے تو نماز پڑھی جائے ورنہ تو نہیں۔

لغت : استهل : هلال سے مشتق ہے، نیا چاند نکلنا، یہاں مراد ہے بچے کا رونا، زندگی کی کوئی علامت ۔ ادرج : درج سے مشتق ہے، پیٹنا۔ خرقہ : کپڑے کا ٹکڑا ۔
(931) And whoever (the child) cries out, he is named, washed, and prayer is performed over him. And if he does not cry out, in the chosen view he is washed, wrapped in a cloth, and buried, and prayer is not performed over him. Translation: And the child who raised his voice, he will be named, given ghusl, and prayer will be prayed over him. And if he does not cry, in the chosen madhhab he is given ghusl, wrapped in a cloth, and buried, and prayer is not prayed over him. Explanation: After the child is born, if any sign appears that he was born alive, e.g., he cries, or moves, or breathes, then he is a living person, therefore he will be named so that he is called by that name on the Day of Resurrection, and he will be given ghusl and prayer will be prayed over him. And if there is no sign of life, then he is stillborn and is a piece of flesh; therefore out of respect he will be given ghusl, given a small shroud, and buried; however, since he was not alive, prayer will not be prayed over him. Evidence: (1) The hadith: from Jabir from the Prophet (ﷺ) said: The child is not prayed over, nor does he inherit, nor is he inherited from, until he cries out. (Tirmidhi, etc.) This hadith states that if he cries, prayer is prayed; otherwise not. Lexicon: istahalla: derived from hilal, new moon; here meaning the child's crying, a sign of life. udrija: derived from daraja, to wrap. khirqah: a piece of cloth.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Thamaratun Najah. The passage presents a clear legal distinction based on whether a newborn shows signs of life after birth. The core ruling: if the child cries (or shows any life sign), he is treated as a full living person—named, given ghusl, and the funeral prayer is performed. If no sign of life appears, the child is considered stillborn; he is given ghusl out of respect, wrapped in a cloth, and buried, but the funeral prayer is not performed. The chosen view (mukhtar) is to still wash the stillborn. The author provides the reasoning: a live-born is a complete human being deserving of all funeral rites; a stillborn is merely a piece of flesh but must be treated with dignity. The proof is a hadith from Jabir stating that until a child cries out, no prayer is performed, no inheritance passes. This hadith is from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah. The Hanafi school follows this ruling, and it is consistent with the general principle that funeral prayer is for believers who were alive. The passage also clarifies that any sign of life (crying, movement, breathing) suffices to consider the child alive.

Key Terms
استهل (istahalla): To cry out; used specifically for a newborn showing a sign of life (crying, movement, breathing).
ادرج (udrija): To wrap; from the root daraja. In the text, it refers to wrapping the stillborn in a cloth.
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth; the shroud for a stillborn child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is done for a stillborn child (no sign of life)?
A) No washing, no burial, no prayer.
B) Washed, shrouded, buried, but no funeral prayer.
C) Full funeral prayer is performed because the soul is present.
D) Only a name is given.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates washing and burial for stillborns but reserves funeral prayer for those who show a sign of life after birth.

Ruling on a Child Captured with a Kafir Parent
States that a child captured with one non-Muslim parent receives no janazah prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer for a child captured with a non-Muslim parent and identify the evidence from the athar of Hammad.

Core Idea
A child captured with a kafir parent is ruled kafir; no janazah prayer is performed.

This lesson addresses a specific case from the laws of jihad and janazah: a child taken captive alongside one non-Muslim parent. The Hanafi school applies the principle of taba'iyyah (following) to determine the child's religious status for funeral rites. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the school prioritizes parental custody over the general rule of fitrah in certain contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a child captured with one non-Muslim parent. The ruling: no janazah prayer is performed for that child if he dies.
The fatwa is clear: لا يصلى عليه (no prayer).
2
Identify the governing principle
The principle is taba'iyyah: the child's religion follows that of the parent he is with. Since the parent is a kafir, the child is deemed kafir.
This is a key Hanafi rule in family and custody matters.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is an athar from Hammad (a tabi'i) recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. The text explicitly differentiates: if the child is between polytheist parents, no prayer; if alone, he is Muslim and prayed over.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi, considered hujja in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Here the child is captured with one parent (kafir). By taba'iyyah, he is kafir. Janazah over a kafir is haram, so no prayer.
This is consistent with the general prohibition in Qur'an 9:84.
5
Note the dispute and tarjih
Some Shafi'is argue the child is Muslim by fitrah. The Hanafi response is that the athar and the principle of taba'iyyah override the general rule in this specific context.
Thamaratun Najah follows the Hanafi position as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۳۲) كصبي سُبِى مع احد ابويه

ترجمه : (۹۳۲) جیسے کوئی بچہ اپنے ماں باپ میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ قید کیا جائے تو اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔

تشریح : قاعدہ یہ ہے [1] کہ بچہ ماں باپ کے تابع ہوتا ہے اور اسی پر اسکے دین کا فیصلہ ہوتا ہے۔ اب والدین میں سے ایک کے ساتھ قید ہوا ہے، اور وہ کافر ہے اس لئے اس کے تابع ہو کر بچہ کا فر شمار کیا جائے ، اور کافر پر نماز جنازہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس بچے پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ۔

وجه : (ا) عـن حـمـاد قال : اذا كان الصبى من السبى أو غيرهم بين أبويه ، و هما مشركان فانه لا يصلى عليه ، و ان لم يكن بين أبويه فانه مسلم اذا مات و هو صبى يصلى عليه ، قال : و قال حماد : اذا ملكت الصبي فهو مسلم . (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الصلاۃ علی الصحی ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۵۴، نمبر (۶۶۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ماں باپ کا فر ہوں اور قید ہو کر آئے ہوں تو بچے کو اسکے تابع کر کے نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ، اور اسی میں ہے کہ تنا بچہ قید ہو ہوتو اسلام دار ہونے
کی وجہ سے مسلمان شمار کیا جائے گا۔
(932) Such as a child captured with one of his parents. Translation: Such as a child who is taken captive with one of his parents, then prayer is not performed over him. Explanation: The rule is that a child follows the parents, and his religion is determined by them. Now he is captured with one of the parents, and that parent is a kafir, so by following him the child is considered a kafir, and no janazah prayer is performed for a kafir, therefore janazah prayer is not performed for this child. Evidence: (1) From Hammad said: When a child is among captives or others, between his parents and they are polytheists, then no prayer is performed over him; and if he is not between his parents, then he is Muslim; when he dies as a child, prayer is performed over him. He said: And Hammad said: When you possess the child, he is Muslim. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...) This athar states that if the parents are kafir and come as captives, then the child follows them and no prayer is performed; and in the same it is said that a child captured alone is considered Muslim because of being in dar al-Islam.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn. It addresses the case of a child taken captive along with one of his parents, where that parent is a non-Muslim. The ruling: no janazah prayer is performed for that child if he dies. The reasoning is the principle of taba'iyyah (following): a child's religion is determined by the parent he accompanies. Since the parent is a kafir, the child is deemed kafir, and funeral prayer for a kafir is prohibited. The evidence is an athar from Hammad in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, which explicitly states that if the child is between two polytheist parents, no prayer is performed; otherwise (if not with a kafir parent), he is Muslim and prayed over. The passage also notes the case of a child captured alone: he is considered Muslim because dar al-Islam gives him the status of Islam. The Hanafi school adheres to this hierarchy: parent's religion determines child's religion in captivity, with an exception if the child converts or if the parent converts (covered in the next ruling). The commentary also cites the verse prohibiting prayer over kafirs (Surah Tawbah 9:84) as a secondary proof, though not quoted in full here.

Key Terms
تابع (tabi'): Following; in fiqh, a child is tabi' (subordinate) to the parent in religion and legal status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A child is captured along with his father, who is a polytheist. According to the Hanafi ruling, if the child dies, what is done?
A) The child is given full Muslim funeral rites because all children are born Muslim.
B) The child is washed and buried without janazah prayer.
C) No janazah prayer is performed; the child is considered a kafir.
D) Janazah prayer is performed, but without takbirs.

Key Takeaway
A child captured with a non-Muslim parent is legally a non-Muslim; no janazah prayer is offered.
